================================================================================
 SphereNet Changelog (English)
 All notable changes are documented in this file.
 Turkish: CHANGELOG-TR.txt  |  Archive (pre 2026-05-29, bilingual): CHANGELOG_OLD.txt
================================================================================

[2026-07-20] - Unified standing-surface resolver: the Z-drift root fix
----------------------------------------

FIX - One surface authority for character Z (the audit design). WalkCheck
        gained ResolveStandingSurface with two policies: IgnoreCollision
        (GM/AllMove/pass-walls steps - collision is bypassed, surface
        collection and Z selection are NOT) and Settle (login, mount,
        dismount, teleport-derive, stuck-menu, NPC step Z - nearest
        standable surface WITH headroom to a reference Z, so two-story
        houses seat the correct floor). It selects from the SAME geometry
        inventory the walk path uses: land average, statics with open-door
        handling, dynamic items, multi/ship components and custom-house
        tiles.

FIX - Every character seat path migrated off MapDataManager.GetEffectiveZ,
        which saw neither dynamics, multis, custom houses nor headroom, and
        whose closest-to-currentZ pick was SELF-REINFORCING for a drifted Z
        (the 5146,993 dungeon report: stored Z=10 held over a floor at 1,
        exposed as a snap by the dclick-facing self 0x20). Migrated: the
        GM/AllMove movement bypass, login seating, mount and dismount (both
        handlers), the world-features dismount, auto-derived teleport
        destinations, the stuck-menu teleport, and all NPC step-Z sites.
        GetEffectiveZ remains for non-character queries (spawn gems, ground
        items, previews) and - deliberately, for cost - the A* route
        heuristic, whose executed steps re-resolve through WalkCheck anyway.
        The dclick 0x20 stays; FaceUsePoint stays untouched (per the audit
        do-nots).

NEW - Z-drift regression tests run against the REAL mul data (path
        auto-detected, clean skip when absent): at the drift tile a normal
        player step, the GM bypass from both the floor and the drifted
        reference, and Settle from both references all agree on one floor;
        sloped-land Settle reproduces every walk step Z; the Britain bridge
        seats on the deck. All three passed against live map data.

[2026-07-20] - NPC AI wave 2: food counters, FOODTYPE diet, gold refusal, scan guards
----------------------------------------

FIX - NPC hunger uses one truth: a fresh spawn seeds the AI hunger counter
        (NpcFood) fed - it used to start at zero while MAXFOOD only filled
        the separate Food stat, so every newborn NPC read as starving
        (want 100 on all edibles, constant ground-food hunts).

NEW - FOODTYPE is a real diet (Source-X Food_CanEat): pack feeding, ground
        foraging, the hunger want score and pet feeding all check the
        chardef FOODTYPE list - a carnivore no longer eats fruit. Undeclared
        diets keep the generic edible classes.

FIX - Gold handed to any NON-banker NPC is refused outright (Source-X
        NPC_OnItemGive) - a vendor wants coins on the ground but never
        pockets a handed pile. An OWNED vendor pet now routes goods into
        its vendor-stock box (LAYER_VENDOR_STOCK equivalent).

FIX - Item/corpse scan guards: the desire scan now needs line of sight and
        CAN_C_USEHANDS on EVERY brain (the humanoid exemption is gone), uses
        a sight-driven look range, and corpse pickup/looting is blocked in
        both guarded AND safe regions (TryLoot got the same guards).

FIX - DESIRES keeps the raw want qty (DESIRES=999 t_corpse stays 999 for
        @NPCLookAtItem ARGN2 - the 0-100 clamp is gone) and r_* region
        aliases are typed as region preferences instead of being hashed as
        fake itemdefs (~167 Scripts-X lines affected).

FIX - Healer alignment is three-way: good healers (positive karma) serve
        only the innocent, evil healers only criminals/murderers, and a
        NEUTRAL healer serves everyone - zero-karma healers no longer
        behave as good ones.

FIX - The self-defense tests now assert a RESOLVED swing via the OnNpcAttack
        hook instead of an adjacent-start distance check that passed even
        when the NPC did nothing (audit round 8 test critique).

[2026-07-20] - NPC AI parity wave: brain alias, give-item semantics, DESIRES, self-defense
----------------------------------------

FIX - brain_animal_trainer resolves to the Stable brain: the Scripts-X
        stablemaster alias (defs.scp value 7) failed the enum-name parse and
        left stablemasters on the pre-spawn Monster fallback brain.

FIX - The 0x77 mobile-move packet and single worn-item updates route through
        the viewer adjustment (Source-X PacketCharacterMove calls
        GetAdjustedCharID per client): a tripping player no longer sees
        mobiles snap back to their real body/hue the moment they move, and a
        fresh equip recolors too.

FIX - Giving an item to an NPC follows Source-X NPC_OnItemGive: @ReceiveItem
        fires FIRST (before train/hire gold pay); an owned pet eats offered
        food and refuses what it cannot carry; a banker deposits gold into
        the giver's bank box; dropping goods on a vendor is a quick-sell
        offer; everyone else runs the NPC_WantThisItem gate - an unwanted
        gift is REFUSED by default, @NPCRefuseItem RETURN 1 overrides the
        refusal, @NPCAcceptItem RETURN 1 cancels the accept. The previous
        contract (default-accept, inverted trigger meanings) is gone and the
        tests now lock the reference semantics.

FIX - DESIRES entries keep their want quantity (Source-X NPC_WantThisItem
        returns the entry's GetResQty, bare defname = 1) instead of a flat
        100 - desiring NPCs are no longer maximally greedy; a hungry NPC
        wants edibles at 100-foodPercent and vendor brains want gold. The
        native item scan runs without the script-trigger gate and now also
        covers idle monsters, animals and vendor brains; pickup requires
        usable hands and corpse looting never happens in guarded territory.

FIX - Non-monster brains defend themselves: Human, Vendor, Banker, Stable
        and Healer NPCs fight (or flee, on fear motivation) the attacker
        assigned as their FightTarget, and animals fight back instead of
        only shying away from war-mode characters.

FIX - Healer alignment: an evil healer (negative karma) serves criminals
        and murderers; a good healer keeps serving only the innocent.

[2026-07-20] - FINDID memory precedence, full hallucination trip visuals
----------------------------------------

FIX - FINDID ranks the hidden spell-memory layer BEFORE the backpack: a
        form memory shares its graphic with the rune scroll, so the old
        pack-first order let the Reaper/Stone toggle delete a spare scroll
        from the pack while the form stayed on.

NEW - Full hallucination visuals (Source-X GetAdjustedCharID /
        GetAdjustedItemID): a hallucinating player sees every OTHER mobile
        as a random classic creature, every mobile plus its worn equipment
        in random dye hues, and ground items recolored too (multis exempt).
        The view refreshes the moment the effect lands, on every 15-30 s
        trip tick, and when the effect ENDS - so the last random colors
        never linger on the client.

[2026-07-20] - Spell-memory reverse link, timerless forms, hallucination visuals
----------------------------------------

FIX - FINDID now searches the hidden spell-memory layer alongside equipment
        and the backpack, and supports chained verb dispatch
        (FINDID.<id>.REMOVE). Removing an IT_SPELL memory item reverts its
        active effect through the new SpellEngine.RemoveEffectByMemory
        reverse link (Source-X: deleting the memory runs
        Spell_Effect_Remove). The Scripts-X Reaper/Stone Form @Select
        toggles (FINDID.<RUNE_ITEM>.REMOVE) now genuinely end the form.

FIX - A zero-duration form (the pack ships Reaper Form with DURATION=0.0)
        now holds with NO expiry - until dispel, death or the script toggle
        - matching the reference's timerless poly memory; the previous
        4-hour approximation is gone.

NEW - Hallucination is visible: a hallucinating player sees every mobile in
        a random dye hue (re-rolled on each view refresh, Source-X
        CClientMsg addChar), the trip tick refreshes the nearby view and
        plays its sound ONLY for the affected client (no more broadcast to
        bystanders). A petrified (Stone) mobile now shows HUE_STONE 0x482
        to everyone.

FIX - The drunk hiccup is visible: an overhead *hic* emote nearby players
        can see, plus a random facing turn and the bow animation when not
        mounted (Source-X Spell_Equip_OnTick), replacing the private system
        message.

[2026-07-20] - Poly forms, corpse-spell reach checks, periodic drunk/hallucination ticks
----------------------------------------

FIX - Animate Dead and Bone Armor validate the targeted corpse like Source-X:
        it must be a TOP-LEVEL world item on the caster's map within casting
        range. A known UID could previously consume a corpse from inside a
        container or across the world, dumping its contents at the corpse.

NEW - Reaper Form and Stone Form apply their form on first cast: body swap
        (Reaper 0xE6 CREID_REAPER_FORM, Stone 0x2C1 CREID_STONE_FORM) on the
        polymorph layer with a timed revert. A pack duration of 0 (Reaper)
        holds the form near-permanently like the reference's timerless poly
        memory. Re-casting another poly-family spell swaps forms cleanly -
        the base body is captured only after the previous form is reverted.

NEW - Chameleon, Beast Form and Monster Form ride the shared polymorph route
        (Source-X LAYER_SPELL_Polymorph, CCharSpell.cpp:4087): menu picks via
        the POLY cast-menu flow now work for all poly-family spells; without
        a pick, Beast/Monster Form roll a classic animal/monster body and
        Chameleon keeps the body (the reference ships its skin-match visual
        commented out). Only Enchant and Forget remain gated as inert.

FIX - Shrink kills a conjured/summoned creature outright (Source-X
        NPC_Shrink zeroes its STR) instead of rejecting it alive.

FIX - Bone Armor pieces run their ITEMDEF @Create metadata
        (ItemDefHelper.ApplyInstanceMetadata) - type, armor, durability and
        events - instead of spawning as graphic-only shells.

NEW - Periodic effect ticks (Source-X Spell_Equip_OnTick): Hallucination
        plays trip sounds (0x243/0x244) every 15-30 s for its duration;
        Ale/Wine/Liquor drain one current stamina and mana point per 5 s
        drunk tick with random hiccups and a 10% early-sober chance,
        replacing the earlier one-shot stat penalty. A charge-driven effect
        that retires early now reverts its applied stat flag.

[2026-07-20] - HARM-flag crime/reflect, @Select stage, custom Sphere spells 1000+
----------------------------------------

FIX - Harmful-spell classification now follows SPELLFLAG_HARM (Source-X
        OnSpellEffect/CheckAntiMagic): pack spells that carry HARM without
        DAMAGE/CURSE - Poison, Paralyze, Mana Vampire - now flag the caster
        criminal on innocent players, are bounced by Magic Reflect, and are
        suppressed in REGION_ANTIMAGIC_DAMAGE regions. Previously only
        Damage/Curse-flagged spells counted as harmful.

FIX - The [SPELL n] ON=@Select stage (Source-X SPTRIG_SELECT) now fires from
        SpellEngine.CastStart, the choke point every cast entry funnels
        through (client, scroll, wand, NPC, console); RETURN 1 cancels the
        selection before any resource is spent. Pack form toggles that live
        entirely in ON=@Select (Reaper Form, Stone Form) now run instead of
        silently burning mana. The client-path double-fire was removed from
        the char-trigger fall-through.

FIX - Noble Sacrifice heals/cures the paladin's PARTY members and own pets
        only; any nearby player - including enemies - used to receive the
        area heal+cure.

FIX - Animated Weapon (Mysticism) summons its classic body 0x2B4
        (CREID_ANIMATED_WEAPON); the summon table returned body 0 and the
        creature was invisible.

NEW - Native behaviors for the Sphere custom spells (1000+), mirroring the
        Source-X SPELL_* cases: Light (timed personal light), Hallucination
        (STATF_HALLUCINATING), Stone / Particle Form (petrify for the
        duration), Shrink (NPC packed into a figurine), Refresh / Restore /
        Mana (stat refills), Sustenance (food refill), Gender Swap (body
        toggle for human/elf/gargoyle), Trance (timed Meditation bonus),
        Shield / Steelskin / Stoneskin (timed AR bonus), Regenerate
        (heal-over-time, one tick per 2 s), Ale / Wine / Liquor (timed
        DEX/INT drunkenness penalty), and Bone Armor (converts a skeleton
        corpse into up to five bone armor pieces at reference odds).

FIX - The inert-spell guard now covers the custom id space (1000+): customs
        without a native handler or scripted stage (Chameleon, Beast/Monster
        Form, Enchant, Forget - inert in the reference too) are refused up
        front instead of consuming mana/reagents as silent no-ops.

[2026-07-18] - Startup wiring fixes, plant growth, multi-server list, gump fallback
----------------------------------------

FIX - Noble Sacrifice reaches its native handler: the pack def carries
        spellflag_heal, and the generic heal branch swallowed the cast into
        a plain caster heal — allies were never healed/cured and the
        paladin never paid the sacrifice.

FIX - Field polish: segments are Move_Never and typed IT_FIRE/IT_SPELL
        (players could pick field pieces up); poison field passes the
        caster as the poison SOURCE (kill/crime credit); harming an
        innocent player with any field marks the caster criminal, matching
        the direct harmful-spell rule.

FIX - Dual guild+town membership survives a restart: the reload used ONE
        claim set across every stone, so a character in both pools kept
        only whichever stone loaded first. Claims are now per pool, and
        the general FindGuildFor() excludes town records — guild chat,
        corpse-loot relations and notoriety never see a citizenship as a
        guild membership (FindTownFor added for town surfaces).

FIX - Remaining classic summons mapped: Rising Colossus (0x33D) and Sphere
        custom Summon Undead (random zombie/skeleton/lich, Source-X odds);
        custom Animate Dead (1001) rides the existing corpse-raise flow.
        Animated Weapon stays scripted — the reference has no native
        mapping either.

FIX - The inert-school gate no longer counts SCRIPTED (without ON= stages),
        POLY or TICK as actionable — those have no generic handler, so such
        defs burned mana and no-opped.

NEW - Spell id surface completed against the reference: Bard Masteries
        (701-706), Skill Masteries (707-745) and the full custom Sphere
        tail (1006-1026: Stone, Shrink, Refresh, Restore, Mana, Sustenance,
        Chameleon, Beast/Monster Form, Gender Swap, Trance, Particle Form,
        Shield, Steel/Stoneskin, Regenerate, Enchant, Forget, Ale/Wine/
        Liquor) now exist in the enum.

FIX - Field spells behave like fields (Source-X Spell_Field): segments use
        the CLASSIC field art per spell with E/W-N/S orientation (stone wall
        0x0080, fire 0x398C/0x3996, poison, paralyze, energy) instead of the
        pack's EFFECT_ID — Wall of Stone/Fire/Energy fields were INVISIBLE
        (EFFECT_ID=0). Typed step/stand behavior: fire deals resisted fire
        damage, poison field POISONS (level from the caster's skill at cast),
        paralyze field freezes through the timed Paralyze effect, stone/
        energy walls are pure barriers (blocking via their tiledata) and
        never materialise on top of a character. Duration follows the
        spell's DURATION curve (2-4 min) instead of a fixed 30 s.

FIX - Fixed summon spells carry their classic creatures (Source-X
        m_uiSummonID defaults): Blade Spirit, Energy Vortex, Air/Earth/
        Fire/Water Elemental and Summon Daemon now summon the right body —
        previously everything but the familiar spawned a bodyless creature.

FIX - Town and guild memberships are independent pools (Source-X
        MEMORY_GUILD vs MEMORY_TOWN): a guild member can become a town
        citizen and vice versa; the overhead abbreviation is a guild-only
        surface (town tags never leak onto names); the record type persists
        via the stone (GUILD.ISTOWN tag + item-type fallback).

FIX - The inert-school-spell gate now also refuses school defs whose flags
        are only markers (good/harm/fx/targ with no damage/heal/bless/curse/
        field/summon/area/tick and no scripted stages) — they cast, consumed
        mana/reagents and silently no-opped; Source-X damages only on
        SPELLFLAG_DAMAGE, so such defs are inert there too.

FIX - Custom Sphere spell ids realigned with the reference: 1001 Animate
        Dead, 1002 Bone Armor, 1003 Light, 1004 Fire Bolt, 1005
        Hallucination — Hallucination previously sat at 1001 (Animate
        Dead's slot), so pack spells 1001-1004 resolved to the wrong enum.

NEW - Chivalry works natively: Cleanse by Fire cures, Close Wounds heals
        (generic heal flag), Dispel Evil strips/banishes conjured creatures
        around the paladin (shared with Dispel's DISPELKILLSUMMONS
        pipeline), Divine Fury refills stamina at a timed -20 defense cost,
        Holy Light bursts energy damage at creatures fighting the caster,
        Noble Sacrifice heals+cures nearby allies at the paladin's expense,
        Remove Curse strips ONLY curse-type effects (buffs survive), and
        Sacred Journey travels by rune like Recall. Spellweaving Gift of
        Renewal is a real heal-over-time (the DOT engine now supports heal
        ticks). Consecrate Weapon / Enemy of One and the Bushido/Ninjitsu
        combat uniques stay script territory — the Source-X reference
        itself implements none of them natively (its native surface is
        buff-icon bookkeeping); the pack's script defs run through the
        generic flag engine as before.

NEW - Classic tailoring material flows work: wool/cotton targeted at a
        spinning wheel spins into 3 balls of yarn / 6 spools of thread
        (Source-X IT_WOOL/IT_COTTON), and thread/yarn targeted at a loom
        accumulates on the loom (MORE1 type / MORE2 units, mixed material
        ejects the partial weave) until a bolt of cloth is finished —
        both previously printed only a hint message.

FIX - Craft strokes honour the Source-X @SkillStroke contract: the trigger
        fires per stroke with LOCAL.Strokes seeded and WRITABLE, so a
        script can lengthen or shorten a craft per recipe (the default
        stays the reference's fixed two strokes), and RETURN 1 aborts the
        craft mid-work. (Imbuing stays deferred: the Source-X reference
        itself has no native property/intensity/unravel model — it is
        script territory there too, tracked in PARITY.md.)

NEW - Town stones work: a town stone runs the same stone engine as guild
        stones (Source-X IT_STONE_TOWN == CItemStone). Staff (Counsel+)
        establish the town at a GM-named stone and become its Mayor;
        players request citizenship through the candidate flow, the mayor
        accepts/dismisses, citizens renounce, and town-town / town-guild
        wars and alliances use the shared relation system. Membership now
        stamps the MEMORY_TOWN / MEMORY_GUILD link on the character
        (readable by scripts) and clears it on leave/dismiss/disband —
        the gump paths previously never wrote the memory.

FIX - Throwing weapons are now truly ranged: they use the archery range /
        LOS / movement rules (itemdef RANGE honored), fly a projectile —
        TDATA4/AMMOANIM art, else the weapon's own graphic, with the
        Source-X returning-weapon animation back to the thrower — and
        consume NO pack ammo (the old resolver demanded crossbow bolts for
        any non-bow ranged weapon, so throwing fell back to melee range).
        NPCs with throwing weapons follow the same rules.

NEW - Cannons work: the muzzle runs the Source-X load/fire state machine —
        target sulfurous ash to load powder, a cannon ball to load shot
        (one unit consumed per load, state in MORE1), then target to FIRE:
        boom + muzzle smoke, cannonball bolt within sight range, 80-230
        blunt/fire damage to a character (items take hitpoint damage).
        Double-clicking a cannon ball targets the muzzle to feed it.
        Previously both types only printed a message.

FIX - The Polymorph and Summon Creature selection menus now run the REAL
        cast: the pick is stashed on the caster and the completed cast
        conveys it (Source-X stores the selection then Spell_CastStart), so
        mana, reagents, cast time, fizzle, interruption and the TIMED
        polymorph revert all apply — the menus previously swapped the body /
        spawned the creature instantly and permanently. The direct GM/script
        POLY and SUMMON verbs are unchanged outside a cast menu.

FIX - Mana requirement and consumption now share one discounted cost at
        both cast start and completion (wand = free, scroll = half, curse
        modifiers via the effective cost). Previously the start demanded the
        FULL effective cost even for a wand, while the completion checked
        only the base cost — wands needed mana they never consume, scrolls
        over-required at start, and a cast could complete on less mana than
        it consumed.

FIX - "Use item, pick target" flows now pin the used item (Source-X
        OnTarg_Use_Item): the response re-validates that the source item
        still exists in the same parent it had when the cursor opened —
        a key/tool moved or handed to another player mid-target refuses the
        use — and the item's @TargOn_Char/@TargOn_Item/@TargOn_Ground
        triggers fire before the native behavior (RETURN 1 cancels).
        Applies to bandage/lockpick/scissors/key/dye/smelt/pick/fish pole/
        seed/pitcher and the weapon prompts.

NEW - Classic blade targets are reachable again: a sharp weapon targeted at
        a corpse carves it (DeathEngine.CarveCorpse finally has a player
        input path), at a sheep shears wool, at a dead fish fillets raw
        fish steaks, at a crop/foliage harvests it, and an axe at the
        ground starts Lumberjacking at the spot — matching the Source-X
        sharp-weapon target block beyond the old poisoning/repair pair.

FIX - Potions are now spell-driven (Source-X Use_Drink): a potion conveys
        the spell in MORE1 at strength MORE2 through the spell engine, so
        strength/agility potions apply TIMED effects — the old code did a
        permanent Str/Dex += 10 (a stat exploit), defaulted every tagless
        liquid to a heal potion (a full water pitcher healed 10 hits), and
        deleted the container. Fixed-point script decimals (MORE2=50.0 ->
        500) now parse, and drinking returns the empty container from the
        itemdef TDATA1 (empty bottle / empty pitcher).

FIX - BOT/STRESS/RESPAWN/RESTOCK typed over the telnet admin console now
        work. The telnet console has its own command processor and those
        harness/maintenance events were only wired on the local console
        processor, so the documented telnet commands were silently dropped.

DOC - README performance section remeasured on the current build (2026-07-20,
        5-vCPU VM): fresh scenario table with verdicts, login/boot/save
        results, corrected tick-rate wording (100 ms / 10 Hz, Source-X
        MSECS_PER_TICK) and GC mode; roadmap pruned of shipped items
        (plant growth, light burnout); both README.md and README-TR.md.

NEW - Ships can be dry-docked in game: the OWNER (or staff) double-clicks
        the tillerman while standing OFF the ship and the ship converts back
        to a deed in the backpack (hold cargo moves to a crate). Aboard or as
        a non-owner the tillerman just talks — and his lines now come from
        the tillerman item instead of appearing above the player (Source-X
        pItem->Speak). Source-X leaves dry-dock to shard scripts; this pack
        scripts none, so the engine provides the classic OSI flow.

FIX - Ship speech commands ("forward", "back", ...) now move the ship. Sphere
        speech sections stack alias patterns over one shared body (on=forward
        / on=foreward / on=unfurl sail -> SHIPFORE); matching any alias but
        the LAST collected an empty body, so most command spellings silently
        did nothing. Any alias in a group now executes the body that follows
        the last consecutive ON= line. This also fixes every aliased NPC
        speech table in the pack, not just ships.

FIX - The ship boarding plank now visually opens. The open-plank art comes
        from the side itemdef's TDATA1 (Source-X model: 03eb1 -> 03ed5); the
        open code only looked at a MORE1 staging value that freshly-placed
        ships never carry, so the plank changed type but kept the closed
        graphic. TDATA1 is now the fallback; closing restores the side art.

FIX - Double-clicking the house sign from INSIDE the house no longer makes
        the sign vanish (and demolish/redeed is reachable again). The item
        double-click gate ran a line-of-sight raycast; with house walls now
        being real LOS occluders, the sign on the wall failed the ray from
        indoors and the server "corrected" the client by deleting the item
        from view — so the gump never opened and the house could not be
        redeeded from inside. Source-X Event_DoubleClick checks
        containment/distance only (no raycast), same as our mobile dclick
        path; the item path now matches. Combat/NPC/spell LOS is unchanged.

FIX - .dupe now makes FULL clones and honours its copy count. A duped item
        previously kept only graphic/hue/amount/name — a duped house or ship
        deed lost its More1/multi-reference tags and came out blank, and any
        scripted item lost its type, link, tags and events. Duplication now
        uses the full-clone path (Source-X CreateDupeItem). ".dupe 10" also
        copies 10 times (Source-X CIV_DUPE argument; top-level runs clamped
        to 25 like the reference complexity cap) instead of always once.

FIX - Ships and houses now render completely. Two halves of one root cause:
        placed multis (ships, classic houses) were sent to the client as plain
        items, and a plain item with a multi graphic renders as nothing — the
        client only draws a structure when the world packet carries the multi
        data type (0xF3 type 2 / 0x1A graphic|0x4000), which previously only
        custom-house foundations got. Now every placed structure is sent as a
        multi, so the client draws the full hull/walls itself from multi.mul.
        Accordingly the server materialises ONLY the invisible placeholder
        components (tiller, planks, hatch, doors, house sign) as working
        items, exactly like Source-X — visible statics are never created as
        server items (no double-draw). Ships placed under the previous build
        should be redeeded and placed again.

FIX - Target cursor no longer "auto-fires": a spell cast (or any target
        command) could resolve instantly against yourself with no cursor
        shown, and only the next attempt displayed one. Root cause: a target
        response left over from a cancelled cursor session (the client zeroes
        its cursor id after a server-side cancel) was accepted as a live pick
        outside a narrow 2s window. Responses must now echo the armed cursor
        id exactly — anything else is dropped. Additionally, per Source-X
        Spell_TargCheck, a ground pick for an object-target spell (e.g. Night
        Sight) now aborts with "target must be an object" instead of silently
        casting on yourself.

FIX - Deleting a ship or house multi with .nuke/.remove/script REMOVE no longer
        leaves a ghost structure in the registry. The ownership counters kept
        counting the deleted ship ("you cannot have more ships"), and its
        region and component items leaked. Deletion now tears the structure
        down like Source-X (~CItemMulti): keys removed, component items
        deleted, region freed, registry entry erased. No deed is refunded on
        destroy — use dry-dock/redeed to get the deed back.

PERF - World-save snapshot capture now runs in parallel. Building the save
        records (property formatting per object) dominated the save stall
        (~0.45s of a 0.75s save on a 32K-object world); the capture is a pure
        read of the frozen world, so it now fans out across cores. This shrinks
        the freeze in both sync (SAVEBACKGROUND=0) and background save modes.

FIX - Placed ships and houses now materialise their full structure. The multi
        component visibility flag was read inverted, so a placed ship consisted
        of only the five invisible placeholder pieces (mast anchor, tiller,
        hatch, planks) with no hull, and houses would have shown no walls. The
        flag now matches the client's own rule (ClassicUO: flags != 0 = drawn
        static part; flags == 0 = placeholder replaced by working server items
        like doors and the tillerman).

FIX - Items bought from NPC vendors now run their scripted @Create body. Vendor
        stock was built as bare items (graphic + name + price only), so a
        purchased ship or house deed carried no structure reference ("that deed
        is blank") and any vendor-sold item with @Create-driven properties lost
        them. Stock now materialises through the same path as loot/spawns/.add.

FIX - Deleting a player's backpack (GM .remove) no longer breaks item drops:
        the character kept a cached reference to the deleted pack, so the
        automatic pack recreation never fired and items dropped onto the player
        landed inside a deleted container and vanished. The cached reference is
        now invalidated on delete, a fresh pack is created on the next drop
        (reference-engine GetPackSafe behavior), and the wearer is redrawn so
        the client sees the new pack before its contents.

PERFORMANCE - NPC route-finding is budgeted per tick: at most four full A*
        searches run in one NPC decision phase; additional chasers wait ~150ms
        for their turn (they keep facing the target meanwhile). A chase burst
        used to stack several 500-node searches into a single phase, visible as
        a 130ms tick on small servers. The background world save is also
        gentler now: it writes on one below-normal-priority thread with
        sequential shard writes, so the game loop wins the CPU during the
        write window instead of competing with parallel compression tasks.

PERFORMANCE - Opening any gump, clicking any dialog button or requesting any menu
        no longer re-reads and re-parses the entire script pack from disk. The
        dialog/menu section lookups used to scan every .scp file per interaction
        (a ~400ms main-loop stall per click on a real pack — worst for ids that
        do not exist in the pack at all, like the native help page fallback,
        which paid the full scan on every Help click). The sections are now
        retained at script-load time and looked up in constant time; resync
        rebuilds the caches.

PERFORMANCE - World saves can now write in the background (sphere.ini
        SAVEBACKGROUND > 0): the main loop only captures an immutable snapshot of
        the world — the expensive shard/encode/write phase runs on a worker
        thread, so the multi-hundred-millisecond save stall shrinks to the
        capture time. Saves never overlap (a new cycle is skipped while one is
        writing), the shutdown save waits for any in-flight write, and the
        atomic temp-file commit is unchanged. SAVEBACKGROUND=0 keeps the old
        fully synchronous behavior.

PERFORMANCE - Network hardening: accepts are budgeted per pass (a reconnect flood
        no longer holds the main loop in the accept while-loop), the per-IP
        connection limit uses a maintained counter instead of scanning all 1100
        slots on every accept, and login connections now use the same
        non-blocking batched sends as game connections — a stalled client mid
        login can no longer block the flush pass. NetworkThreads/UseAsyncNetwork
        ini keys are documented as deliberate no-ops (main-loop network design).

FIX - The server now validates its engine wiring at startup and refuses to boot
        half-wired: eleven mandatory hooks (movement cast-interrupt, NPC night
        lights, speech routing, shutdown/broadcast commands, world resolvers and
        more) are checked after wiring completes, turning the silent
        "assigned before the engine existed" bug class into an immediate,
        named startup error.

FEATURE - House/ship deed placement now raises the multi-preview cursor (0x99):
        the client ghosts the full building footprint at the cursor instead of a
        plain crosshair, and the server applies the reference engine's anchor-Y
        correction so the house lands exactly where the preview showed it. The
        placement reply is also fully re-validated (deed still in the same pack,
        reachable, caster alive and unfrozen) so a deed traded or dropped while
        the cursor was up can no longer place.

FEATURE - Lit light sources now live a real lifecycle: one charge burns per
        minute (20 by default), the flame goes out by itself when the charges run
        dry, a burned-out source can never be relit, and static/decoration lights
        burn forever. The remaining burn time survives restarts.

FIX - Ship movement and placement now treat static water tiles (coast fills,
        harbour water laid as statics) as sailable, and blocking world items on
        the water line stop the hull the same way docks and rocks do. The smooth
        boat-move packet (0xF6) also carries the full deck-object list, so
        smooth-sailing clients move passengers and cargo with the hull instead
        of waiting for individual resends.

FIX - Characters younger than the MinCharDeleteTime day count (default 7) can no
        longer be deleted from the character-select screen; the client shows the
        proper "not old enough" reason and staff accounts bypass the gate. The
        creation timestamp now persists in saves using the reference engine's
        CREATE key (age-based), and pre-existing characters without a stamp stay
        deletable.

FIX - Casting a spell from the unimplemented spell schools (Bushido, Ninjitsu,
        Spellweaving, Mysticism and the rest of that id range) now clearly reports
        "not supported yet" up front instead of consuming mana and reagents and
        then silently doing nothing. Script packs that implement those spells
        themselves (flags, effect curves, or ON= trigger stages) are unaffected.

PERFORMANCE - The automatic worker-thread count now leaves one core to the main
        thread instead of saturating every core, which starved the serial tick
        phases on shared/overcommitted VMs. An explicit MulticoreWorkerCount
        still wins. Tick telemetry also gained honest sub-phases: the parallel
        world tick is measured separately from the pre-compute setup, and the
        previously unmeasured replay/recorder/macro/reschedule work between
        apply and flush now reports as its own post_apply phase.

FIX - Double-clicking an NPC while standing near a map static door no longer
        toggles that door and makes the NPC vanish. The static-door fallback ran
        before the character lookup and, without validating the clicked serial,
        toggled the nearest door (with its open/close sound) and rebroadcast the
        door art under the NPC's serial — the client then showed the mobile as a
        door graphic until the next view refresh. The fallback now runs only when
        the clicked serial is neither an item nor a character, and the door art
        broadcast only ever reuses the synthetic static-door serials. Also removed
        the LOS raycast from the character double-click gate (the reference checks
        distance and visibility only), which could likewise delete a drawn mobile
        from the client when clicked through a wall. Temporary [static_door] field
        diagnostics removed.

PERFORMANCE - NPC chase pathfinding is now bounded like the reference engine and
        runs off the main thread. Three changes: (1) route-finding only engages for
        targets 2-13 tiles away and searches inside the same 28x28 local box the
        reference uses, so a walled-off target exhausts a small area instead of the
        whole node budget; (2) a chase route no longer treats the tile the target
        itself stands on as a hard wall — that made every route toward a character
        "unreachable", burning the full search budget each time while the NPC fell
        back to blind side-steps; routes now actually find detours around obstacles;
        (3) the search itself is precomputed in the parallel NPC decision phase, so
        the single-threaded apply phase finds a ready-made route instead of spending
        up to ~17ms per NPC on it. Behavior stays serial-authoritative: the serial
        phase re-validates every precomputed step and recomputes if the world moved.

PERFORMANCE - Tooltip pushes during view updates are now version-only, like the
        reference engine's default tooltip mode: when objects enter view the server
        sends the tiny revision packet and the client requests the full property list
        only for tooltips missing from its own cache. Full data is still pushed
        immediately when the client asks, when the tooltip actually changed, or in
        the send-full mode. A login or teleport into a crowded area now costs one
        small packet per object instead of a full serialized tooltip each.

PERFORMANCE - The built AOS tooltip is now cached on the object itself (the reference
        engine's model): one build serves every observer, expiry is purely time-based
        (sphere.ini ToolTipCache seconds), and the entry is no longer thrown away when
        the object scrolls out of a client's view. Previously every client kept its
        own copy and dropped it on view-exit, so login/teleport bursts rebuilt every
        visible object's tooltip from scratch; now re-entry is served from the shared
        cache. Explicit invalidation still forces a rebuild and bumps the revision so
        clients re-request changed tooltips.

PERFORMANCE - Speech no longer sweeps every nearby ground item per spoken line. The
        reference engine keeps a per-sector count of items that can actually hear
        (comm crystals; here also multis/ships, which route speech the same way) and
        skips the item sweep entirely when that count is zero — the common case. The
        same counter model is now maintained on item place/remove/retype, so shards
        without a crystal or house in earshot pay nothing per utterance. Scripted
        item @Hear still forces the full sweep, since then any item may listen.

PERFORMANCE - Tooltips no longer run a line-of-sight raycast per object. The reference
        engine gates tooltips on distance and visibility only (the client draws objects
        through walls, so their tooltips must arrive too); the extra per-object raycast
        during view updates was both a behavior mismatch (objects visible on screen
        could silently lack a tooltip) and a measurable cost when many objects enter
        view at once. Now matches Source-X: distance + visibility, no raycast.

INTERNAL - Removed redundant unused code paths flagged by a code review: a second
        expansion feature-flag lookup table and two never-instantiated scripting shells
        (a global-variable holder and a conditional-evaluator wrapper) whose real
        behaviour already lives in the running engine, so wiring them would only risk a
        divergent second source of truth. Verified-intentional scaffolding that was
        wrongly flagged as dead (the bot-performance CI gate, the fast-walk protocol
        packets, and the speed-hack audit hook) was kept and documented instead. No
        behaviour change.

PERFORMANCE - Removed a redundant per-NPC network scan when speaking near a crowd.
        Each NPC that turned to face a speaker did its own immediate broadcast of the
        turn to nearby clients — a separate scan per NPC on every spoken line. The turn
        is already carried by the normal view update (the same movement packet, to the
        same clients), so the extra broadcast was dropped. NPCs still face whoever
        addresses them; the turn is just delivered on the next view refresh.

PERFORMANCE - Cheaper speech handling in NPC-dense areas. When a player speaks, every
        nearby NPC runs a hear handler; it fired the global f_onchar_speech hook and the
        first-contact greeting trigger for every NPC on every line, even when no script
        defined them. Both are now skipped when unused, so a spoken line near a large
        crowd of NPCs costs noticeably less. NPCs still turn to face the speaker and
        scripts that do define those hooks behave exactly as before.

PERFORMANCE - Smoother NPC wake-up after login near a crowd. Logging in lights up the
        sector window around the player and could wake ~140 NPCs into the exact same
        100ms timer slot, so their AI all ran in one tick and caused a brief stall. The
        wake is now spread across ~8 slots by a stable per-NPC offset, so the load is
        distributed over a short window instead of one spike. Single-target wakes
        (an NPC reacting to being attacked) are unaffected and still immediate.

PERFORMANCE - Faster view updates in crowded areas / on login. Every object entering a
        client's view builds a tooltip, and that path fired the @ClientTooltip script
        trigger for every object even when no script hooked it — re-parsing the object's
        script definition and allocating per object. It is now skipped when unused (the
        same IsTrigUsed gate the single-click path already uses), so entering a busy
        region or logging in near many objects costs far less. Scripts that do hook the
        tooltip trigger behave exactly as before.

FIXED - Customizable house foundations now render on modern (SA/High Seas) clients.
        The multi body was sent to the client as a plain item instead of a multi (the
        0xF3 packet's data-type byte was hard-coded to "item", and the 0x1A packet sent
        the raw multi index which is below the client's multi range), so the client
        never treated a foundation as a house and silently discarded the streamed
        custom-house design. Multi bodies are now flagged as multis on the wire
        (data-type 2 on 0xF3; the 0x4000 multi bit on 0x1A) while the stored id is
        unchanged. Fixed (non-custom) houses and ships are unaffected — they already
        render from their placed component tiles.

CHANGED - State recording is now OFF by default. This optional diagnostic/replay
        feature took a periodic full-world snapshot on every server whether or not
        anyone used it. It is now disabled unless you set StateRecordingEnabled=1 in
        sphere.ini, so servers no longer pay that cost by default. Existing setups
        that rely on recording must add that line to keep it on.

PERFORMANCE - Removed the periodic latency spike from sleeping-sector upkeep. Item
        timers, spawns and decay in sectors with no nearby player used to all run in a
        single tick every few minutes, causing a recurring stall. That upkeep is now
        spread across ticks with a small per-tick budget and a resume cursor, so it
        completes over a short window instead of one big burst. Nothing is skipped:
        every eligible sector is still serviced once per cycle.

PERFORMANCE - Two per-tick/periodic sweeps no longer scan the entire object list.
        The TIMERF timer sweep now walks only the handful of objects that actually
        hold a pending timer, and the item-decay catch-up now walks only loose
        ground items. Both cost now scales with the small working set rather than the
        total world size, so large worlds no longer pay a fixed per-tick tax for
        timers and decay. Behaviour is unchanged: the same timers fire and the same
        items decay, just found more cheaply.

IMPROVED - House/ship placement now explains why it failed. Instead of a single
        "Cannot place here", a rejected deed placement reports a specific reason
        (house/ship limit reached, structure not defined, off the map edge, location
        blocked, or a script veto). Classic small ships can be re-placed from a
        dry-dock deed again (a raw multi id of 0 was wrongly treated as "no id"), and
        the first custom-house foundation deed now opens as a customizable foundation
        even without a CUSTOMHOUSE tag — the type is read from its [MULTIDEF].

FIXED - Test/doc hygiene: three local-only MUL diagnostic tests reported as passed
        when their data was absent instead of skipping; they now report as Skipped.
        Trigger docs synced — NPCSeeWantItem is wired and fires (the outstanding
        not-fired char trigger is now UserVirtue, the virtue-gump path).

FIXED - Several sphere.ini settings were parsed but never applied. Now honored:
        GameMinuteLength (world clock; was a hardcoded 20s/game-minute), the speech
        hearing distances (DistanceTalk/Whisper/Yell), MaxFame/MaxKarma/MinKarma
        limits, UseHttp (the web status endpoint can now be turned off), MapReadId
        (which map*.mul group to load, distinct from the client-facing MapSendId), and
        MapViewSize (default network view range). TICKPERIOD is now a legacy alias for
        the canonical ServerTickMs, and the <TICKPERIOD> script value returns the real
        tick interval. Defaults were aligned to the previous behavior, so unset configs
        are unchanged; only explicit sphere.ini values now take effect.

FIXED - Houses and ships could be lost on restart. Their world item stores the type
        (Multi / MultiCustom / Ship) only at runtime, but the saver never wrote it, and
        the item's BaseId is a raw multi index with no ITEMDEF to re-derive it from — so
        after a reload the structure read as a plain item and the housing/ship engines
        never re-registered it. The saver now persists the structure TYPE and it is
        restored on load. Old saves without it keep the previous legacy behavior.

ADDED - Placed houses/ships now use their script [MULTIDEF] metadata. The multi
        registry held only the binary geometry from multi.mul; the script name, type,
        storage and vendor limits were parsed but never merged in, so houses got a
        blank name and a flat storage default. The metadata is now overlaid by the
        shared multi id, and a placed house takes its script BaseStorage (e.g. 489 for
        a small stone house) instead of the hardcoded default. (Dynamic components —
        doors, signs, tillermen — and script regions remain a separate step.)

FIXED - Scripted house/ship deeds could load as plain items. A deed written as
        "[ITEMDEF i_deed_house] ID=i_deed" with no TYPE of its own stayed
        ItemType.Normal, so double-clicking it never reached the deed handler and
        placement never started. ID=<defname> now inherits the referenced base's
        TYPE (matching Source-X, which dupes the referenced typed base), so such a
        deed becomes a real deed. Type only — a graphic-only ID= reference does not
        pull in unrelated layer/tiledata.

FIXED - House/ship placement failed ("Cannot place here") on modern multi.mul data.
        The multi reader assumed the original 12-byte component record, but High Seas+
        data uses a 16-byte record (a trailing ship-access dword). Read the wrong way,
        every component offset shifted and the footprint inflated to thousands of tiles,
        so the map-bounds check rejected every location. The reader now auto-detects the
        12- vs 16-byte layout (from the index block lengths, with an offset-plausibility
        tiebreak) and reads the ship-access field on High Seas records.

PERF  - The state recorder no longer copies the whole world object table on every
        server tick. It walks the character roster only when its move-scan (2s) or
        snapshot (15s) interval is actually due, and uses the character-only roster
        instead of the full ~52K-object table — eliminating a large per-tick
        allocation (~10x/sec) that added GC pressure.

FIXED - Movement-based spell interruption was dead at real startup. MovementEngine
        was given the SpellEngine reference before SpellEngine existed, binding
        null; the wiring now runs after SpellEngine is constructed.

FIXED - NPCs always assumed daylight. The NpcAI night-light hook was wired behind
        an "if WeatherEngine != null" guard that ran before WeatherEngine existed,
        so it was skipped entirely; it is now wired after WeatherEngine is built.

FIXED - .SHUTDOWN and .BROADCAST admin/GM commands were accepted but did nothing
        (no subscriber). .SHUTDOWN now ends the main loop cleanly; .BROADCAST sends
        the message to every in-world client.

ADDED - The world is now saved on a clean shutdown (SaveOnShutdown, default on;
        set 0 to disable), so changes since the last periodic save are not lost on
        a planned stop.



ADDED - Plant growth (Source-X CItemPlant crop regrow). Planted crops and foliage
        now advance through their growth chain on a timer: each tick a crop grows
        into its next stage (ITEMDEF TDATA2); a fully grown crop drops its fruit
        (TDATA3) and resets to the first stage (TDATA1), hidden as an invisible
        regrowing plot (staff still see it) until it grows back. A crop moved into
        a container dies. Planting a seed starts the growth chain, and reaping a
        mature crop resets and regrows it instead of a flat cooldown. (This is the
        Source-X crop model, not the OSI plant-bowl minigame, which Source-X has no
        implementation of.)

ADDED - Config-driven multi-server login list (0xA8). The server list now uses the
        configured ServName/ServIP instead of a hardcoded "SphereNet"/127.0.0.1
        entry, and can advertise additional shards via a new SERVERLIST ini key
        ("name,ip,port" entries separated by ';', capped at 32). Server selection
        relays to the chosen shard's ip/port. (KR/EC 0xFFFFFFFF-seed handshake is
        still deferred — it needs a live KR/EC client to verify the crypto.)

ADDED - Uncompressed 0xB0 gump fallback for very old (pre-3.0) clients. Modern and
        not-yet-detected clients keep the compressed 0xDD gump, so the established
        path is unchanged.

[2026-07-17] - Bandage macro, virtue transport, region jail, HCI/luck suit aggregation
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Hit Chance Increase (HCI) now aggregates the whole equipped suit. The
        AOS to-hit formula read HCI from the attacker's own tag plus the weapon/
        talisman only, so HCI on armor or jewelry was silently ignored. It now
        reads the full suit (all equipped layers), matching Source-X's equip-time
        accumulation. Defense Chance Increase (DCI) on the target is read the same
        way. Both keep the +45% cap.

ADDED - Luck now aggregates the equipped suit for the status display. Each item's
        LUCK adds to the number shown on the status bar (previously only the base
        character luck was shown). Matching Source-X, luck remains display-only and
        is not wired into loot or any other mechanic.

ADDED - Bandage macro (client bandage hotkey, 0xBF 0x2C). The client's
        bandage-target hotkey now applies a bandage to a pre-selected target with
        no target cursor. This subcommand was previously mislabeled as virtue
        invocation; it is the Source-X PacketBandageMacro carrying [bandage uid]
        [target uid]. The handler verifies the item is a bandage and routes it
        through the Healing skill against the given target.

FIXED - Virtue invocation moved to its correct transport. Virtue hotkeys
        (Honor/Sacrifice/Valor) are delivered by the real client on the 0x12
        text-command packet as ext-type 0xF4 (EXTCMD_INVOKE_VIRTUE), not on
        0xBF 0x2C. @UserVirtueInvoke now fires from that path with the virtue id
        in N1 and no longer collides with the internal skill-lock funnel.

ADDED - Region-driven jail cells. The JAIL staff command and the login
        re-confine now locate the cell from an AREADEF region named "jail" (or
        "jailN" for a numbered cell) instead of hardcoded coordinates, matching
        Source-X GetRegionPoint. Syntax: JAIL <serial> [minutes] [cell]. Shards
        with no jail region keep the previous Britain coordinates. New FORGIVE /
        PARDON staff commands release an inmate (alias of UNJAIL), and the
        .forgive character verb now actually frees a jailed character.

FIXED - RESPHYSICALMAX was never written to the world save. The other four
        per-element resist caps (fire/cold/poison/energy) were persisted but the
        physical cap was dropped on every save. These caps remain display/storage
        only, matching Source-X, which does not clamp damage to them.

[2026-07-16] - NPC keyword word-matching, GM yell broadcast fix, vendor leash
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Panel Scripts page listed nothing when the Host process served the
        panel. SphereNet.Host read the script directory with the key name
        "ScpFilesDir" (the C# property name) instead of the actual sphere.ini
        key SCPFILES, so the lookup always missed and fell through to a
        "scripts" folder next to sphere.ini. With SCPFILES pointing anywhere
        else, PanelContext.ScriptsPath stayed null and GET /api/scripts
        returned an empty list. The in-process SphereNet.Server host was
        unaffected — it resolves the path through SphereConfig.

FIXED - sphere.ini LOG= was parsed into nothing. SphereConfig declared LogDir
        but LoadFromIni never read the key, and no code consumed the property;
        "logs" was hardcoded at the Serilog file sink and in the Host crash
        handler instead. LOG= now binds to SphereConfig.LogDir and both call
        sites honour it. Relative values follow the same CWD-first rule as the
        other path settings.

ADDED - sphere.ini now ships WORLDSAVE= and ACCTFILES= entries. Both keys were
        already read by SphereConfig, but were absent from the shipped file, so
        their directories could only be changed by knowing the undocumented key
        names. Values match the previous defaults (save/, accounts/) — no
        behavior change for existing installs.

ADDED - Panel self-update (Updates page, new sidebar entry). A new workflow
        (.github/workflows/release.yml) builds a win-x64 package on every main
        commit and refreshes the assets of a rolling "nightly" prerelease; the
        panel checks it, downloads it, and applies it in place. New endpoints:
        GET /api/update/status, POST /api/update/check, POST /api/update/apply.
        New sphere.ini keys: APPUPDATEREPO (empty = feature off and the page is
        hidden), APPUPDATECHANNEL, APPUPDATERUNTIME, APPUPDATECHECKMINUTES
        (0 = no background check), APPUPDATETOKEN. Distinct from the existing
        APPUPDATEREPODIR / update.cmd flow, which builds from source and needs
        git + SDK + Node on the box; this one only needs network.
        Release assets, not Actions artifacts: artifact downloads require an
        actions:read token even on a public repo and expire after 90 days,
        whereas releases/download/<tag>/<name> is anonymous, unauthenticated
        and not API-rate-limited. The artifact is still uploaded for CI use.
        The workflow uploads version.json LAST, after the zip is fully up, so
        the "latest" pointer can never reference a half-uploaded package.
        Version identity is version.json next to the exe; ordering uses
        github.run_number since SHAs cannot be compared. No version.json means
        a source build, which reports IsDevBuild and refuses to apply so a
        developer's own binaries are never silently overwritten — build.ps1's
        existing keep-list already strips version.json from local Release
        output, so this is automatic.
        Applying is always an explicit operator action; the background check
        only lights the sidebar badge. The flow saves the world first and
        aborts if the save is rejected, verifies the package SHA256 against the
        published checksum, rejects zip entries that escape the staging dir,
        and validates that the extracted tree actually holds Host, Server, the
        panel assets and a matching version.json before touching anything.
        Because the running Host holds a lock on SphereNet.Host.exe, the swap
        is done by a short-lived external PowerShell process (kept as a string
        in UpdaterScript.cs so it cannot be replaced by the very update it is
        applying): it waits for the Host to exit, backs up, swaps, and
        relaunches — restoring the backup and still relaunching on failure.
        config/, save/ and scripts/ are absent from the package and never
        touched; panel/ is replaced wholesale so stale hashed bundles cannot
        linger. Details land in logs/update.log.

ADDED - AdminPanelAutoFill (sphere.ini, default 0): pre-fills the admin panel
        login field with ADMINPASSWORD so a local operator does not retype it.
        Handing the panel's only secret to the browser needs all three gates:
        the flag on, the request from loopback, and ADMINPASSWORD still stored
        as plaintext — the setup wizard writes an MD5 hash, which has no
        plaintext to recover, so autofill stops after setup runs. New endpoint
        GET /api/auth/local-hint returns {password: null} when any gate fails.
        Leave off for anything reachable through a reverse proxy: the proxy
        also connects from loopback, so remote users would receive the password.

FIXED - Monster corpses were empty (Balron field report): ITEM=loot_x in
        @NPCRestock bodies resolved the defname, saw RES_TEMPLATE instead
        of RES_ITEMDEF and silently spawned nothing. Source-X
        CItem::CreateHeader accepts a template in defname position and
        ReadTemplate pours the whole loot list into the pack
        (CItem.cpp:461-539/586). The ITEM verb now expands sequential
        templates: per-row R# 1-in-N chance and {lo hi} dice amounts
        (CreateHeader parity), inline weighted pools in defname position
        ({ a w b w }, "0" = empty slot), nested templates, CONTAINER=
        sub-bags, and numeric itemdef rows (ITEM=0EED). The template
        loader keeps raw row args and CONTAINER rows; vendor stock
        enumeration skips container rows. NOTE: the live pack shipped
        with 33 ON=@NPCRestock and 423 ITEM= loot lines commented out in
        the monster chardefs (likely because the loot rows did nothing) —
        those are re-enabled pack-side.

FIXED - A dismounted mount ignored its owner's fights: dismount put the
        pet in Follow mode, which only self-defends. Source-X leaves the
        dismounted pet idle (CCharUse.cpp:1205); an idle owned pet
        defaults to guarding its owner (NPC_LookAtChar,
        CCharNPCAct.cpp:1036) and NPC_Act_Guard attacks whatever the
        owner fights (CCharNPCAct.cpp:1300-1303). Dismount now sets
        Guard mode on the rider, so the mount joins the owner's attack.
        MountEngine.Dismount also clears STATF_RIDDEN itself (parity
        with Use_Figurine) instead of relying on each caller — a path
        that forgot left the mount skipped by its own AI tick.

FIXED - Fast consecutive chat messages silently vanished: an invented
        speech rate limit (10 messages per 5s sliding window, commands
        consuming the same quota) dropped everything past the cap.
        Source-X Event_Talk has no such limit — the throttle is removed;
        extreme packet floods remain handled at the network layer
        (MaxPacketsPerTick / FloodDetectionCount).

FIXED - Service NPCs answered unrelated player-to-player chatter: the
        built-in keyword dispatch used substring Contains(), so any word
        embedding a keyword triggered a response — Turkish "buyur"/
        "buyuk"/"buyu" contain "buy" (vendors opened the buy gump and
        barked on nearly every sentence), "banka" contains "bank". All
        service keywords (buy/sell/purchase/train/teach/heal/resurrect/
        cure/stable/claim/balance/help/guards) now match whole words;
        "bank" matches as a word prefix so "banka"/"bankaya" keep
        working. The withdraw/check amount parser is word-bounded too —
        "check" inside another word can no longer trigger a withdrawal.

FIXED - A staff yell disconnected the client: GM yell ran the NPC-hear
        loop over every character in the world AND swept every world item
        for @Hear (9999-tile scans), stalling the main loop until the
        client timed out. Source-X promotes a Counsel+ yell to
        TALKMODE_BROADCAST (CCharAct.cpp:3575) — a CLIENT-only broadcast.
        Now the speech packet goes to every playing client via a direct
        client-list path (BroadcastNearby global branch; the sector walk
        is never entered for huge ranges), while NPC/item hearing stays
        at normal yell earshot (48 tiles). Ghost yell per-recipient
        garbling is also clamped to earshot.

CHANGED - Service NPCs (vendor/banker/stable brains) keep to their post:
        they wandered up to ~3 tiles plus drift and strolled out of their
        buildings. They now pull back beyond 1 tile from home and only
        wander while standing on it (max ~2 tiles drift, ignores MOREZ
        by design — same shard rule as spawn-on-gem).

[2026-07-16] - Vendor detection unified across dclick, speech, and trade paths
----------------------------------------

CHANGED - NPC spawners now place the child ON the worldgem bit (deliberate
        deviation from Source-X, shard owner request). Source-X GenerateChar
        scatters the child MoveNear(pt, rand(MOREZ)+1) up to MOREZ tiles
        from the gem (CCSpawn.cpp:433); SphereNet mirrored that. MOREZ
        (third MOREP field) keeps its wander-leash role (HOMEDIST,
        CCSpawn.cpp:640). The random scatter survives only as a fallback
        when the gem's own tile is impassable (gem buried in a wall).
        @Spawn scripts that set an explicit position still win. Item
        spawners are unchanged (still scatter within MAXDIST).

FIXED - Double-clicking some vendors opened the paperdoll while "buy"
        speech listed their goods: the speech path widened BRAIN_HUMAN
        NPCs into vendors by role name (legacy packs ship e.g. c_h_vendor
        with brain_vendor commented out and NPC=brain_human active), but
        the double-click, context-menu, and 0x3B/0x9F trade-validation
        gates checked NpcBrain == Vendor strictly. All paths now share one
        VendorEngine.IsVendorLike predicate (brain Vendor, or Human/None
        brain with a vendor/shopkeep/merchant name keyword), so any NPC
        that answers "buy" also opens the buy/sell dialog on double-click
        and can actually complete purchases and sales. Restock, the script
        BUY verb vendor resolution, and the owned-vendor CASH command use
        the same predicate.

FIXED - Context-menu "Sell" on a vendor only printed a sysmessage stub;
        it now opens the sell list like the speech path.

[2026-07-16] - Field batch 2: message formatting, speech color, dismount follow
----------------------------------------

FIXED - "You pull out a %s!" printed literally: nine call sites passed
        %s-bearing messages through Get() with no arguments (fishing success,
        detect-hidden, begging, resurrect, pet guard, party decline/leave).
        All now format with the proper name per the Source-X SysMessagef
        call. The hiding-fail path printed DEFMSG_HIDING_STUMBLE (a
        walk-into-hidden-char message) with a raw %s — Source-X Skill_Hiding
        FAIL sends no text at all (CCharSkill.cpp:2481), so it was removed.

FIXED - Skill-gain text removed: Source-X Skill_SetBase sends no "skill
        increased" message — only the 0x3A skill-window refresh
        (CCharSkill.cpp:222). The invented blue line is gone; shards can add
        one via @SkillChange.

FIXED - Dismounting left the mount masterless: it fell into the Animal brain
        and wandered off, and GM inspection showed no IPet memory. Source-X
        Use_Figurine re-owns the mount to the rider on every dismount
        (NPC_PetSetOwner → MEMORY_IPET + follow, CCharUse.cpp:1202-1206);
        MountEngine.Dismount now assigns ownership (which also mirrors the
        IPet memory item) and sets follow mode.

ADDED - NPC speech honors SPEECHCOLOR/SPEECHCOLOROVERRIDE (Source-X
        CChar.cpp:4147): default stays the reference light gray 0x03B2, but
        scripts can now color an NPC's overhead speech per character.

FIXED - First cast after a pause hit the PREVIOUS target with no cursor:
        when a new cursor replaces an open one, ClassicUO zeroes its stored
        cursor id after our cancel, so its queued last-target reply arrived
        as id-0 + old serial and slipped past the session-id guard. Any
        id-less response inside the 2s replacement window is now swallowed
        (cancel echo or stale pick alike); cursor teardown also retires the
        session id and echo window so nothing lingers across exchanges.

FIXED - Fixed-point spawner NPCs (MOREZ=0, e.g. the bank's vendor) strolled
        away from their spawn: HomeDist=0 was mapped to "unlimited wander"
        (the non-spawn default). Source-X CCSpawn writes the spawner's max
        dist verbatim as the wander leash (CCSpawn.cpp:640); spawn children
        now get a leash of at least 1 tile around the gem.

ADDED - [slow_gump] log: a 0xB1 gump response that holds the receive path
        >=100ms (field: 211ms) now logs its gumpId/button so the offending
        dialog script can be identified.

FIXED - Invisible-door self-heal: the client purges ground items on its own
        (distance culling / resync races) while the server's known-set still
        counts them as delivered — the player then collides with a door they
        cannot see (Britain bank report; the item was server-side, walking
        far and back redrew it). A rejected step now re-sends the dynamic
        items on the forward tile; redrawing an item the client already has
        is a no-op. The client's own 0x22 resync (Ctrl+R) also rebuilds the
        full view.

ADDED - End-to-end gather regression tests: fishing schedules through the
        real client path and delivers the fish at completion; mining's
        pending window must span strokes × DELAY (3.2-9.6s), never the old
        1.6s total. NPCRestock chardef-body loot verified through the full
        dispatcher chain.

[2026-07-16] - Gather-skill stroke timing, skill gain for GMs, spell-memory info, NPC loot
----------------------------------------

ADDED - slow_tick reports now break npc_apply into commit/purge/dirty
        sub-phases with decision and dirty-object counts, so the field
        46-157ms npc_apply spikes can be attributed (decision commit vs
        path purge vs dirty-view marking) instead of guessed at.

FIXED - Spawner NPCs came up with empty backpacks and dropped no loot: the
        pack declares monster gear and backpack loot in ON=@NPCRestock
        blocks (~192 chardefs), but the trigger only fired for vendor-brain
        NPCs. Source-X NPC_LoadScript fires @NPCRestock for EVERY freshly
        created NPC (CCharNPC.cpp:289-290); both the spawner hook and the
        .add pipeline now do the same. The ITEM/ITEMNEWBIE trigger verbs
        (and the top-level chardef key path) now also stamp ATTR_NEWBIE on
        ITEMNEWBIE items so worn gear stays with the owner on death while
        plain ITEM loot drops to the corpse.

FIXED - Fishing/mining/lumberjacking finished 2-6x too fast with a burst of
        cosmetic animations: the skill DELAY curve was treated as the TOTAL
        duration and strokes were animated every DELAY/5 (clamped 0.5-2s).
        Source-X runs strokeCount x DELAY — the stroke count is rolled at
        skill start (fishing 1-2, mining/lumberjacking 2-6) and each stroke
        is one animation+sound a full DELAY apart (Skill_Stroke re-arms with
        SetTimeout(delay)). Non-gather delayed skills no longer repeat
        strokes at all (Source-X routes SKTRIG_STROKE only for CRAFT/GATHER
        skills). Each fishing stroke now also drops the 1s water-splash FX
        item at the cast point, and completion lands together with the final
        stroke so the end of the attempt is unambiguous.

FIXED - Skill gain never happened for GM-level characters (reported as
        "anatomy won't gain"): GainExperience had an invented PrivLevel>=GM
        early-out. Source-X Skill_Experience has no priv gate — PRIV_GM only
        forces the success roll in Skill_CheckSuccess. Also matched the
        failed-use credit: a fail arrives as negative difficulty and clamps
        to the minimum 1 (we used to Abs() it to full credit, wrongly
        passing the GAINRADIUS gate on failures).

FIXED - Double-clicking a spell-effect memory (e.g. the Night Sight rune
        shown by .edit) answered "Object not found": the mirror item lives
        only in ch.Memories with no world UID, and the edit menu routed it
        into a FindObject(0) lookup. The pick now lands in the memory
        readout branch and prints the spell id, strength and caster.

[2026-07-16] - GM pass-through movement follows the ground
----------------------------------------

FIXED - GM/AllMove (and pass-walls) movement stepped on pure delta KEEPING Z
        frozen: a GM entering a dungeon at Z=10 crossed the whole floor at 10
        while the client rendered its own terrain-following Z — invisible
        drift until any self-redraw (dclick facing) snapped the character up.
        Confirmed by the [z_drift] report at 5146,993 (stored 10, floor 1) and
        a real-mul probe (WalkCheck lands at 1 from every neighbor). The
        bypass keeps its cannot-be-blocked property but now seats Z on the
        nearest surface each step.

[2026-07-15] - RESPAWN FULL: incremental, orphan sweep; dungeon Z-drift diagnostic
----------------------------------------

FIXED - RESPAWN FULL froze the main loop for ~47s (4445 spawners reset
        synchronously; the freeze also invited double-issuing the command).
        The reset now runs incrementally (~25ms budget per tick) with an
        in-progress guard and progress/summary logs.

FIXED - RESPAWN FULL left the old broken 1-hp NPCs alive while spawning fresh
        ones: their spawner link (ADDOBJ) was broken, so KillAll never saw
        them. The reset now finishes with an orphan sweep deleting non-owned
        NPCs that carry the Spawned flag/SPAWNITEM tag but belong to no
        spawner's child list (tamed ex-spawns are never swept).

ADDED - [z_drift] diagnostic: the dclick-facing redraw re-imposes the stored
        server Z; when that differs from the map-derived standing Z (the
        "dungeon chest dclick bumps me up" report), the pair is logged to
        locate the drift source.

[2026-07-15] - All target-cursor paths record their session id
----------------------------------------

FIXED - The cursor session guard only knew the ids sent by SetPendingTarget;
        every other cursor path (.info/.kill/teleport/script TARGET — 19 call
        sites) sent an unrecorded random id, so the guard dropped the player's
        legitimate clicks ("target broken", ".kill shows no cursor"). All
        sends now route through a shared SendTargetRequest that records the id.

[2026-07-15] - Cursor echo window, sqlite DQS compatibility, log noise
----------------------------------------

FIXED - First-cast "Targeting cancelled": the replaced cursor's cancel-echo can
        arrive with cursorID 0 (ClassicUO zeroes its stored id after a server
        cancel), slipping past the session-id match and cancelling the fresh
        spell target. One id-less cancel inside a 2s replacement window is now
        swallowed; a real ESC always echoes the matching id and still works.

FIXED - Script DB: classic packs write SQL string literals in double quotes;
        Microsoft.Data.Sqlite's bundled sqlite disables that legacy quirk
        (DQS), so F_RESTYPES_SETUP's INSERTs failed with "no such column:
        C_TROLL". DQS is now enabled on every script DB connection (Source-X's
        sqlite behavior).

CHANGED - [NAME_CHANGE] dropped from Warning to Debug: script @Create renames
        are routine pack behavior and flooded the log during RESPAWN FULL.

[2026-07-15] - Target cursor session guard (first cast mis-target fix)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Casting while another target cursor was still open fired instantly at
        self/the previous target instead of showing the spell cursor: replacing
        an open cursor sends the client a cancel, and the client's cancel-echo
        for the OLD cursor raced the newly armed spell target, consuming or
        cancelling it. Target responses now echo-match the 0x6C request id —
        a response carrying a replaced cursor's id is ignored. The second cast
        always worked because no stale cursor existed by then.

[2026-07-15] - Script engine: assignments inside IF/DORAND/DOSWITCH were dropped
----------------------------------------

FIXED - LOCAL.x= / ARGN / ARGS / REFn= / REFn.prop= / FLOAT.x= assignment lines
        were only handled by the top-level interpreter loop; the IF, DORAND and
        DOSWITCH block executors dispatched their body lines straight to the
        generic verb path, so every such assignment INSIDE an IF block silently
        vanished. Field symptom: F_RESTYPES_SETUP set LOCAL.TABLENAME inside
        IF (<LDB.CONNECTED>) — the CREATE TABLE targeted an empty name, every
        later restypes query failed, and "<EVAL <SERV.RTICKS>-<LOCAL.HOUR>>"
        printed the whole epoch. The handlers are now shared with all block
        executors (regression probe: ScriptLocalScopeProbe).

[2026-07-15] - Character roster snapshot for follower scans
----------------------------------------

CHANGED - GameWorld keeps a char-only mirror of the object table; the
        follower-count recompute now scans ~9K characters instead of copying
        and walking the 100K+ full object array. The [slow_packet] 0x34 lines
        (20-27ms per status request on cache expiry) drop to sub-millisecond.

[2026-07-15] - Static-door auto-close: open-leaf art fix + field diagnostics
----------------------------------------

FIXED - A map-static door whose .mul static is baked as the OPEN leaf
        auto-closed by re-broadcasting its own (open) art — visually never
        closing. The sweep now derives the closed art through the same
        GetDoorDir slot math the manual toggle uses (open leaf → tile-1).
        Sweep logic extracted to StaticDoorSweeper (unit-tested end to end).

ADDED - [static_door] log lines on open/manual close and on every auto-close
        sweep pass (with a dropped-no-static counter): an "opened" with no
        auto-close within ~21s pinpoints a dead sweep; an auto-close logged
        while the door still looks open pinpoints a stale client ghost.

[2026-07-15] - Invented-values audit, wave 5: craft quality, Blood Oath, throwing
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Crafted item quality ported to the Source-X Skill_MakeItem band table
        (CCharSkill.cpp:724-794): skill picks a band (shoddy..superior), a
        logarithmic ±0-2 band variance shifts it, the value rolls inside the
        band. The invented linear 100+excess/10 curve, the "exceptional"
        rename at 150+ and its +20% durability boost are gone; the reference
        grandmaster maker's-mark (skill > 99.9 and quality > 175) remains.

FIXED - Blood Oath reflect level now the exact Source-X formula on the layer
        owner (caster): MagicResistance*10/20 + 10, unclamped
        (CCharSpell.cpp:1313) — was an invented /20+10 clamped 10-90 computed
        from the enemy's skill.

FIXED - NPC rock-throwing stamina cost 4+rand(6) (CCharSkill.cpp:3372); the
        Dex/4 damage roll was verified as reference (CCharSkill.cpp:3447).

NOTES - Verified as genuine Source-X (citations added, no change): the entire
        NPC hostility coefficient set (51/100/-50/kin softenings/+50 grudge,
        NPC_GetHostilityLevelToward), SpiritSpeak 24s (4*60 tenths). Deferred:
