[2026-07-03] - Death/corpse waves D1-D2: death penalties, carve crime, death-screen config
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Player death penalties (Source-X CChar::Death):
  - A dying player loses a tenth of their experience (min 1) and a tenth
    of their fame (suppressed by DEATHFLAGS & DEATH_NOFAMECHANGE); the
    deaths counter increments. The fame loss runs through @FameChange.

FIXED - Death-time state cleanup:
  - Kill() now clears Hidden/Invisible/Freeze/Stone/Sleeping/Hovering
    (Source-X Reveal + StatFlag_Clear) — a character that died while
    hidden previously stayed an unseen ghost.
  - The victim's FIGHT/HARMEDBY memories are cleared at death.

ADDED - Corpse carving rules:
  - Carving an innocent player's corpse now flags the carver criminal,
    like looting it (Source-X CheckCorpseCrime with fLooting=false).
  - Corpses of bonded pets, summoned creatures and sleeping bodies are
    born uncarvable (Source-X m_carved = 1).

ADDED - sphere.ini HitpointPercentOnRez (Source-X default 10):
  - The resurrection HP percent is configurable; it was a hardcoded 50%.
    Shards that want the old behavior set HitpointPercentOnRez=50.

ADDED - sphere.ini PacketDeathAnimation (Source-X default 1):
  - When 0, the 0x2C death-screen packet is not sent, so ClassicUO never
    enters its 1.5-second death-screen render freeze; the ghost redraw
    sequence carries the full transition (the reference addPlayerUpdate
    fallback).

FIXED - Open secure trades survive a participant's death:
  - The dying side's trade is cancelled before the corpse forms: items
    return to the packs (and so reach the corpse loot), both windows
    close and @TradeClose fires. A clientless victim takes a packetless
    fallback path.

NOTE - @CreateLoot stays a spawn-time trigger in SphereNet (deliberate
  divergence): death-time ITEM= materialisation is covered by the
  existing deferred-loot drop, and firing the script again at death
  would double the loot.

[2026-07-03] - NPC AI wave N1: dormant NPC_AI flags, trigger contracts, CAN-flag hex fix
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Dormant NPC_AI_* flag behaviors:
  - NPC_AI_FOOD now routes through the feeding pass (previously only
    INTFOOD did); the basic/intelligent distinction is collapsed into the
    one implementation.
  - NPC_AI_COMBAT gates the ally heal/cure targeting: without it the
    Source-X friend list is self-only, so group support no longer runs
    unconditionally. Self-heal stays ungated.
  - NPC_AI_EXTRA (NPC_ExtraAI): humanoid-brain NPCs fire @NPCAction
    (RETURN 1 skips the pass), equip a weapon and shield from the pack in
    war mode, and carry a hand light by night / stow it by day. Lighting
    the torch (IT_LIGHT_OUT -> LIT) stays deferred.
  - NPC_AI_MOVEOBSTACLES: a hands-capable, smart-enough NPC shifts a
    movable blocking item onto its own tile before giving up the path.
  - NPC_AI_VEND_TIME stays deferred: it is define-only in Source-X too.

CHANGED - NPC trigger contracts:
  - @NPCActCast now carries ARGN2 = wand-use (the documented Source-X
    contract; upstream's own value is always 0 due to an early reset).
  - @NPCLookAtItem matches Source-X: ARGN1 = distance, ARGN2 = want-score
    (writable, read back), ARGO = the item; RETURN 1 takes the item over,
    RETURN 0 ignores it; move-never/locked/secure items never fire it.
  - NPC wands require ATTR_MAGIC (Source-X NPC_FightMagery); a wand with
    no CHARGES tag stays infinite for legacy-import compatibility.

FIXED - CHARDEF CAN flags parsed leading-zero values as decimal:
  - Sphere's numeric convention treats a leading zero as hex, so a legacy
    chardef's CAN=0300 (mt_equip|mt_usehands) resolved to decimal 300 and
    mis-flagged every imported chardef. The item-side parsers already
    followed the convention; the chardef CAN parser now does too.

ADDED - @Hit LOCAL.Arrow (hit-path ammo takeover):

    a ranged hit (previously miss-only); LOCAL.ArrowHandled=1 hands the
    ammo to the script — the engine neither consumes the stack nor runs
    the 40% stick-in-body economy then, matching Source-X's nulled pAmmo.

  - Spell damage now applies the slayer scaling with the equipped

    inside the shared scaler), mirroring the Source-X DAMAGE_MAGIC branch.

ADDED - Hit-area splash sparkle:
  - Each splashed victim shows the Source-X sparkle effect (0x3779) in
    addition to the per-element epicenter sound.

[2026-07-03] - Combat parity wave C5: AOS on-hit properties
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Life/mana/stam leech and mana drain (Source-X Fight_Hit formulas):
  - HITLEECHLIFE heals rand(0 .. dmg x prop x 30/10000), HITLEECHMANA the
    x40 window, HITLEECHSTAM restores the full damage prop% of the time,
    HITMANADRAIN transfers 20% of the damage from the victim's mana
    (clamped) prop% of the time. Any leech plays the 0x44D sound.

ADDED - On-hit spell procs (weapon required, like Source-X):
  - HITDISPEL/HITFIREBALL/HITHARM/HITLIGHTNING/HITMAGICARROW apply the
    spell's effect directly on the victim at the attacker's Magery — no
    cast time, mana or reagents (SpellEngine.ApplyOnHitSpell).

ADDED - Hit-area splashes:
  - HITAREAPHYSICAL always, the FIRE/COLD/POISON/ENERGY variants only
    under COMBAT_ELEMENTAL_ENGINE: half the damage splashes the chars
    within 5 tiles of the victim through their own resists, skipping the
    two principals, the attacker's pets and the dead, with the
    per-element impact sound at the epicenter.

ADDED - Property surface:
  - The 14 property names are tag-backed on chars and items and accepted
    as CHARDEF/ITEMDEF lines (def-tag flow). The effective value sums the
    attacker's own tag with the weapon's and equipped talisman's
    (instance tag first, ITEMDEF def-tag fallback).
  - HitLowerAtk/Def, HitCurse and HitFatigue stay deferred — they are
    unimplemented in Source-X as well.

[2026-07-03] - Combat parity waves C1-C4: @GetHit contract, trigger locals, flags, Slayer
----------------------------------------

CHANGED - @GetHit armor-damage contract (wave C1):
  - The on-hit trigger pipeline moved into TriggerDispatcher.RunHitDamageTriggers
    with a HitDamageContext. @GetHit now seeds LOCAL.ItemDamageLayer (random
    pick from the Source-X sm_ArmorDamageLayers set) and LOCAL.ItemDamageChance;
    the item @GetHit fires on the worn piece at the script-final layer instead
    of only a TwoHanded shield.
  - Armor durability wear rolls ItemDamageChance after the trigger chain in
    BOTH armor modes (elemental combat previously never wore armor); a
    RETURN 1 cancel skips the wear roll.

FIXED - Elemental damage split (wave C1):
  - Removed the forced 1-damage floor: a fully-resisted elemental hit now
    deals 0, like Source-X.
  - An unset physical percent defaults to the remainder the elemental
    percents leave of 100, applied consistently at spawn def-apply time.

ADDED - Trigger local contracts (wave C2):
  - @HitCheck fires before the swing range/LoS validation (Source-X order)
    and seeds LOCAL.Recoil_NoRange; the read-back drives the per-swing
    range-ignore decision and the windup window.
  - @HitMiss LOCAL.Arrow carries the live pack ammo stack UID; ammo
    consumption moved to outcome resolution so LOCAL.ArrowHandled or
    RETURN 1 hands the ammo's fate to the script.
  - @Hit seeds LOCAL.ItemDamageChance and ItemPoisonReductionChance/Amount
    (shared with the weapon item @Hit); the read-backs gate the weapon
    durability wear and the poison charge spend.

ADDED - Dormant combat flag behaviors (wave C3):
  - COMBAT_ALLOWHITFROMSHIP: combat across a ship region boundary is blocked
    unless the flag is set; same-ship combat stays allowed.
  - COMBAT_DCLICKSELF_UNMOUNTS: a mounted char in war mode with an active
    fight opens the paperdoll on self-dclick instead of dismounting, unless
    the flag opts into the unmount.
  - COMBAT_NOPETDESERT: attacking your own pet makes it desert (cancellable
    via @PetDesert) unless the flag allows friendly fire.
  - COMBAT_ATTACK_NOAGGREIVED: skips the criminal marking when starting a
    fight against an innocent, on the melee and harmful-spell paths.
  - Config load normalizes COMBAT_PREHIT|COMBAT_SWING_NORANGE by clearing
    SWING_NORANGE with a warning (Source-X RC_COMBATFLAGS).

ADDED - Slayer system (COMBAT_SLAYER, wave C4):
  - SlayerFaction is a verbatim CFactionDef port: faction groups, the
    opposite/super/lesser matching tables and the damage constants (lesser
    +200%, super +100%, opposite-group penalty -100%), quirks included so
    script data behaves identically to Source-X.
  - Script surface matches Source-X: FACTION_GROUP/FACTION_SPECIES on
    chardefs and chars, SLAYER_GROUP/SLAYER_SPECIES on itemdefs and items
    (def-tag flow to spawns, tag-backed persistence).
  - ResolveAttack scales the settled damage under COMBAT_SLAYER: weapon
    slayer first, the equipped talisman as fallback; NPC victims take the
    bonus, a player victim takes the Source-X opposite-group penalty from
    an NPC's super slayer. The magic-damage/spellbook path is deferred.

[2026-07-02] - Smoke test fixes: web status deadlock, CWD path resolution, T2A map bound
----------------------------------------
A headless boot smoke test with the real mortechUO script pack (554 .scp)
and UOP maps: 32845 itemdefs / 822 chardefs / 168 spells / 1645 recipes /
1271 teleporters loaded; telnet console (status/save/garbage/account add),
an account save-restart-load round trip and the web status endpoint were
exercised. Three real bugs found and fixed:

FIXED - The web status endpoint never answered (requests timed out):
  - WebStatusServer.Tick started a NEW BeginGetContext every tick; the
    previous pending accepts were abandoned and an arriving request was
    consumed by an accept nobody reaped (plus a per-tick async-op pileup).
    A single pending accept now survives across ticks.

FIXED - Relative save/accounts paths always resolved to the exe directory:
  - ResolvePath now applies the same CWD-first rule as FindConfigFile/
    FindDir: a relative path existing in the working directory wins, else
    it falls back to the exe directory. A server run from a data directory
    now writes its saves there.

FIXED - MAP0/MAP1 default 6144 -> 7168 (config/sphere.ini):
  - Width 6144 left the T2A/Lost Lands area (x>6144) outside the world;
    mortechUO teleport defs use x 6992-7153 and 10 Lost Lands teleporters
    failed to place. The UOP map0 file carries 7168.

ADDED - Item verbs SMELT and CARVECORPSE (Source-X CIV_*):

  - CARVECORPSE carves the corpse as SRC (meat/hides/feathers, the

[2026-07-02] - Parity wave W-H10: bulletin boards (IT_BBOARD) end to end
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Bulletin boards (Source-X addBulletinBoard/CItemMessage):
  - Dclicking a board sends 0x71 sub 0 (board name) plus the message items
    as container contents; the client then requests each header itself.
  - Posting (sub 5) creates a real message item inside the board (Name =
    subject, LINK = author, AUTHOR/TIME/BODY_n tags) — persists with saves.
    Past 32 messages the oldest rolls off; a reach check applies.
  - A header request (sub 3) answers with the sub 1 summary, a full read
    (sub 4) with the sub 2 body (author/subject/date + lines).
  - Deletion (sub 6) is restricted to the author or a GM.

FIXED - The 0x71 sub 3 parse DROPPED the message uid:
  - Source-X BBOARDF_REQ_HEAD carries the message uid; the handler chain
    (NetState/NetworkManager/Program) was renamed to RequestHead(board,msg).

[2026-07-02] - Parity wave W-H9: map display (IT_MAP), pin protocol, ISMYPET
----------------------------------------

ADDED - IT_MAP display (Source-X CClient::addDrawMap):
  - Dclicking a map now sends the 0x90 map gump with its world-coordinate
    bounds (MORE1 = top/left, MORE2 = bottom/right words) and replays the
    stored pins one by one via 0x56 — treasure maps render.
  - A blank map (t_map_blank or an invalid rect) only reports blank.

FIXED - 0x56 pin-edit commands realigned to Source-X MAPCMD:
  - The old mapping was wrong (assumed 6=insert, 7=move). Correct: 1 add
    (append), 2 insert, 3 move, 4 delete (tail shifts), 5 clear all,
    6 toggle plot mode — the server replies mode 7 with the new state.
  - Pins live as 1-based PIN_n tags (same surface as the script PIN.n).

ADDED - <ISMYPET> (Source-X CHC_ISMYPET):
  - Resolves in the interpreter against SRC: 1 when the target char is
    SRC's pet. An OWNER/NPCMASTER property read (owner uid) was added too.

ADDED - IT_SPAWN_CHAMPION (Source-X CCSpawn champion special case):
  - Champion spawners ignore the amount cap and never pause their timer —
    the wave keeps coming. TYPE=t_spawn_champion is recognized at runtime too.

ADDED - NPCs turn to face whoever addresses them (Source-X NPC_OnHear):

  - By number or spell name; answers mana, primary-skill requirement and
    region anti-magic checks through the engine hook.

ADDED - Dclicking a marked recall rune reports its destination:
  - Sextant coordinates in the "rune name: 40° 12'N, 12° 5'E" form; a blank
    rune keeps the old name hint.

[2026-07-02] - Parity waves W-A..W-G: Source-X behavior surface alignment
----------------------------------------

The first seven waves of the category-by-category Source-X audit
(wiki/hedef.txt) were applied in one pass. Test suite grew 1040 -> 1076
(all green, ParityWaveA-G guardrail suites). Highlights:

FIXED - Trigger contracts:
  - Trigger names aligned with the Source-X tables: @Jailed, @Ship_Move/
    _Stop/_Turn, @itemSPELL (scripts using the reference names never fired).
  - @Hit/@HitTry/@HitCheck/@HitMiss: SRC=victim, ARGO=weapon; damage-type
    ARGN2 on @Hit/@GetHit/@HitCheck; @HitCheck ARGN1=swing state.
  - @Death SRC=the dying char (killer on ARGO), @Kill ARGN1=attacker count,
    item @Step ARGN1=standing flag.
  - @SpellEffect fires on the AFFECTED char (SRC=caster, ARGN2=skill level,
    writable LOCAL.Effect/Resist/Duration, RETURN 1 cancels per target);
    @SpellCast seeds ARGN2=difficulty + writable ARGN3 cast time.
  - [SKILL n] section stages (ON=@Start/@Stroke/...) execute for the first time.

FIXED - Combat core:
  - Players now gain weapon skill + Tactics from combat (never gained before).
  - Era-0 hit roll is the two-stage model: random difficulty 0..iDiff checked
    against the weapon-skill bell curve; frozen targets are near-certain hits.
  - Coverage-weighted whole-body AR replaces the single-region reduction;
    legacy parry formula (shield/40, DEX<80 erosion, GM +5, trains Parrying).
  - IT_TRAP dclick SPRINGS the trap (full Use_Trap state machine); equipped
    cursed items refuse to move; paralyze breaks on damage; Dispel strips
    active buffs/curses.

FIXED - Notoriety follows the Source-X decision order:
  - Party/guild resolve BEFORE criminal/murderer (a party-member murderer
    renders green); TAG.OVERRIDE.NOTO honored; PLAYEREVIL/PLAYERNEUTRAL
    karma thresholds added (sphere.ini); murderers see themselves red; your
    own pet renders neutral (the Source-X default).

ADDED - NPC AI / economy / social:
  - NPC hostility: karma alignment + CREID ally-group families (orcs no
    longer attack orc mages) + fight-memory grudges.
  - The vendor purse is always tracked (restock funds it, partial sell fill
    with a shortfall bark); VENDORMARKUP drives the sell payout.
  - Guild stone gump: dismiss member, declare/break alliance, set name/
    abbreviation, fealty vote. Party member health bars update beyond
    visual range.
  - Region names are announced only in ANNOUNCE-flagged regions.

ADDED - Housing/ships/persistence:
  - House placement generates a pack key + bank spare; lockdown/secure stamp
    the item ATTR; redeed sweeps loose floor items into the moving crate.
  - Ship planks open/close (5s autoclose); ships collide with statics and
    other hulls.
  - Sector environment (light/season/weather), ALL memory types (with
    remaining timeouts) and the attacker log survive save-load.
  - SERV.B / SERV.GARBAGE / SERV.INFORMATION bridged to scripts; DISTANCE,
    HITPOINTS/USESCUR aliases, item CONSUME/BOUNCE/DECAY verbs.

[2026-07-01] - World-ops parity: RESTORE rollback hardening (Wave 217)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - SERV.RESTORE no longer silently loses the old object on load failure:
  - RESTORE takes a temporary rollback .scp snapshot through WorldSaver.ExportObjects
    before deleting colliding serials.
  - If loading the restore file throws after those objects were removed, possible
    partial new records from the restore file are cleaned up and the backup snapshot
    is loaded through the normal LoadFile path.
  - Rollback behavior is covered by a test that corrupts the restore file after the
    backup is taken.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - World-ops parity: scoped IMPORT (Wave 216)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - SERV.IMPORT now has the matching flag/distance filter:
  - SERV.IMPORT supports `IMPORT file, flags, distance`. The command target is
    used as the center; flags are interpreted as 1=items, 2=chars, 3=both.
  - Scoped import reduces the source file to a temporary filtered text .scp and
    then reuses the existing LoadFile path, preserving duplicate-serial,
    container/equipment relink and SPELLEFFECT restore behavior.
  - Items under selected containers/chars are imported with their parent chain.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - World-ops parity: scoped EXPORT / SAVESTATICS (Wave 215)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Source-X-style distance/flag export slice:
  - SERV.EXPORT now supports `EXPORT file, flags, distance`. The script SRC
    object is used as the center; flags are interpreted as 1=items, 2=chars,
    3=both.
  - Scoped export preserves the normal world-save filters: static items stay out
    of dynamic export and vendor stock is still excluded. Items under selected
    containers/chars are written with the selected root so CONT links stay valid
    on import.
  - WorldSaver.ExportStatics can use the same scope filter; argument-less
    SERV.SAVESTATICS now writes WorldSaveDir/spherestatics.scp.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - World-ops parity: RESTORE replaces colliding serials (Wave 214)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - SERV.RESTORE is no longer a LOAD/IMPORT alias:
  - WorldLoader.RestoreFile pre-scans WORLDITEM/WORLDCHAR SERIAL records and
    removes currently registered world objects with those serials before loading
    the file back in.
  - SERV.LOAD / SERV.IMPORT remain non-destructive; duplicate serials keep the
    existing object and skip the imported record. The script bridge now routes
    RESTORE through a separate _RESTORE channel.
  - World-ops restore behavior is covered by a test that locks the duplicate
    LOAD versus destructive RESTORE distinction.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - World-ops parity: SERV.EXPORT / LOAD first slice (Wave 213)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Safe first slice of the Source-X world-ops long tail:
  - SERV.EXPORT can now write one object, or WORLD/ALL for the dynamic world, as
    classic text .scp records under WorldSaveDir. Export intentionally uses
    script-compatible text even when normal saves use binary/gzip.
  - SERV.LOAD / SERV.IMPORT / SERV.RESTORE load one .scp/save-format file at
    runtime with two-pass item/char parsing; container/equipment links are resolved
    after load. RESTORE is a non-destructive import alias in this slice; destructive
    replace semantics stay deferred for a data-integrity-focused slice.
  - SERV.SAVESTATICS exports ATTR_STATIC items to a text .scp file.
  - Paths are jailed under WorldSaveDir; absolute paths, "..", and drive prefixes
    are rejected.

[2026-07-01] - Persistence parity: spawn/restock timer audit (Wave 212)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Spawn and vendor restock timings could drift across restart:
  - IT_SPAWN_CHAR component initialization no longer overwrites a loaded TIMERMS
    remaining-time value; the saved spawn timer is rebound to the same target tick.
  - IT_SPAWN_ITEM now mirrors its next spawn time to the object Timeout, so WorldSaver
    can write it as TIMERMS and component init can preserve the same remaining-time
    pattern after load.
  - Vendor RESTOCK_TIME is now written as UTC Unix milliseconds instead of process-local
    TickCount64, matching TradeEngine and staying meaningful across save-load.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Persistence parity: active spell effects survive save-load (Wave 211)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - An active buff/debuff could become a permanent stat exploit after restart:
  - Timed spell effects such as Bless/Curse/Strength/Weaken are now written to the
    world save as remaining-time SPELLEFFECT records. The save keeps base stats clean;
    after load, SpellEngine restores the effect, reapplies live stat/flag/visual state,
    and lets the effect expire normally.
  - Incognito/Polymorph/NightSight state reverted for save is now fully re-applied
    after save, and the reapply path runs from finally even when saving fails.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Network: server-initiated RTT ping disabled by default (Wave 210)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - The client ping meter showed absurd values (hundreds of thousands of ms):
  - The server sent an unsolicited 0x73 ping to each client every 30s to measure its
    own RTT. The stock ClassicUO client feeds EVERY incoming 0x73 into its own ping
    average (Time.Ticks minus a baseline that only advances when the client itself sends
    a ping), so the server's pings made the client display its own uptime as "ping" —
    an average in the 500k ms range with spikes to millions, dropping to the real 8-12ms
    only in the instant after the client sent its own ping. The server-side RttMs value
    was never consumed anywhere. The feature now ships disabled (RttPingIntervalMs=0);
    the client's own ping still works (the server echoes client-initiated pings). Set
    RttPingIntervalMs to a positive value only with a client that ignores unsolicited
    pings. NOTE: if RttPingIntervalMs is set in your .ini, change it to 0 there too.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Persistence parity: active poison survives save-load (Wave 209)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - An active poison was lost on save-load:
  - A poisoned character's level, remaining ticks, next-tick schedule and poisoner were
    never written to the world save, so the poison silently ended on restart (and a
    poison kill lost its attribution). The poison is now saved as remaining time + tick
    count (like item decay / TIMERF) and restored exactly on load via a new
    CharacterPoisonState.Restore, so it resumes rather than re-arming fresh.

KNOWN - Active spell buffs/debuffs still become permanent across a restart:
  - Stat effects (Bless/Curse/Strength/Weaken/...) modify the character stat directly
    and are runtime-only, so save-load keeps the buffed stat but drops the expiration —
    the buff never wears off after a restart. Fixing this needs a design decision
    (persist the effect list so it expires, or revert effects at save so base stats are
    stored); tracked in PARITY_MATRIX.md rather than rushed here.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Persistence parity: TIMERF timers survive save-load (Wave 208)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - A pending TIMERF / TIMERFMS timer was lost on save-load:
  - Per-object delayed function/verb timers (AddTimerF) were never written to the world
    save, so a scheduled delayed action was dropped when the server restarted — unlike
    Source-X, which keeps object timers across a save. Each pending entry is now saved
    per object as remaining time (not the absolute tick, which resets on restart) and
    re-scheduled on load, mirroring how item decay/TIMERMS already persist. The saver
    emits one TIMERF property per entry (remainingMs|function|args); the loader routes
    it through TrySetProperty, which re-adds the timer with the remaining delay.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Scripting parity: SERV.VARLIST / PRINTLISTS write to the caller (Wave 207)
----------------------------------------

CHANGED - SERV.VARLIST and SERV.PRINTLISTS now output to the invoking client:
  - As commands they carry the caller's UID through the script bridge (like
    SERV.ALLCLIENTS / SERV.GMPAGE), so the server dumps the global VAR / list contents
    to that GM's console instead of only the server log (the Wave-197 deferred half). A
    log fallback is kept when there is no online caller, and the <...> read form still
    returns the count. The VAR enumeration was factored into a shared sink so the log
    and console paths share one implementation.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Speech parity: @Speech text rewrite wired end-to-end (Wave 206)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - A player's @Speech trigger can now rewrite the spoken text:
  - The ARGS-mutation mechanism (Wave 204) is now carried through the speech path. The
    speaker's @Speech self-trigger runs with the utterance as ARGS; if the script
    rewrites it (ARGS=<new text>), the rewritten words are read back and become what
    the NPC-hear routing, guild/alliance routing and the spatial broadcast all use —
    matching Source-X, where @Speech can reshape the line. RETURN 1 still cancels the
    whole utterance. FireSpeechSelfTrigger gained an overload that returns the rewritten
    text; OnPlayerSpeech now returns (Cancel, Text) and ProcessSpeech an out finalText;
    a ghost's garbled speech is left untouched by the rewrite.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Scripting parity: RETURN preserves string values (Wave 205)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - RETURN coerced string values to a number:
  - Both RETURN handlers evaluated the argument as a long and stored that number, so a
    [FUNCTION] returning a name, defname or message (RETURN of a resolved string)
    collapsed to a digit instead of its text. The expression evaluator only returned a
    long with no way to signal "this was not numeric", so the two cases were
    indistinguishable.
  - Added ExpressionParser.TryEvaluate, which reports whether the whole expression was a
    genuine numeric value — it clears an internal flag when an atom resolves to a
    non-numeric string (an unresolved bareword, or a <...> that expanded to text) or
    when content is left unparsed. RETURN now keeps the string when the arg is not
    numeric, and still evaluates numbers, hex and expressions. Plain Evaluate is
    untouched, so no numeric path changes.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Trigger parity: ARGS string mutation (Wave 204)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Scripts could not rewrite a trigger's string argument (ARGS):
  - <ARGS> was seeded and readable, but a line like ARGS=<new text> fell through to a
    no-op (the interpreter had no ARGS assignment path) and RunWrapped never copied the
    string back, so trigger text was read-only. ARGS assignment now writes the trigger
    arg and the rewrite is copied back to the caller — the mechanism a script needs to
    reshape trigger text (Source-X @Speech-style rewrite). FireResourceTrigger and
    FireSpellTrigger, which duplicated the ARGN copy-back inline, now share RunWrapped
    so they pick up the ARGS write-back too.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Trigger parity: ARGN write-back from every trigger source (Wave 203)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - ARGN mutations were dropped from most trigger sources:
  - Only object EVENTS lists and character def triggers ran through RunWrapped, the
    method that copies a script's ARGN1/2/3 changes back into the caller's args. Item
    ITEMDEF / TEVENTS / TYPEDEF triggers (where most item behaviour lives), region and
    room events, and all global (EVENTSPLAYER / EVENTSPET / EVENTSITEM / EVENTSREGION)
    events called the runner directly and discarded the mutations — so an item @DClick
    that set ARGN1, or a global event adjusting a trigger number, had no effect on the
    caller. Every trigger firing path now goes through RunWrapped, so ARGN write-back is
    uniform regardless of where the trigger is defined.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Trigger parity: ARGN3 seeding and ARGN mutation (Wave 202)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - <ARGN3> read 0 inside every trigger:
  - TriggerDispatcher.WrapArgs built the script args with only ARGN1/ARGN2 (the
    constructor's two number slots) and never seeded Number3, so a trigger fired with
    N3 set — e.g. @DropOn_* passing the drop Z, @SkillUseQuick passing the result —
    saw <ARGN3> as 0. WrapArgs now seeds Number3 as well.

FIXED - Scripts could not modify ARGN1/ARGN2/ARGN3:
  - The interpreter had no assignment path for ARGN, so a line like ARGN3=99 fell
    through to a no-op property-set — trigger numbers were effectively read-only,
    defeating the RunWrapped copy-back for script-driven changes (Source-X @Hit damage,
    @DropOn drop-Z, @NPCActFight dist/motivation). ARGN1/ARGN2/ARGN3 (and bare ARGN =
    ARGN1) assignment now writes the trigger args, and the value is copied back to the
    caller after the block.

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Scripting parity: TRYSRV runs at server privilege (Wave 201)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - TRYSRV did not elevate to server privilege:
  - TRYSRV is meant to run a verb as the server (Source-X g_Serv, PLEVEL 7) so it
    bypasses the calling source's privilege restriction, but it passed the original
    source through — a low-plevel player, or a Guest-level null console — so a
    privileged verb under TRYSRV still failed the very check it exists to bypass. It
    now runs the verb under a server (Owner) source; the original source's script
    bridge stays as the fallback so client-scoped verbs still reach a client.

ADDED - TRY-family coverage: tests pin TRYSRV's server elevation and TRYP's
  privilege gate (verb blocked below the required PrivLevel, allowed at or above).

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Scripting parity: SERV.ACCOUNT.n indexed access (Wave 200)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - SERV.ACCOUNT.<n> (indexed account access) was stubbed to return "0":
  - Source-X admin dialogs iterate SERV.ACCOUNT.0 .. SERV.ACCOUNT.<count-1> to list
    accounts, but the index path always returned "0". It now resolves the n-th account
    via the new AccountManager.GetByIndex, which orders by name so the index is stable
    across reads (a raw dictionary enumeration is not). SERV.ACCOUNT.<key>.<prop> also
    works now for both names and indices (e.g. SERV.ACCOUNT.0.PLEVEL), reading the
    property off the resolved account; an out-of-range index still yields "0".

================================================================================

[2026-07-01] - Scripting parity: script <LINK> reads the object's own link (Wave 199)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - <LINK> in scripts was aliased to the ACT object instead of the object's link:
  - The interpreter resolved both <ACT> and <LINK> to the trigger's second object
    (Object2), so <LINK> never reflected an object's actual m_uidLink — e.g. a lever's
    linked door was unreachable from <LINK> / <LINK.NAME>. <LINK> (and <LINK.prop>) now
    delegate to the current object's LINK property, which already resolves the linked
    object and its sub-properties for both items and characters. <ACT> still resolves
    Object2, so the two references are now independent (VarObjs chain consistency).

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Scripting parity: TIMERFMS and delayed-verb timers (Wave 198)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - TIMERFMS object verb (Source-X millisecond timer):
  - TIMERFMS <ms>, <payload> schedules a delayed function/verb on an object in
    milliseconds, the counterpart of TIMERF's seconds (which was the only unit
    supported). Both now share one parser (ObjBase.ScheduleTimerF) that differs only
    in the delay multiplier.

FIXED - A delayed TIMERF payload that was not a [FUNCTION] silently did nothing:
  - The timer executor only tried the payload as a script function, so a bare verb
    such as TIMERF 5, SAY hi or TIMERF 10, REMOVE never ran. It now falls back to
    executing the payload as a command on the object when no matching function
    exists, matching Source-X TIMERF (delayed verb OR function).

[2026-06-30] - Parity backbone: SERV.* world-ops verbs and parity matrix (Wave 197)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Parity matrix measurement backbone (roadmap Faz 0):
  - docs/PARITY_MATRIX.md itemises the Source-X SERV.* verb surface with a status
    (Implemented / Partial / Stub / Missing / NotApplicable) and code location for
    each, turning the subjective category scores into a concrete, regression-guarded
    checklist. Points at the existing trigger guardrail for the trigger surface.

ADDED - Script-reachable SERV.* world-ops verbs (Source-X parity):
  - SERV.RESPAWN and SERV.RESTOCK now run from scripts (they delegate to the same
    engine actions the admin console fires; previously console-only).
  - SERV.CLEARLISTS drops all global script lists (optional name prefix) and returns
    the count — the list counterpart of SERV.CLEARVARS, backed by the new
    GameWorld.ClearGlobalLists primitive (the var store had a clear, the list store
    did not). SERV.VARLIST / SERV.PRINTLISTS dump the global var/list contents to the
    server log (caller-console routing deferred).

[2026-06-30] - Death parity: gender-specific player death cry (Wave 196)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Every player death played one fixed sound:
  - A dying player always emitted sound 0x01FE regardless of gender. ServUO/Source-X
    Mobile.GetDeathSound for a human body returns a random gender-specific death cry —
    female Random(0x314, 4) (0x314..0x317), male Random(0x423, 5) (0x423..0x427). The
    death path now picks the correct cry (gender captured before the ghost-body swap,
    since IsFemale reads the live body). DeathEngine.GetHumanDeathSound centralises it.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Vendor parity: refuse to buy a non-empty container or immovable item (Wave 195)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Selling a non-empty container to a vendor destroyed its contents:
  - VendorEngine.ProcessSell validated amount, gold and the optional buy-list filter
    but not the item itself, so a vendor with no buy list (buys anything) would accept
    a bag and Delete() it — silently eating every item inside for the bag's sell price
    (an item-loss exploit). The sell path now refuses an immovable item (Move_Never)
    and any container that still holds items, mirroring ServUO BaseVendor's sell guard
    (skip !Movable and a Container with Items.Count != 0). An empty container stays
    sellable.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Notoriety parity: criminal flag on attacking an innocent is region-independent (Wave 194)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Attacking an innocent only flagged the attacker criminal inside a guarded region:
  - A melee attack on an innocent (NOTO_GOOD from the attacker's view) set the criminal
    flag only when the attacker stood in a guarded region, so attacking a blue player in
    the open left the aggressor blue. ServUO Mobile.CriminalAction sets Criminal = true
    unconditionally — only the guard RESPONSE (Region.OnCriminalAction) is gated on a
    guarded region — and the harmful-spell path here already flagged everywhere. The
    melee path now matches: an innocent attack flags the attacker grey regardless of
    region, with guard summoning still limited to guarded zones elsewhere.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Speech parity: per-recipient ghost speech garbling (Wave 193)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - A dead player's speech was garbled identically for every listener:
  - A ghost's words were replaced once with a fixed "OooOoo" and broadcast that way
    to everyone in range — including other ghosts, staff and the speaker. Source-X
    (ServUO Mobile.MutateSpeech / CheckHearsMutatedSpeech) garbles per listener: the
    speaker, other ghosts and staff read the clear words, while each living listener
    who cannot hear the dead sees an independently-scrambled o/O string (spaces kept,
    length preserved). Delivery now runs through ForEachClientInRange for a dead
    speaker, choosing clear vs garbled per recipient (GhostSpeech.HearsGhostClearly).
    The NPC/guild routing copy stays garbled, so NPCs still ignore a ghost's words.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Macro/message parity: macro engine tests, name macro tags (Wave 192)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - <CNAME> and <NAME_TITLE> message macros (Source-X name variants):
  - DEFMSG / speech templates may now use <CNAME> (the speaker's name with a
    capitalised first letter) and <NAME_TITLE> (the name prefixed with its title,
    e.g. "Lord Yunus"; falls back to the bare name when no title is supplied)
    alongside the existing <NAME> and <SEX a/b>. MessageMacros.Context gained an
    optional Title. The bare <NAME> pattern still cannot collide with the variants.

TESTS - Macro record/playback engine coverage (was zero):
  - The macro engine's deterministic control flow is now under test: capture step
    cap, target self/object/location classification, record↔playback mutual
    exclusivity, empty-recording discard, stop-on-missing-client during Tick (driven
    by an injected nowMs and getClient), and disconnect cleanup. No behaviour change.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Party parity: decline notification, corpse-loot flag fix (Wave 191)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Party decline (0xBF 0x06 sub 0x09) sent a null packet to the inviter:
  - Declining an invitation invoked the inviter's send path with a null packet
    (null!) — a latent NullReferenceException in the send pipeline. The inviter now
    receives the proper notification ("<name>: Does not wish to join the party.",
    party_decline_1) as a system message.

FIXED - Corpse-loot crime checked the wrong party member's loot flag:
  - Looting a party member's corpse consulted the LOOTER's loot flag instead of the
    corpse OWNER's. The flag means "the party may loot ME", so it belongs to the
    owner: as written, a looter who enabled their own flag could freely loot every
    party member's corpse without criminal penalty. The check now reads the owner's
    flag (DeathEngine.IsLootingCriminal).

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Guild parity: alliance declaration verbs, overhead abbreviation (Wave 190)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Alliance declaration verbs on guild/town stones (symmetric to the war set):
  - DECLAREALLY <stone> records our side of an alliance; INVITEALLY <stone>, <who>
    records the other side's accept (who = 1 we / 0 they), mirroring INVITEWAR; the
    alliance only goes active once both sides have declared (IsAlly). DECLAREUNALLY
    <stone> withdraws our declaration (mirror of DECLAREPEACE). Previously the
    underlying AddAlly/RemoveAlly were only reachable from save-load, so alliances
    could not be formed at runtime from a guild stone script.

ADDED - Guild abbreviation on the overhead name:
  - A guilded player's single-click overhead label now carries the guild abbreviation
    (e.g. "Lord Yunus [TO]") when the guild has one and the member keeps it visible
    (TOGGLEABBREVIATION). The suffix is computed on-demand per click (not in the delta-
    tracked name path) and is suppressed for unguilded characters, hidden members and
    enemy/ally relationship records. GuildManager.GetAbbrevSuffix centralises the rule.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Chat parity: conference moderation, private message, ignore list (Wave 189)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Conference channel moderation (Source-X chat owner/moderator model):
  - A channel now tracks an owner, moderators, voiced members, an optional password
    and a default-voice flag. The member who creates an ad-hoc channel becomes its
    owner (and an implicit moderator). Channel state lives on ChatChannel; routing
    and packets stay in GameClient.

ADDED - Password-protected channels:
  - A protected channel rejects a join with a wrong or missing password. The 0x62/0x63
    payload parser extracts a trailing "{password}" suffix from the channel name, and
    0x41 sets/clears the password (moderator only). The channel list (0xB2 CreateChannel)
    advertises the password flag so the client shows the lock marker.

ADDED - Moderator actions (0xB3 sub-commands):
  - 0x76 kick, 0x6C/0x6D add/remove moderator, 0x69/0x6A grant/revoke voice, 0x77/0x78
    default-voice toggle, 0x64 rename. Each action is gated on the actor being a
    moderator of the channel they are in; rename re-keys the channel and rejects static,
    empty or taken names. AddUser (0xB2 0x03EE) now carries a userType marker
    (1 = moderator, 2 = voiced) so clients render the role beside the name.

ADDED - Moderated talk gating and emote:
  - With default-voice off, only moderators and explicitly voiced members may speak
    (CanSpeak gate); promoting a member to moderator overrides a revoked voice. 0x7A
    routes an emote (0xB2 EmoteMessage) instead of a normal channel message. The voice,
    moderator and default-voice toggles (0x6B / 0x6E / 0x79) and the OSI leave alias
    (0x58) are wired alongside their explicit on/off counterparts.

ADDED - Private messages (0xB3 0x65):
  - A player may whisper another by chat handle ("<recipient> <text>"). The sender
    always sees their own copy; the recipient receives it unless they are ignoring the
    sender.

ADDED - Ignore list (0xB3 0x66 / 0x67 / 0x68):
  - Per-character, channel-independent ignore set (add / remove / toggle) resolved by
    chat handle. A character cannot ignore itself. Channel lines and private messages
    from an ignored sender are suppressed server-side for that recipient (matching the
    OSI conference behaviour) while everyone else still receives them.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Gathering parity: weight-based carry gate, partial node regen (Wave 188)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Weight-based CanCarry on gather/craft delivery (Source-X CanCarry):
  - A gathered or crafted item that would push the actor over its carry weight now
    bounces to the ground instead of going into the pack (previously only a full-by-
    ITEM-COUNT pack bounced; weight was ignored). New Character.MaxWeight / CanCarry
    helpers (Str*7/2 + 40 + mod). Staff bypass the gate.

ADDED - Partial resource-node regen (Source-X gradual vein regrow):
  - A resource vein now slowly refills over time — one unit per (Regen / max) seconds,
    capped at its original pool — instead of only resetting after it is fully depleted.
    A recovering node clears its decay timer so it is not deleted mid-regrow. The node
    stores its full size and last-change time (RES_MAX / RES_LAST tags) alongside the
    remaining pool.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Pet parity: pet figurine shrink / restore (Wave 187)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Pet figurine (Source-X shrink / restore), the last vendor/trade/bank/stable gap:
  - A controlled pet can now be packed into a figurine item carrying a FULL snapshot
    of its state (name, body, stats, brain, AI mode, charDef, skills up to 1200,
    friends, original UUID) and recreated from it later — mirroring the stable
    claim/restore, stored on the item instead of the owner's tag list (PetFigurine).
  - "<pet> shrink" / "all shrink" packs the pet into a figurine in the backpack (the
    pet leaves the world); double-clicking the figurine restores the pet beside the
    player and consumes it. Restore is follower-cap aware (a capped owner keeps the
    figurine) and shrinking rejects summoned/un-owned creatures, like stabling.
  - The previous figurine double-click (which only re-placed a still-living world char
    by a More1 serial) is kept as a fallback for figurines without a snapshot.

[2026-06-30] - Bank parity: self bank box gated by banker proximity (Wave 186)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Remote bank-box access (Source-X bank-open proximity):
  - Items inside the player's own bank box could be picked up or dropped from any
    distance — the self bank box was treated as unconditionally reachable, so a client
    could keep manipulating it after walking away from the banker. Pickup and drop into
    the self bank box (directly or via a nested bag) now require a live banker NPC
    within 3 tiles, matching the proximity required to open it. GM access is unchanged,
    and other containers / the self pack are unaffected.

[2026-06-30] - Vendor/stable parity: opt-in vendor money pool, stable target cursor + validation (Wave 185)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Opt-in vendor money pool (Source-X m_Check_Amount):
  - A vendor with a VENDOR_GOLD tag now tracks finite funds: a player's purchase
    credits the pool and a sale debits it. A sale the vendor cannot fully afford is
    rejected (items kept, pool untouched). A vendor WITHOUT the tag keeps unlimited
    funds, so existing vendors are unchanged — the pool is entirely opt-in.

ADDED - Stable target cursor + pet validation (Source-X stablemaster):
  - Saying "stable" now asks the player to TARGET the pet to stable instead of
    auto-picking the nearest one (a headless/scripted call still falls back to the
    nearest owned pet).
  - Stabling now rejects a summoned/temporary creature and a pet out of range of the
    owner (≤12 tiles, same map), not just non-owned/player targets.

[2026-06-30] - Vendor/stable parity: buy-list, item clone, bank check redeem, stable skill snapshot (Wave 184)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Stable skill snapshot (data loss):
  - Stabling a pet clipped every skill to 1000 (100.0), silently dropping the value of
    GM+ pets on retrieval. The snapshot now keeps the full value (up to 1200), so a
    claimed pet returns with the skills it went in with.

FIXED - Bought item is now a full clone (Source-X CreateDupeItem):
  - Buying from a vendor copied only id/name/hue/amount, dropping the stock entry's
    tags, durability, price and more-fields. The purchase now full-clones the stock
    item's per-instance state.

ADDED - Vendor buy-list restriction (Source-X NPC_FindVendableItem):
  - A vendor with a BUY list now only buys items on that list — the sell gump hides
    other backpack items and the authoritative sell path rejects them (anti-exploit).
    A vendor with NO buy list still buys anything, so existing vendors are unchanged.

ADDED - Bank check redeem:
  - Double-clicking a bank check now converts it to gold in the container it sits in
    (bank box or backpack) and consumes the check (previously checks were one-way —
    created but never redeemable).

ADDED - Stable capacity from skills / MAXPLAYERPETS:
  - Stable slots are no longer a flat 5: an explicit MAXPLAYERPETS tag overrides,
    otherwise the base plus one slot per ~60.0 combined Taming + Animal Lore +
    Veterinary. Never below the base, so unskilled owners keep 5.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Combat parity: COMBAT_ANIM_HIT_SMOOTH swing animation pacing (Wave 183)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - COMBAT_ANIM_HIT_SMOOTH (0x10000), the last deferred swing flag:
  - When enabled, the swing animation is paced to the swing time (a slow weapon shows
    a correspondingly slow swing) instead of the fixed default speed. The legacy 0x6E
    animation packet's per-frame delay byte is now set proportionally to the swing
    delay on both the player and NPC swing paths; with the flag off the delay stays 0
    (unchanged). The exact pacing is client-interpreted; the value is proportional and
    byte-clamped. Enhanced/KR clients (0xE2) have no per-frame field and are unaffected.

FIXED - Test stability:
  - The damage-interrupt skill test looped only 20 swings to land a hit through the
    non-seedable Random.Shared combat RNG, so it could intermittently miss all 20 and
    fail; the loop now runs enough swings that a damaging hit is effectively certain.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Combat parity: two-phase swing state machine (PreHit / StayInRange / SwingNoRange) (Wave 182)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Two-phase windup -> hit swing (Source-X WAR_SWING_TYPE), giving meaning to
        COMBATFLAGS that were defined but inert:
  - A swing now splits into a windup (animation + recoil + a pending hit) and a hit
    phase (ResolveAttack + feedback). The hit resolves when the windup elapses, and
    reach/LoS are re-checked at that moment. Both the player and NPC swing paths share
    the model.
  - COMBAT_STAYINRANGE (0x200): if the target leaves reach/LoS before the hit lands,
    the swing MISSES instead of connecting.
  - COMBAT_SWING_NORANGE (0x8000): the swing may START out of range / without LoS; the
    damage is held until reach + LoS are regained (or dropped if never regained).
  - COMBAT_PREHIT (0x4): forces the hit back to swing-start (atomic) and disables
    SWING_NORANGE, matching Source-X precedence.
  - IMPORTANT: the flagless default keeps a ZERO-length windup, so the hit resolves in
    the same tick the swing starts — byte-for-byte the previous atomic behaviour. No
    existing combat test changed; the windup only opens for the flags above.
  - Deferred: COMBAT_ANIM_HIT_SMOOTH (animation-pacing packet field) — cosmetic and
    needs client-version verification; tracked as a follow-up.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Speech parity: SPEECH RETURN 0 continues, item @Hear coverage (Wave 181)
----------------------------------------

CHANGED - [SPEECH] trigger scan (Source-X OnHearTrigger RETURN semantics):
  - A matched [SPEECH] ON= block that does RETURN 1 still consumes the line and
    stops, but a block that RETURN 0s (or falls through without a RETURN) no longer
    ends the scan — it continues to the next matching ON= block in the SAME speech
    resource. Previously the first matching block always won regardless of its return
    value, so a "didn't handle it" block blocked later handlers.

ADDED - Item @Hear coverage (Source-X item / multi OnHear):
  - Spoken speech now reaches nearby ITEMS: ProcessSpeech fires the new @Hear item
    trigger on every item within hearing range (same range as characters), so
    scripted listening items (signs, comm-crystal-style relays, multi components) can
    react to speech. Gated — the per-utterance item scan runs only when some item def
    actually hooks @Hear, so shards that don't use it pay nothing. S1 = spoken text,
    N1 = talk mode.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Skill parity: @SkillChange as a cancelable setter guard for runtime skill changes (Wave 180)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - @SkillChange on runtime skill value-sets (Source-X setter guard):
  - A GM .ADDSKILL command and a script property assignment (e.g. MAGERY=80) now fire
    a cancelable @SkillChange BEFORE the value is set, so a script can rewrite the new
    value (ARGN2) or RETURN 1 to veto the change. Previously only a skill GAIN raised
    @SkillChange; these runtime setters changed the value silently.
  - Implemented as Character.SetSkillRuntime (fires Character.OnSkillChange, then
    applies the possibly-adjusted value); the GM command and script setter route
    through it. World-load, spawn, decay and gain keep using the raw SetSkill and do
    NOT fire the guard, so save/restore stays side-effect-free. Installed only when
    @SkillChange is hooked.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Skill parity: @SkillGain fires pre-roll with chance/cap tuning + cancel (Wave 179)
----------------------------------------

CHANGED - @SkillGain timing (Source-X Skill_Experience):
  - @SkillGain now fires BEFORE the gain roll instead of after the gain, so a script
    can raise/lower the per-mille gain chance (ARGN2) or the effective skill cap
    (ARGN3), or RETURN 1 to cancel the gain attempt entirely. Previously it fired
    post-gain with the new value and its return was ignored.
  - The new pre-roll hook (SkillEngine.OnSkillGainCheck) is installed only when a
    script actually hooks @SkillGain, so unscripted shards pay a single null check.
  - @SkillChange and the blue "your skill increased" message still fire post-gain on
    the actual value change — only @SkillGain moved.

================================================================================

[2026-06-30] - Spell parity: wand/scroll consume fix, engine cast triggers, [SPELL] ON= dispatch (Wave 178)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Wand charge / scroll consumption (Source-X Spell_CastDone consume stage):
  - A wand charge is no longer deducted at double-click, before the cast resolves —
    so it is no longer lost when the cast fizzles, is interrupted, or the target is
    cancelled. The double-click now tags the source wand (WAND_UID); the charge is
    spent only when SpellEngine.CastDone commits to success. An interrupted/cancelled
    cast clears the tag without spending.
  - Spell-scroll consumption moved from the client success path into the engine
    (CastDone), so precast casts consume the scroll too (previously they leaked it),
    and the consume happens at one shared point for every completion path.

ADDED - Engine-level cast resolution triggers (Source-X parity, NPC/direct casts):
  - @SpellSuccess / @SpellEffect / @SpellFail now fire from one engine hook
    (SpellEngine.OnCastResolved) at cast completion for ANY caster — player, NPC or
    direct — instead of only the client path. The duplicate client fires were
    removed, so player casts still fire each exactly once. (Cast-start failures and
    the targeting cursor's @SpellSelect / @SpellCast / @SpellTargetCancel remain on
    the client UI flow; NPCs gate casts via @NPCActCast.)
  - [SPELL] ON=@Trigger blocks now dispatch: TriggerDispatcher.FireSpellTrigger runs
    a spell def's own ON=@Success / @Effect / @Fail body (the [SPELL] link already
    retained its trigger bodies), wired through the same OnCastResolved hook.
