    server-side.

[2026-06-11] - Corpse carving uses the chardef RESOURCES list (Wave 127)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Death:
  - Carving produced hardcoded hides/meat for every corpse. Per the
    reference, parts now come from the victim chardef RESOURCES list
    (with amounts — "19 i_ribs_raw" works): player-corpse parts are
    renamed "<part> of <victim>" and fall to the ground with decay,
    creature parts go into the corpse. Defs without RESOURCES keep the
    legacy random rolls; a corpse can only be carved once.

[2026-06-11] - NPC cast FX, spell-damage feedback, gated per-action triggers (Wave 126)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Magic / NPC AI:
  - Spell damage applied silently — no damage number, no health-bar
    update — until the victim died; both packets are now broadcast on
    every spell hit (the melee/breath paths already had them).
  - NPC casts had no completion visuals (the bolt/impact effect lives
    in the player client path); a host hook now emits the same effect
    packet for clientless casters, so NPC spells are visible.
  - Per-action NPC triggers (@NPCActWander/Fight/Follow/Cast,
    @NPCLookAtChar/Item) install only when a script hooks them
    (IsTrigUsed gate) — an idle 20-30K NPC world no longer pays a full
    dispatch walk per wander step.
  - Diagnostics: [npc_cast] logs every NPC cast attempt and
    [death_path] names the kill entry point, for the delayed-death
    report.

[2026-06-11] - Staff drag tiledata-locked ground items; stacking and resource names (Wave 125)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Items:
  - The client refuses to start a drag on tiledata-locked graphics
    (weight 255 — corpses, anvils) unless the world-item packet
    carries the force-movable flag; staff clients now receive it on
    ground items, so a GM can actually pick a corpse up.
  - Stack merging required the scripted CAN_I_PILE flag, which packs
    rarely declare; the reference seeds it from the tiledata stackable
    flag, now used as a fallback — mined ore/ingots/logs merge in the
    pack again.
  - Gathered resources (mining/fishing/lumberjacking) now carry their
    itemdef display name, so single-click and vendor rows name them.

[2026-06-11] - Full hands exclusion; container click shows contents (Wave 124)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Items:
  - The hand-slot exclusion only covered the shield cases, so a
    one-hand weapon and a two-handed weapon could be held together.
    A true two-handed weapon now bounces whatever the other hand
    holds to the backpack, and any one-hand-layer equip bounces a
    held two-handed weapon (shields still coexist).
  - Containers and corpses append "(N items, N stones)" to their
    single-click label (CONT_ITEMS defmessage).

[2026-06-11] - Attack announcements per reference; death FX reach the dying client (Wave 123)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Combat / Death:
  - The "is attacking" announcement formatted the victim-facing
    template with the wrong name and broadcast it to everyone. Per the
    reference both lines now render over the ATTACKER: "*X is
    attacking Y!*" in the emote hue to all observers except the
    victim's client, and "*X is attacking you!*" only to the victim.
  - The death particle and sound were delivered broadcast-only and
    never reached the dying client (confirmed by wire capture); they
    are now sent to it directly, with observers still covered by an
    exclude-victim broadcast.

[2026-06-11] - Swing and surround sidestep no longer share a tick (Wave 122)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - NPC AI:
  - When a melee swing actually fired, the NPC could also take its
    surround/flank sidestep in the same AI tick; the walk packet made
    the client cancel the just-started attack animation (hits looked
    like sliding). The sidestep now only happens on recoil ticks where
    no swing fired — the same move-pair conflict class as the pet
    GO/follow bug.

[2026-06-11] - Single-step descent cap raised to climbable parity (Wave 121)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Movement:
  - The server-only descent cap (MaxDescendZ=11) rejected walking DOWN
    cave-floor ramps that step 24 units in one tile, while the maxZ
    window accepted the matching climb UP — the ramp was one-way and
    every descent rejection rubber-banded the running player back to
    the top (the "mine exit threw me up" report; one session tallied
    33 descent_cap rejects). The client has no descent limit, so for
    client-driven moves the cap can only create desyncs. Raised to 25
    so anything a mover can climb passes back down; kept as an
    extreme-fall guard for chasing NPCs at true cliff faces.

[2026-06-11] - Zero success chance never rolls a success (Wave 120)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Skills:
  - Skill_CheckSuccess compared "successChance >= rand(0..999)", so a
    ZERO chance still succeeded when the die came up 0 — a 1-in-1000
    fluke per roll. In game that let skill-0 attempts occasionally
    pass impossible difficulties; in the test suite it was the
    long-standing intermittent failure class in the success-curve
    tests (craft fail-loss, stealth — the Wave 111-era test hardening
    only masked the symptom). A non-positive chance now fails
    outright before the die is cast.

[2026-06-11] - Dying in the saddle dismounts before the corpse snapshot (Wave 119)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Death:
  - The death pipeline never dismounted a mounted victim, so the
    mount-layer item survived into the death state: the client kept
    drawing a mounted body under the dead character, the ghost
    transition did not show and the mount NPC never reappeared.
    DeathEngine now runs a dismount hook before the corpse is made
    (reference Death → Horse_UnMount order): the mount item is
    removed for observers and the mount NPC is placed back into the
    world. Covers every kill path through ProcessDeath.

[2026-06-11] - SPELLFLAG_* constant names resolve in spell flag parsing (Wave 118)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Magic:
  - SPELLFLAG_* names are engine constants in the reference
    (game_macros.h), not script defnames — script packs typically
    never declare them in a [DEFNAME] block. Spell FLAGS lines using
    those names silently parsed to None, so no spell ever opened a
    target cursor (every cast self-targeted) and field/area/bolt
    behaviors were lost. The flag parser now falls back to the
    built-in constant table (values match the reference one-to-one);
    script-defined defnames still take precedence.

[2026-06-11] - Region EVENTS entries bind REGIONTYPE resource tables (Wave 117)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Gathering:
  - Area definitions attach their natural-resource tables through the
    region EVENTS list ("EVENTS=r_default,r_default_rock,…"), and the
    reference scans that list by res-type (FindNaturalResource). The
    region loader only stored those names as plain event links, so
    every region had an empty resource-table list and gathering
    (mining / fishing / lumberjacking) fell back to an arbitrary
    loaded table — often an all-nothing dungeon table, which made
    every dig yield nothing and never spawn the resource marker.
    REGIONTYPE names in EVENTS now also populate the region-type list.

[2026-06-11] - Double-click equips first; vendor buy list reverse order (Wave 116)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Items / Vendors:
  - Reference Cmd_Use_Item parity: an equippable item that is not
    currently equipped is now armed/worn on double-click — from the
    ground or a container — before its use-type behavior runs (weapons
    and tools used to jump straight to the target prompt and never
    reached the hand). Routes through the real pickup + equip paths so
    reach, ownership, @PickUp_*/@EquipTest/@Equip triggers and
    hand-swap rules all apply; the layer's previous occupant bounces
    to the backpack. Spellbooks and ground light sources keep their
    open/toggle behavior.
  - The 0x74 vendor buy list is now sent in REVERSE of the 0x3C
    container order: the client walks the stock container's item list
    from the tail when decorating rows, so same-order packets paired
    every row with another row's price and name (rows showed 0gp and
    blank names on mismatch).

[2026-06-11] - Pet GO order overrides following; dragon-family breath (Wave 115)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - NPC AI:
  - The "all go" pet order ran the follow step and the GO step in the
    same AI tick, so the two moves cancelled out and the pet oscillated
    between its owner and the ordered spot without arriving. An active
    GO order now overrides following entirely; the pet walks to the
    spot and stays there (reference NPCACT_GOTO). Regression test
    added (NpcPetGoOrderTests).
  - The breath attack only fired for the Dragon brain, fire-immune
    monsters or a BREATH.DAM tag — script packs routinely keep
    BRAIN=brain_monster on dragons and relied on the legacy
    body-derived creature type. Dragon-family bodies (dragons, drakes,
    wyvern, serpentine/skeletal, shadow/white wyrm, swamp dragon,
    ancient wyrm) now breathe regardless of the scripted brain.

[2026-06-10] - Shared death-effects pipeline; DeathCorpse, Reveal, SpellEffectAdd/Remove triggers (Wave 114)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Death:
  - GM kill paths (UID form, target-cursor form) and the guard
    instant-kill path called the corpse/loot engine directly, skipping
    the client-visible death sequence — corpse packet ordering, the
    per-observer 0xAF dispatch and the victim ghost transition — and
    the @Kill/@Death triggers. The visual sequence was extracted from
    the NPC-kill handler into a shared ProcessDeathWithEffects pipeline
    and every non-combat-handler kill path now runs it; self-kills are
    unattributed (no kill credit, no murder mark).

ADDED - Triggers:
  - @DeathCorpse fires on the victim once the corpse exists and loot
    has been transferred (argo = corpse), per the reference order.
  - @Reveal: hidden/invisible removal is centralized in
    Character.ClearHiddenState (attack, speech, detect-hidden, NPC
    detection, reveal spell, stealth-step expiry); the trigger fires
    before the state drops and RETURN 1 keeps concealment. Speech now
    also drops spell invisibility, matching the reference reveal.
  - @SpellEffectAdd / @SpellEffectRemove fire across the timed-effect
    lifecycle (apply, expiry, re-cast refresh, death cleanup);
    ARGN1 = spell id, SRC = caster on add. The transient save-time
    revert/reapply is deliberately silent.
  - @SpellEffectTick is declared but not fired: the engine has no
    periodic spell-effect (tick-flagged) mechanism yet; documented in
    the trigger-coverage guardrail backlog (char backlog now 3).
  - New static hooks added to the test-isolation reset list. Stub
    inventory doc updated with this audit's false-positive list so
    future scans do not re-flag implemented features. Full suite
    green (783).

[2026-06-10] - Dialog layout engine: string LOCALs, function calls, FORINSTANCES, GUMPPIC/TOOLTIP (Wave 113)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Dialogs:
  - LOCAL assignments in the layout expansion pass coerced every value
    to a number, destroying comma lists and .= string concatenations
    (a list stored as "0" made every downstream loop bound and lookup
    collapse). Values are now stored verbatim; ++/--/.= forms arrive
    pre-rewritten as expressions by the script-key parser and keep
    working, and +=/-= stay numeric.
  - The layout expression resolver had no script-function resolver, so
    [FUNCTION] calls inside layouts (list helpers used as FOR bounds,
    formatters in text args) never resolved and the affected loop
    bodies dropped out of the rendered gump. Function expressions now
    execute through the trigger runner with the dialog character as
    the target object.
  - Bare function tokens resolved to their resource index through the
    plain-defname fallback instead of executing; Function-typed
    defnames are excluded from that fallback so they reach the
    function resolver.

ADDED - Dialogs:
  - FORINSTANCES expansion: runs the body once per live world instance
    of the given itemdef (matching BaseId or the SCRIPTDEF tag) —
    covers the bare counting pattern. FOR-family block matching added
    so a nested FOR* loop's shared ENDFOR terminator cannot close an
    outer loop early.
  - GUMPPIC was only accepted in its single-P spelling; the canonical
    double-P verb is now an alias of the same renderer. TOOLTIP layout
    op added (cliloc tooltip attached to the previous element, new
    GumpBuilder.AddTooltip). Layout verb coverage for the imported
    dialog pack is now complete. Full suite green (783).

[2026-06-10] - Allocation-free decay catch-up; precomputed trigger-function gate (Wave 112)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE - Tick path:
  - The 5-second decay catch-up sweep materialized a full snapshot of the
    world object table (ToArray + LINQ chain) on every pass; on imported
    worlds with 100k+ objects that is a megabyte-scale transient
    allocation and a periodic GC spike. The sweep now collects expired
    ground items directly into a reusable buffer
    (GameWorld.CollectExpiredGroundItems); collection completes before
    any deletion, so the snapshot-free enumeration is safe in the
    serial post-tick phase.
  - Trigger dispatch paid a name concat + lowercase + argument wrapping
    on every char/item trigger fire to probe the f_onchar_*/f_onitem_*
    function fallback even when no such function exists. The set of
    trigger names that have function fallbacks is now precomputed from
    loaded [FUNCTION] defnames (also covers custom TRIGGER-verb names,
    which the old enum scan missed); the fallback step is skipped
    entirely otherwise. If the cache is never built the gate stays open,
    preserving embedded/test behavior.
  - Script resync now rebuilds the used-trigger cache, so [ON=@X] hooks
    and function fallbacks added or removed by reloaded files take
    effect without a restart. Full suite green (783).

[2026-06-10] - Craft work-site proximity matches map statics (Wave 111)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Crafting:
  - The Wave 107 forge/heat proximity check only saw dynamic forge/fire
    items, so the built-in static forges of town smithies did not count
    as work sites. The check now also scans the map statics around the
    crafter and resolves each static graphic through its itemdef type
    (forge / fire / campfire) — the same graphic→itemdef resolution the
    reference uses for static tiles. Note: the static branch depends on
    loaded MUL data and is exercised in-game; the unit suite covers the
    dynamic-item path (the existing CraftParityTests). Full suite green
    (783).

[2026-06-10] - Spell disturb follows the INTERRUPT curve (Wave 110)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Magic:
  - The INTERRUPT spell property was read with plain int parsing — the
    pack's decimal curve values ("INTERRUPT=100.0,100.0") failed
    silently and the field was never used anyway: the disturb chance was
    an invented damage/max-hits ratio clamped to 5-95%. Ported the
    reference semantics (OnTakeDamage disturb block): INTERRUPT is a
    per-mille curve across the caster's skill with legacy fixed-point
    values ("100.0" = 1000 = always disturbable, the reference default),
    the damage amount does not factor into the roll, and only player
    casters are disturbed. INTERRUPT=0 spells are uninterruptible. The
    protection-effect dampening is kept as an engine approximation of
    the reference protection-spell cancel.
  - New tests (SpellInterruptTests, 3): zero curve never disturbs, full
    curve disturbs on any damage, NPC casters exempt. Full suite green
    (783).

[2026-06-10] - Multi-stroke crafting + spellbook-in-hand casting (Wave 109)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Crafting:
  - Crafting now runs as a stroke loop (reference Skill_MakeItem →
    Skill_Stroke) instead of resolving instantly on the gump click: two
    work strokes spaced by the skill's DELAY-curve timeout (one-second
    reference floor), each broadcasting the craft animation and sound;
    the skill roll and resource consumption happen at completion, after
    a CanCraft re-check — walking away from the forge or losing the
    materials mid-craft fails without the roll and without loss. A
    second craft cannot start while one is pending. Both the crafting
    gump and the SKILLMENU MAKEITEM verb route through the same loop,
    driven from the per-client tick pump.

FIXED - Magic:
  - A wielded spellbook counted as a blocking weapon for the
    equipped-cast check, so casting with the book in hand fizzled when
    EQUIPPEDCAST was off. Spellbooks (like wands) no longer block
    casting in either hand.

INTERNAL - Tests:
  - Two spell tests toggled the global spellbook-requirement static,
    which parallel test collections reset mid-run (intermittent
    failures); they now satisfy the requirement with a real spellbook
    item instead. New tests (CraftStrokeTests, 2) cover the stroke
    delay, the busy guard and the walk-away completion failure. Full
    suite green (780) across repeated runs.

[2026-06-10] - [SKILLMENU] selection menus: load, open, select (Wave 108)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - Script menus:
  - [SKILLMENU] sections (reference Cmd_Skill_Menu) are now retained at
    load and reachable at runtime: the new SKILLMENU client verb opens
    the named section as a 0x7C selection menu — first non-ON line is
    the title, each ON=<itemdef> [text] entry shows the itemdef art
    ("<name>"/empty text falls back to the itemdef name), TEST=SKILL
    value lines gate entries on the character's skills (legacy
    fixed-point values), and the remaining lines run as script verbs on
    selection. Menu selection now falls through from console verbs to
    the character's own property/verb surface, so entry bodies like
    POLY work.
  - New entry verbs: SUMMON <chardef> (reference CV_SUMMON — summons the
    chardef as a temporary summoned pet, duration from the Summon
    spell's curve, two-minute fallback) and MAKEITEM <itemdef>
    (reference SKILLMENU MAKEITEM — crafts through the crafting-engine
    recipe loaded from the itemdef's SKILLMAKE/RESOURCES).
  - POLY now resolves chardef defnames and weighted "{ c_a 1 c_b 1 }"
    lists in addition to numeric bodies (the script pack's sm_polymorph
    entries use both forms).
  - Casting Polymorph or Summon Creature opens the pack's
    sm_polymorph/sm_summon menu when one exists (@SkillMenu fires first
    with the menu name and can veto); without a script menu the normal
    cast flow continues unchanged.
  - New tests (SkillMenuTests, 4): menu open + TEST gating, selection
    running POLY, unknown-menu fallthrough, weighted POLY lists. Full
    suite green (778).

[2026-06-10] - Craft parity: work-site proximity, SKILLMAKE tools, fail loss (Wave 107)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Crafting:
  - Work-site proximity (reference Skill_Blacksmith / Skill_Cooking):
    smithing recipes now require a forge within 2 tiles and cooking a
    heat source within 3 (fire, forge or campfire). Crafting previously
    worked anywhere; the requirement also greys out the crafting gump
    entries when no site is near. (Dynamic forge/fire items only — map
    statics are not type-matched.)
  - SKILLMAKE t_*/i_* entries were parsed and silently discarded; they
    are now presence requirements (reference SkillResourceTest): t_*
    resolves through the TYPEDEF table to an item type that must be
    carried or wielded, i_* to a specific item that must be present.
    Neither is consumed.
  - Fail loss now matches the reference ResourceConsumePart semantics:
    one 0-50% roll applied uniformly to every required resource. The
    old behaviour rolled per resource (50% chance to lose exactly half,
    always at least 1 even for single-unit resources).
  - New tests (CraftParityTests, 4): forge/heat proximity bounds, tool
    presence without consumption, and the fail-loss ceiling. Full suite
    green (774).

[2026-06-10] - Spell cast parity: spellbook, scroll/wand costs, cast-time curve, resist (Wave 106)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Magic:
  - Spellbook requirement (reference Spell_CanCast): a player casting a
    classic spell (1-64) from memory must now have it in an accessible
    spellbook (equipped hands or backpack; the classic 64-bit More1/More2
    mask). Scroll and wand casts bypass the book. New SpellbookRequired
    config knob (default on) wired next to ReagentsRequired and covered
    by the test-suite static baseline.
  - Scroll casts now pay half mana and roll at half difficulty, and wand
    casts cost no mana (reference parity); scroll casts also skip the
    reagent check. Previously a wand cast still consumed the full mana
    cost and scrolls behaved like memory casts.
  - CAST_TIME is now a curve like EFFECT/DURATION (single value =
    constant, "A,B" interpolates across skill); the invented
    "-skill/250" faster-casting formula is gone — with the script pack's
    constant CAST_TIME values every spell used to get faster with magery
    against the reference.
  - Magic resist now follows the reference roll: a quick MagicResistance
    check whose chance is max(resist/50, resist - ((magery-200)/50 +
    (1 + spell/8)*50)) / 30 — success absorbs a flat 25% of the effect,
    failure absorbs nothing. The previous gradient (circle*80 difficulty,
    0-50% scaling) was an invention.
  - New tests (SpellCastParityTests, 3) pin the resist formula, the
    cast-time curve and the book bit-mask lookup.

INTERNAL - Tests:
  - The Wave 103 reference success curve tops out below certainty
    (~99.6% at the maximum skill-vs-difficulty delta) and keeps a ~0.5%
    success tail at the minimum, which made success- and fizzle-asserting
    tests intermittently flaky. Hardened the margin tests: actors that
    must succeed train past the curve's certainty point or use the GM
    bypass, and the fizzle test's requirement moved past the zero-chance
    tail. Full suite green (770) across repeated runs.

[2026-06-10] - Resource loader: legacy numeric section-id parse (Wave 105)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Script loading:
  - Numeric section ids ([SKILL n], [SPELL n], [ITEMDEF n], [CHARDEF n],
    [MULTIDEF n]) were always parsed as hex. The reference uses the
    legacy script number rule: "0x.." and leading-zero forms are hex,
    anything else is decimal. Real packs write itemdef/chardef ids with
    a leading zero ("0eed") — unaffected — but skill and spell ids as
    plain decimal, so every [SKILL 10]..[SKILL 57] and [SPELL 10]+
    definition landed on the wrong slot (e.g. the Swordsmanship def
    [SKILL 40] registered as skill 64): names, delays, ADV_RATE curves
    and spell properties above index 9 were silently mismapped or lost.
  - A scan of the mortechUO pack confirms the fix is safe: 32,239
    leading-zero headers keep their hex meaning, 57 [SKILL] + 167
    [SPELL] decimal headers are corrected, and no header uses bare hex
    without a leading zero. Tests that had encoded the hex behaviour
    were updated to decimal ids. Full suite green (767).

[2026-06-10] - Stat-gain parity ([ADVANCE] curves, STAT_* targets) + 0x3A caps (Wave 104)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Skills:
  - Stat gain was a simplified invention: a flat 5%-per-use chance (or
    BONUS_STATS misread as that chance) picking a weighted stat, with a
    hardcoded skill→stat table as fallback. Ported the reference
    Skill_Experience stat section instead: stats train only while the
    used skill's lock is Up; each stat trains toward the skill def's
    STAT_STR/DEX/INT ceiling; the chance comes from the script [ADVANCE]
    advance-rate curves (uses-per-point, inverse like ADV_RATE) scaled by
    BONUS_* weights and BONUS_STATS percent; polymorphed characters can
    only train INT; one stat gain per skill use. The [ADVANCE] section —
    present in the mortechUO pack but previously skipped as a generic
    sphere section — is now parsed and handed to the skill engine, and
    the test-suite static reset covers the curves.
  - Ported the reference Stat_Decrease for the total stat cap: under the
    cap a gain is simply allowed; over it a DOWN-locked stat (the one the
    skill values least) may erode by 1 (floor 10) to make room, with the
    reference S-curve loss chance.
  - The 0x3A skill-list cap field was hardcoded to 100.0; it now reports
    the per-skill display cap (class caps/overrides).
  - New tests (StatGainParityTests, 5). Full suite green (767).

NOTES - Known gap (next wave):
  - The resource loader parses numeric [SKILL n] section ids as HEX while
    the reference (and the real script pack, [SKILL 0]..[SKILL 57]
    decimal) uses the legacy number rule (decimal unless leading zero) —
    skill defs with index >= 10 currently land on the wrong skill. Fixed
    in its own wave because the same id parse feeds spell defs.

[2026-06-10] - Skill success curve parity + stat-adjusted skill checks (Wave 103)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Skills:
  - The skill success roll used a tanh-based S-curve with variance 100;
    the reference uses a piecewise halving bell curve with
    SKILL_VARIANCE=150 (chance halves per 15.0 skill points of distance
    from the difficulty midpoint). The tanh shape was much steeper —
    e.g. 15.0 points above the difficulty succeeded ~95% of the time
    instead of the reference 75%. Ported the reference
    Calc_GetSCurve/Calc_GetBellCurve pair exactly and fixed the variance
    constant (the old comment also mis-cited the reference value).
  - Skill checks now use the stat-adjusted skill value (reference
    Skill_GetAdjusted): raw skill + BONUS_STATS percent of the
    BONUS_STR/INT/DEX-weighted stats from the skill def. Previously the
    BONUS_* properties never influenced any check. Scope note: combat
    hit/damage formulas still read the raw skill (their parity is a
    separate combat-engine subject).
  - New tests (SkillSuccessCurveTests, 7) pin the curve points and the
    adjusted-skill formula. Full suite green (762).

[2026-06-10] - Skill gain/atrophy parity: total cap no longer freezes characters (Wave 102)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Skills:
  - The gain and decay rolls were wrapped in a single gate that required
    a positive difficulty, and the total skill cap zeroes the difficulty
    — so at the cap neither roll ran and a capped character was frozen
    permanently regardless of lock arrows. On top of that the decay
    helper guarded itself with "only at the total cap", which combined
    with the outer gate made skill atrophy dead code on every path.
    Restructured to the reference Skill_Experience shape: the block is
    entered while the trained skill can still rise, the decay roll
    (3:4 of the gain chance) runs independently of the cap and erodes a
    DOWN-locked skill by 0.1, and only the gain roll is gated on
    difficulty — a capped character now retrains by setting arrows just
    like the reference.
  - Removed the invented GAINRADIUS=300 default: the reference treats an
    unset GAINRADIUS as disabled, while the default silently blocked
    low-difficulty gain rolls for every skill above 30.0.
  - New tests (SkillGainParityTests, 4): capped retraining via a
    DOWN-locked skill, frozen-at-cap without one, high-skill gain with no
    gain radius, and locked-skill immutability. Full suite green (755).

[2026-06-10] - Skill definitions: legacy value-curve parsing + ADV_RATE semantics (Wave 101)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Skills:
  - [SKILL] definition numerics were read with plain int parsing, which
    silently fails on every decimal/multi-value property real script
    packs use (ADV_RATE=2.5,50.0,200.0; DELAY=2.0): the values dropped to
    zero, so ADV_RATE was ignored for every skill and every skill delay
    became instant. Added ValueCurve, a port of the reference curve type
    (credit: Sphere 0.56 CValueCurveDef + ahextoi): legacy fixed-point
    number parse (decimal point concatenates digits, leading zero marks
    hex) and linear interpolation across skill 0-100.0. ADV_RATE, DELAY
    and EFFECT are now curves; the remaining numeric fields use the same
    legacy number parse (this also fixes FLAGS, which the old decimal
    parse misread for leading-zero hex values).
  - ADV_RATE semantics corrected: the curve expresses "skill uses per 0.1
    gain" and the per-mille gain chance is its inverse (100000/value,
    reference GetChancePercent). The previous interpretation treated the
    value as a 0-100 multiplier on a homegrown curve, which made gain
    pacing both wrong and untunable per skill.
  - Skill delays now follow the DELAY curve at the user's skill level
    (reference Skill_GetTimeout); the delayed-skill pipeline passes the
    character's skill value through.
  - New tests (ValueCurveTests, 14) pin the parse rules with the actual
    mortechUO script values and the interpolation/chance math. Full suite
    green (751).

[2026-06-10] - NPCs open unlocked doors on blocked steps (Wave 100)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - NPC movement:
  - Closes the door gap documented in Wave 99: NPC walk validation
    treats a closed door as a hard block, so NPCs could not chase or
    wander through doorways. When a direct step is blocked, the AI now
    checks the blocked tile for a closed, unlocked door item (locked
    doors and portcullises stay barriers when locked) and opens it with
    the reference 50%-per-attempt gate before re-validating the step
    (reference parity: the idle look-at path uses the door, then walks
    through).
  - The state flip lives in a new world-level DoorHelper.TryOpenDoorState
    (same art-offset and DOOR_OPEN tag transition as the player
    double-click path, portcullis offset 2, DISPID-override aware, no
    network side effects); the server wiring broadcasts the open sound
    (0xEA) and the refreshed world item to nearby observers via a new
    OnNpcOpenDoor hook. Doors opened by NPCs close again through the
    normal double-click toggle.
  - New tests (NpcDoorOpeningTests, 5) cover the state flip (closed,
    portcullis, locked, already-open) and the blocked-tile door lookup.
    Full suite green (737).

[2026-06-10] - NPC polish: idle fidget animation + pet follow leash (Wave 99)
----------------------------------------

ADDED - NPC behaviour:
  - Idle NPCs now occasionally (1-in-8 idle ticks) play a fidget
    animation in place instead of taking a wander step, through a new
    OnNpcFidget hook wired to the version-aware, body-translated
    animation broadcast (humanoid fidget/yawn, monster groups 0x11/0x12,
    animal groups 0x09/0x0A, mounted mapping applied). Reference plays
    random idle fidgets; standing NPCs previously never animated at all.
  - Pet follow/guard/return movement now gives up beyond a leash
    distance on the same map (NpcAI.PetFollowMaxDistance, default 36 =
    the reference radar range; 0 disables) and resumes when the owner
    comes back into range. The cross-map catch-up teleport is unchanged.
    The new static is registered in the test-suite static reset.

NOTES - Known gap (documented, not yet implemented):
  - Reference NPCs open adjacent doors while idling (NPC_LookAtItem:
    use the door, then walk through). Our NPC walk validation treats a
    closed door as a hard block, so NPCs cannot chase or wander through
    doorways. Implementing this needs a world-level door toggle (the
    current toggle lives on the client handler surface) - deferred.
  - Full suite green (732).

[2026-06-10] - NPC visibility: untracked-in-range appear + cross-map leave (Wave 98)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - NPC visibility:
  - The object-centric NPC move notification had no branch for a mobile
    that is in range on both ends of the step but not yet tracked by the
    observer (the player path already handled this). An NPC that unhid
    after a scout-hide, or whose initial appear was filtered at spawn
    time, moved invisibly until the observer's next full view refresh.
    NotifyCharMoved now falls through to the appear path in that case
    (hidden/ghost filters still apply), mirroring the player
    enter/leave handler.
  - Cross-map moves (pet follow teleporting to the owner's map) only
    swept sectors on the destination map, so observers left on the old
    map never received the leave-range delete and kept a ghost copy of
    the mobile until their own view refreshed. The sector sweep is now
    per-map: the destination map around the new position plus, for
    cross-map moves, the source map around the old position. This also
    removes the pathological sector rectangle the old min/max span
    produced when the two positions were on unrelated coordinates.
  - New tests (NpcVisibilityNotifyTests, 2) cover the untracked-appear
    branch and the tracked-move 0x77 path. Full suite green (732).

[2026-06-10] - NPC run-bit consistency on path-follow, flee and pet steps (Wave 97)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - NPC movement:
  - The 0x77 direction byte carries the run flag (0x80) that clients use
    to pick the walk vs run animation. Chasing NPCs set it on direct
    steps but lost it on A*-path-follow steps, so a pursuing NPC stepping
    every ~250ms animated as walking — the visible "skating/sliding NPC"
    artifact — and mixed direct/path routes flickered between run and
    walk. Path-follow steps now inherit the caller's run intent.
  - Flee steps now run once there is room and walk while cornered
    (reference parity: the flee path walks at threat distance <= 3 and
    runs beyond), and pet follow/guard/return steps run when the target
    is more than 3 tiles away (reference NPC_Act_Follow run threshold).
  - Full suite green (730); movement + runtime-pressure suites green
    (70).

[2026-06-10] - Spell cast animation: body translation + gesture dispatch (Wave 96)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Animations:
  - The spell-cast animation hook broadcast a raw legacy 0x6E packet with
    the humanoid cast indices (0x10/0x11) to every observer regardless of
    caster body and client version. Non-humanoid casters (liches, mages
    with monster bodies) therefore played the wrong group on classic
    clients, and KR/Enhanced clients never received the 0xE2 gesture
    variant. The hook now routes through the version-aware animation
    broadcast: the legacy path gets the body-translated group via
    BodyAnimTranslator (monster cast = stomp/pillage, animal cast =
    attack/eat per the Wave 95 table, mounted mapping unchanged) and
    KR/Enhanced observers get 0xE2 with the Spell gesture. Full suite
    green (730).

[2026-06-10] - Body-type animation translation for the legacy 0x6E path (Wave 95)
----------------------------------------

FIXED - Animations:
  - Classic clients read the 0x6E action field as a raw group index into
    the actor body's own anim.mul file, so humanoid action indices sent to
    monster or animal bodies played the wrong group (or none). Added
    BodyAnimTranslator, a port of the reference body-translation table
    (credit: Sphere 0.56 GenerateAnimate): bodies < 200 use the
    high-detail monster set (attacks 4-6, get-hit randomized over
    get-hit/block-right/block-left, cast = stomp/pillage, deaths 2/3),
    bodies 200-399 use the low-detail animal set (attacks 5-6, get-hit 7,
    cast 5/eat, deaths 8/12), bodies >= 400 pass through unchanged.
  - Applied at every emit site where the actor can be non-humanoid: the
    hit-reaction broadcast in the player swing path and the NPC attack
    wiring (both previously sent the humanoid get-hit index 0x14 to any
    body), the NPC swing-action helper (animals previously received the
    monster attack group 4; humanoid check also widened from the two
    human bodies to the full >= 400 range so elf-range bodies animate
    with the humanoid set), the healer heal animation, and the script
    ANIMATE/BOW/SALUTE verbs (mounted mapping preserved, body translation
    added for the unmounted path).
  - New deterministic unit suite (BodyAnimTranslationTests, 7 tests)
    covers the table boundaries and group mappings. Full suite green
    (730).

[2026-06-10] - GameClient decomposition phase 4: IClientContext interface (Wave 94)
----------------------------------------

INTERNAL - GameClient decomposition (plan complete):
  - The union of the nine handler classes' context-shim blocks was derived
    into a narrow internal IClientContext interface (~125 members: core
    state, engine accessors, decomposition components, script services,
    shared mutable state bridges, server-wired callbacks, packet/gump
    helpers, gameplay bridges and targeting helpers). It extends
    ITextConsole because handlers pass their context onward as the script
    console identity (TriggerArgs.ScriptConsole, TryRunFunction,
    TryExecuteCommand). GameClient implements it explicitly in the new
    GameClient.Context partial - pure forwarding, no behaviour - which
    keeps the internal members internal. All nine handlers
    (ViewUpdater, Inventory, ItemUse, WorldFeatures, Targeting, Dialog,
    Skills, Combat, ScriptConsole) and the InfoSkillSink glue type now
    hold IClientContext instead of the concrete GameClient, so the
    compiler enforces that handler code can only reach the declared
    surface; handler constructors became internal (a public constructor
    cannot take an internal parameter type). The field-level shims
    (vitals last-sent, pending-menu state) route through interface
    properties backed by the existing GameClient fields. Full suite green
    (723) + RuntimePerformancePressure 6/6; mojibake scan clean. This
    closes the decomposition plan (phases 1-4); the PacketHelpers/Login/
    Handlers/Chat/Housing partials remain on GameClient by design.

[2026-06-10] - GameClient decomposition phase 1: state-machine components (Wave 84)
----------------------------------------

INTERNAL - GameClient decomposition:
  - The decomposition plan for the ~16k-line GameClient partial-class cluster
    is documented in docs/GAMECLIENT_DECOMPOSITION_TR.md (phase 1: state
    machines, phase 2: view cache, phase 3: per-partial handler classes over
    a ClientContext), and phase 1 is executed in this wave.
  - Three cohesive state clusters moved out of GameClient fields into
    components, with every reference across the partials renamed — pure
    state relocation, logic untouched:
      * ClientTargetState (GameClient.Targets) — all 28 pending-target-cursor
        fields plus the cursor-active flag; its Clear() is the former
        ClearPendingTargetState body verbatim (notably it still does NOT
        clear the Kill flag, the callback slot or the skill-cancel id,
        matching the original).
      * ClientGumpRegistry (GameClient.Gumps) — active gump set, per-gump
        response callbacks, open script-dialog registry.
      * ClientMovementThrottle (GameClient.Throttle) — walk token bucket
        (seeded with WalkBufferMax at first use, same timing as the former
        field initializer), move-time gate, violation counter, movement
        queue processor.
  - Tests that reached these fields by reflection now use the internal
    component properties directly (InternalsVisibleTo).
  - Phase 2 (same wave): the view-delta bookkeeping (known-char/item/door
    sets, last-known position/item state, tooltip hash cache) moved into
    ClientViewCache (GameClient.View) the same way. Phase 3 — converting
    the partials into handler classes over a ClientContext — is the next,
    per-partial effort and is intentionally left for dedicated sessions.

[2026-06-10] - Character decomposition slice 3: memory subsystem component (Wave 83)
----------------------------------------

INTERNAL - Character decomposition:
  - The memory-item subsystem (EqMemoryObj list, fight/aggressor memories,
    timeout ticks, notoriety notifications — Source-X CChar Memory_*) moved
    into a new CharacterMemoryState component (Character.MemoryState, lazily
    created). All Memory_* methods and the Memories view delegate, so the
    public API, the @MemoryEquip hook, pet-flag handling, the cowardice/fame
    retreat rule and the fight-memory tick cadence are unchanged — the logic
    moved verbatim. Character.cs is down to 4,500 lines (from ~4,950 before
    the decomposition pass).
  - Deliberate completion point for the state-extraction pass: the vitals
    regen + hunger tick block and the core stat fields stay in Character ON
    PURPOSE. That code writes the private stat fields directly and manages
    the dirty-flag discipline by hand (e.g. Resurrect seeds _hits directly);
    forcing it through the public property setters to move it into a
    component would subtly change clamp/dirty semantics, which breaks the
    "logic moves verbatim" guarantee these slices are built on. Any future
    slice of that block needs a dedicated behavioural test net first.

[2026-06-10] - Combat ability trigger, spawner start/stop triggers, lost-NPC teleport (Wave 80)
----------------------------------------

ENGINE - triggers:
  - @UserSpecialMove fires from the 0xD7 sub 0x19 combat ability request
    (client Send_UseCombatAbility — payload layout verified against the
    ClassicUO writer), N1 = the ability index. Routed ahead of the
    house-design session gate since it shares the 0xD7 opcode.
  - @Start / @Stop fire when the spawner START/STOP verbs toggle spawning
    (Item.OnSpawnStartStop host hook).
  - @NPCLostTeleport is anchored to new engine behaviour: a wild NPC that
    ends up more than three leash radii from home teleports straight home
    instead of walking the whole way back; the trigger fires first and
    RETURN 1 cancels the teleport (the NPC walks as before). Confirmed safe:
    the chase/leash logic runs in the serial ApplyDecision phase, not the
    parallel decision builder.
  - Item @RegionEnter/@RegionLeave remain deferred with a sharpened reason:
    there is no central item-move path to hook (Position is assigned directly
    on hot paths such as ship movement).

[2026-06-10] - Conference chat system (Wave 79)
----------------------------------------

ENGINE - chat:
  - The UO conference chat system is implemented. ChatEngine holds channels
    and membership (one channel per member; ad-hoc channels disappear when
    emptied, the static "General" channel survives). Opening the chat window
    (0xB5) accepts the character's name as the chat handle and sends the
    channel list; the client then auto-joins "General".
  - Incoming 0xB3 chat actions are parsed and handled: talk (0x61, broadcast
    to channel members), join (0x62 — channel name arrives wrapped in quote
    characters, optional password stripped), create channel (0x63), leave
    (0x43). Disconnect drops the membership so channels hold no stale entries.
  - Outgoing 0xB2 chat messages cover the subcommands the client renders:
    create/remove channel, username accepted, add/remove user, clear users,
    joined/left channel, channel message. The byte layout (cmd + 4 reserved
    bytes + null-terminated BE-unicode strings) is verified in tests against
    the exact ClassicUO parser shape. The T2A feature bit that enables the
    client chat button was already sent at login.

[2026-06-09] - Script console compat verbs, drag-release verbs, trigger backlog closure (Wave 78)
----------------------------------------

SCRIPTING - console verbs:
  - DIALOGCLOSE closes the named open script dialog for real: open dialogs are
    tracked server-side (name → gump id), the close sends 0xBF sub 0x04 and
    drops the tracking; ISDIALOGOPEN.* now answers from that registry instead
    of a constant 0. BYE ends the NPC interaction (closes open script dialogs,
    clears the dialog subject). BUY opens the vendor buy list — the dialog
    subject when it is a vendor NPC, otherwise the nearest vendor in range.
  - Character BOUNCE/DROP act on the dragged item (the DRAGGING state set by
    the pickup packet): BOUNCE returns it to the backpack, DROP releases it at
    the character's feet; both cancel the client drag cursor with 0x27 (new
    PacketPickupFailed writer). Item FIXWEIGHT refreshes the client view
    (weight is already computed on demand).

ENGINE - triggers:
  - @HitIgnore is implemented: AttackerRecord gained an Ignored flag, scripts
    control it through ATTACKER.n.IGNORE (read/write), and a hit landed by an
    ignored attacker fires @HitIgnore on the victim (RETURN 1 clears the flag).
  - @Targon_Cancel fires when the player dismisses a target cursor.
  - @ToolTip (char) and @Tooltip (item) fire on single click ahead of @Click,
    IsTrigUsed-gated since single click is a hot path.
  - @UserQuestArrowClick fires from 0xBF sub 0x07 (newly known subcommand).
  - @UserBugReport fires from the 0xF4 crash report.
  - 0xFA (Ultima Store button) and 0xB5 (chat window open) gained packet
    handlers that fire @UserUltimaStoreButton / @UserGlobalChatButton.
  - @UserExWalkLimit fires when the walk token bucket runs dry
    (IsTrigUsed-gated — movement rejects can storm).
  - Still deferred with reasons recorded in the guardrail: UserMailBag /
    UserSpecialMove (no carrier packets in the supported protocol set),
    NPCLostTeleport (leashed NPCs walk home; the AI decision stage is
    parallel), NPCSeeWantItem (covered by @NPCLookAtItem). The sector ambient
    wind sound inventory item was dropped after checking the Source-X
    reference: CSector has no such sound logic — the item was speculative.

[2026-06-09] - Custom house foundation placement and design walk geometry (Wave 77)
----------------------------------------

ENGINE - custom housing:
  - Customizable foundation placement: a house deed carrying TAG.CUSTOMHOUSE
    places the multi as a MultiCustom foundation (PlaceHouse customFoundation
    path) with an empty committed design at revision 1. Unlike regular house
    placement, no real component items are materialized — the client renders
    the foundation multi and the committed design from the 0xD8 stream, so
    nothing double-renders.
  - Committed designs are now server-side walk geometry: WalkCheck virtualizes
    the DESIGN_n tiles of a MultiCustom item the same way it virtualizes
    multi.mul components (surface/bridge/impassable tile flags respected,
    per-tile Z honored for upper stories). The design lookup is served by a
    revision-keyed cache on CustomHousingEngine — a design commit bumps
    DESIGN_REVISION, which invalidates the cache on the next step check. The
    cache is concurrent because the parallel NPC-pathfinding stage consults
    WalkCheck too.

[2026-06-09] - Guild channel delivery, custom house design editor, script verb completeness (Wave 76)
----------------------------------------

ENGINE - speech:
  - Guild/alliance channel chat is now delivered. The channel event carries the
    recipient (it previously invoked with no recipient, so nothing could be
    routed), the host subscribes it and sends 0xAE with talk type 0xD/0xE per
    member, the speaker gets the server echo, and alliance delivery requires a
    mutual (both-sides declared) alliance. Guild/alliance lines are no longer
    spatially broadcast to bystanders near the speaker.

ENGINE - custom housing:
  - The house design editor is implemented end to end. Incoming 0xD7 encoded
    commands now carry their payload (it was previously discarded after the
    subcommand) and are handled: Build, Delete, Stairs, Roof, RoofDelete, Level,
    Clear, Backup, Restore, Sync, Revert, Commit, Close. A per-character design
    session holds the working design; Commit persists it as DESIGN_n tags on the
    multi item (same format the script ADDITEM verb writes) and bumps
    DESIGN_REVISION.
  - Outgoing design packets: 0xD8 design stream (zlib-compressed mode-0 planes,
    byte layout verified against the client parser, large designs split across
    planes), 0xBF 0x1D revision notice, 0xBF 0x20 customization mode on/off.
    The 0xBF 0x1E design query is now a known subcommand answered from the
    committed design. The house sign gump gained a "Customize House" entry for
    owners/co-owners, and a committed design broadcasts the new revision to
    nearby clients so they re-query.
  - @HouseDesignCommit and @HouseDesignExit now fire (Commit/Close paths).

ENGINE - experience:
  - Experience/level runtime: ChangeExperience routes every EXP change (script
    writes included) through @ExpChange (ARGN1 adjustable, RETURN 1 cancels);
    crossing a level threshold fires @ExpLevelChange with the new level. Killing
    an NPC awards the victim's EXP value to the killer — characters without EXP
    grant nothing, so the system stays inert unless definitions/scripts assign
    experience. Level curve is configurable (LevelNextAt step, linear or
    doubling mode).

ENGINE - help menu:
  - The help-menu buttons do real work now: "stuck" teleports to a safe town
    spot and is refused while jailed or in combat; "page" opens a text-entry
    gump routed through the .PAGE command path (staff broadcast + a capped
    recent-page log); "page list" shows recent pages (staff see all, players
    their own).

ENGINE - client packets:
  - 0xA5 web link writer added, exposed as the WEBLINK script verb and a
    "Visit Web Page" button on the guild stone gump when the guild has a web
    URL set.
  - Ground-drop sound is item-aware: gold coins play the amount-scaled coin
    sounds (0x2E4..0x2E6) instead of the generic 0x42.
  - @UserVirtue (0xBF 0x2C) and @UserKRToolbar (0xBF 0x24) now fire.

SCRIPTING - verbs:
  - Item OPEN opens the container on the acting client with script authority;
    DCLICK/USE replay the real client double-click path (doors, potions,
    containers). Character DISMOUNT performs a full dismount through the mount
    engine (client path fires @Dismount and refreshes the rider; flag-clear
    fallback remains for headless runs).
  - Object TRIGGER fires the named trigger through the dispatcher's new by-name
    path, so custom trigger names defined only in EVENTS/TEVENTS work. FIX
    re-seats the object Z on the terrain surface. TAGLIST (character, region,
    room) dumps tags to the invoking console. Region/Room ALLCLIENTS delivers a
    sysmessage or runs a script function for every online client character in
    the area.

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - Unimplemented SERV.* verbs are no longer silent: first use of each verb is
    warn-logged (debug afterwards) and GM-level callers get an in-game notice.
  - FILE.OPEN failures report their reason through a host-wired diagnostic sink
    instead of being swallowed; bare catch blocks in the recording loader,
    host IPC connect retry and stable-pet tag parser were narrowed to the
    expected exception types.

INTERNAL:
  - GameWorld now documents its threading contract (single-writer plain
    collections vs concurrent dirty/region caches; parallel stages must queue
    intents for the serial phase). Stub inventory updated; remaining gaps are
    marked as deliberate deferrals with reasons.

[2026-06-07] - Pet-command speech gating, skin hue preserved across death/resurrect (Wave 75)
----------------------------------------

ENGINE - speech:
  - The pet-command parser no longer treats every two-word line as "<pet name>
    <command>"; it only engages when the line actually starts with a pet command
    verb, so ordinary two-word speech no longer prints the "Sorry" pet-failure
    message when the speaker has no pet.

ENGINE - death / resurrect:
  - Skin hue is preserved across death. The living body's skin hue is captured into
    OSkin before the death spell-cleanup runs, and a dead character logging in keeps
    that hue instead of losing it when switching to the ghost hue. Fixes the
    character staying grey/default-hued after resurrect.

ENGINE - NPC definitions:
  - CHARDEF skill ranges (WRESTLING, TACTICS, MAGERY, etc.) are now parsed and
    rolled onto the character on spawn / applyDefName (CharDefHelper
    ApplyNpcDefinitionSkills, clamped 0..1200). Definition TAG defs are applied to
    the runtime character too (ApplyNpcDefinitionTags), so AI that reads BREATH.*,
    THROWOBJ, THROWDAM, THROWRANGE for dragon/breath/throw special attacks now sees
    the values from the definition (previously the AI read tags that were never set).

ENGINE - combat:
  - Hit-chance gained a stat-based fallback for NPCs whose weapon skill or Tactics
    is 0: the inferred value is clamp(max(Str,Dex)*10, 250..1000). It only applies
    to non-player attackers and weapon skills, so player accuracy is unchanged. This
    stops skill-less NPC definitions from missing almost every swing.

SCRIPTING - definition parsing:
  - Fixed bare Sphere hex parsing in ItemDef and CharDef: values like 0F5E / 013B
    are no longer mistaken for decimal, and the {min max} form is parsed for item
    damage/range. This also closes a path where an item definition could load with
    wrong metadata (e.g. a sword mis-typed so it emitted the bow/arrow shoot sound).

HOST / PANEL / BUILD:
  - Replaced the in-app panel update with a single update.cmd / update.ps1, run
    with the server stopped: git pull --ff-only -> full build.ps1 (panel + Server +
    Host) -> copy the build output into the run (deploy) folder -> relaunch
    SphereNet.Host. Running as a separate process it can replace SphereNet.Host.exe
    too, which the in-app updater could not. The source repo comes from sphere.ini
    AppUpdateRepoDir (or -RepoDir); the deploy folder defaults to the script's own
    folder (or -DeployDir) and the build-output==deploy case skips the copy.
    build.ps1 copies update.* into the build output so a deploy folder self-updates.
  - Removed the in-app UpdateService, POST /api/update/run, GET /api/update/status,
    the Settings "System Update" card and the AutoUpdate startup check.
    AppUpdateRepoDir is now read only by update.ps1; the AutoUpdate key is gone.

ENGINE - sound / visual / effects:
  - Added 0xC0 PacketEffectHued, 0xC7 PacketEffectParticle and 0x23
    PacketDragAnimation outgoing packets.
  - ObjBase.SOUND / EFFECT are no longer stubs: item- and char-based script
    commands now broadcast to nearby clients. Character SOUND / EFFECT route through
    the shared ObjBase path, and FACE now triggers a 0x77 facing broadcast.
  - Pickup and ground-drop emit the 0x23 drag animation, filtered to clients that
    support it (KR / Enhanced / SA).
  - Region change resends GlobalLight, a silent Season and Weather to the client.

ENGINE - combat & movement:
  - NPC walk steps now always face the step direction (surround step, Wander, flee
    and move-away paths previously moved without setting Direction, so the 0x77 move
    mismatched the tile delta and the client snapped the NPC). The surround step is
    also constrained to tiles adjacent to the NPC, so it can no longer jump two
    tiles in one move ("NPC teleport" during combat).
  - A player turning to face a combat target now also updates the attacker's own
    client (0x20 PlayerUpdate + walk-seq reset), mirroring Source-X
    CChar::UpdateMove -> addPlayerView/addPlayerUpdate, so in top-down view the
    avatar visibly faces the target instead of only nearby observers seeing it.

ENGINE - items & visuals:
  - Ground items carry a facing direction: 0x1A and 0xF3 world-item packets send it,
    the per-client known-item cache tracks it, and WorldSaver persists DIR. Dropping
    separate (non-stacking) items on one tile scatters their facing by the tile's
    existing item count instead of every drop landing on Direction=1.
  - A worn item previously known to a client as a ground item is no longer
    0x1D-deleted by the per-tick view delta (the 0x2E worn packet already re-homes
    it) - fixes worn items vanishing until a resync after a GM recolour/property edit.
  - GM x-verbs on item targets (.xcolor / .xid / ...) refresh the item visual for
    all observers; previously only COLOR (via OnVisualUpdate) and character targets
    refreshed.

ENGINE - persistence:
  - Periodic world auto-save: sphere.ini SavePeriod (minutes, 0 = off) now drives a
    save on the main loop. It was read into config but never used; with
    auto-save-on-shutdown disabled, the server never saved on its own.

CONFIG:
  - Notoriety name hues (ColorNoto*): a configured 0 falls back to the built-in
    default instead of rendering the single-click name label black; invis/hidden
    hues keep an explicit 0. sphere.ini docs corrected (hue is hex; 0 = default) and
    the duplicate/incorrectly-"unimplemented" block removed.

LOGGING:
  - Demoted [move_z_delta] (per-step) and [tick_stats] / [gc_stats] (every 30s) from
    INFO to DEBUG so a debug-off console stays quiet; they reappear when packet or
    script debug raises the level. [slow_tick] stays a warning.

[2026-06-06] - Panel update service, smelt/spell item triggers, configurable hues (Wave 72)
----------------------------------------

HOST / PANEL:
  - Added UpdateService and the POST /api/update/run + GET /api/update/status
    endpoints, surfaced as a "System Update / Update from GitHub" card on the
    Settings page (state and last log lines shown live). The update runs git
    status, git pull --ff-only, server save, server stop, build.ps1 -ServerOnly,
    then server start, in that order.
  - build.ps1 gained a -ServerOnly switch that publishes only SphereNet.Server and
    copies the panel static files, leaving the running (and therefore locked)
    SphereNet.Host.exe untouched so the panel can update itself.

TRIGGERS:
  - @Smelt: double-clicking ore now prompts for a forge target and fires @Smelt
    (N1 = ore amount, O1 = forge, S1 = smelt message) before the native smelt;
    RETURN 1 cancels it. On success the ore stack is consumed and an iron ingot
    stack is added to the backpack (or dropped if there is no pack), firing
    @Create on the result.
  - Item-targeted @SpellEffect: Mark, Recall/Gate rune travel, Dispel Field and
    generic TargObj item targets now fire @SpellEffect (O1 = caster, N1 = spell id,
    S1 = spell name); RETURN 1 suppresses the native behaviour. SpellEngine takes
    a TriggerDispatcher, wired from Program.

CONFIG:
  - Notoriety and invisibility hues are configurable via sphere.ini: ColorNotoGood,
    ColorNotoGoodNPC, ColorNotoGuildSame, ColorNotoNeutral, ColorNotoCriminal,
    ColorNotoGuildWar, ColorNotoEvil, ColorNotoInvul, ColorNotoInvulGameMaster,
    ColorNotoDefault, ColorInvisItem, ColorInvis, ColorInvisSpell, ColorHidden.
    NotoToHue now resolves through the loaded NotorietyHueSettings, distinguishing
    NPC innocents (GoodNpc) and GM-level invulnerables (InvulGameMaster). Hue keys
    parse hex; PetsInheritNotoriety and AdvancedLos keys are also read. Hex/decimal
    parsing handled by GetHue / GetIntOrHex helpers.

NPC AI:
  - Consolidated every NPC move/wander/chase/path-step gate into a single
    CanNpcMoveTo check: negative-coordinate guard, tile passability, static-block
    items and occupying characters, all skipped when the NPC can pass walls
    (hidden/invisible staff above the occupied tile do not block).

NETWORK:
  - 0xBE now distinguishes the modern length-prefixed assist/version packet from
    the legacy 5-byte uint form, via TryGetLegacyAssistPacketLength: implausible
    declared lengths followed by a real packet boundary are treated as the legacy
    form so following movement packets are not stranded behind a phantom partial.
  - 0xD9 Hardware Info length corrected to 0x010C (268 bytes total).

SCRIPTING:
  - SRC-aware dialog verb dispatch: UID.<obj>.DIALOG and similar verbs now route
    through _REF_EXEC_AS (srcUid|targetUid|command|args) when SRC is known, so
    client-bound verbs open on SRC's client while the UID object stays the dialog
    subject. HandleDialogCommand / OpenNamedDialog thread the subject through.
  - TriggerRunner stops a trigger body at any following ON= key (not only @-named
    triggers), so ON=*keyword* speech blocks no longer bleed sibling responses
    into one spoken line.

[2026-06-06] - Pickup-source trigger variants (@Pickup_Self / @Pickup_Stack) (Wave 71)
----------------------------------------

TRIGGERS:
  - HandleItemPickup now selects the pickup-source trigger by where the item is
    taken from, via SelectPickupTrigger: Self (dragged off the picker's own
    equipment layers), Stack (a partial amount split out of a larger stack), Pack
    (from inside a container), Ground (loose on the ground). The equip check runs
    before the container check, since equipped items report ContainedIn = the
    wearer and previously fired @Pickup_Pack by mistake. RETURN 1 cancels the
    pickup in every case.

[2026-06-06] - NPC first-sight perception (@NPCSeeNewPlayer) (Wave 70)
----------------------------------------

TRIGGERS:
  - Added per-NPC seen-player memory and wired @NPCSeeNewPlayer.
    Character.SeeNewPlayer records a perceived player and fires the trigger only on
    a first sighting (the per-player timer refreshes on continued sight, so a
    player standing nearby is not re-greeted; it fires again after the player
    leaves for longer than the TTL and returns). NpcAI scans nearby visible players
    each tick, gated on the Character.OnNpcSeeNewPlayer hook (installed only when a
    script hooks the trigger) plus a throttle, so the range scan is skipped when
    unused. O1 = the newly-seen player. Reset in ResetEngineStatics.

    player and NPC speech). Each value is a comma-separated list of defnames.
