[2026-06-06] - Animation client-type gating, NPC facing, tooltip and regen parity (Wave 59)
----------------------------------------

ANIMATION:
  - The body-agnostic 0xE2 new-animation packet is now sent only to KR and
    Enhanced clients; Classic/ClassicUO clients receive the legacy 0x6E packet
    even when their version reports High Seas or newer. Selection switched from
    SupportsHighSeas to the parsed client type. Added NetState
    IsKingdomRebornClient / IsEnhancedClient.

NPC AI:
  - NPC attacks no longer emit a synthetic 0x77 MobileMoving on every hit/miss.
    A facing update is broadcast only when the swing actually changes the NPC's
    direction (OnNpcFacingChanged -> BroadcastFacingUpdate), matching Source-X.

TOOLTIP:
  - A 0xD6 full property-list response is no longer followed by a 0xDC revision
    packet (Source-X sends only the requested list). ToolTipMode default is now
    1 (0=off, 1=revision/request, 2=force full) and a ToolTipCache setting was
    added; set TOOLTIPMODE=0 to disable tooltips entirely.

REGEN:
  - HP/stam/mana regeneration intervals derive from the configured REGEN values
    (tenths of a second) instead of hard-coded periods. The HP regen no longer
    grants an extra +1 per tick for STR > 50; it heals 1 per interval while fed.

[2026-06-06] - Client speed mode (0xBF sub 0x26) parity (Wave 58)
----------------------------------------

PROTOCOL / PACKET:
  - Added 0xBF sub 0x26 (PacketSpeedMode) outgoing packet, carrying the client
    movement speed mode byte.

MOVEMENT:
  - SPEEDMODE bit 0 makes a foot character move at the mounted cadence
    (walk/run 200/100ms instead of 400/200ms), matching Source-X Event_Walk.
    Added a speedMode-aware GetMoveDelay overload; the per-step move delay now
    derives from the character's SpeedMode.
  - The speed-hack detector treats a speed-mode character as mounted so the
    faster cadence is not flagged as a violation or counted as a burst.
  - SendSpeedMode pushes the current mode to the active client and resets the
    walk validator (token/throttle state) so the new cadence applies cleanly.

GM / COMMANDS:
  - SPEEDMODE is a GM command (".speedmode <n>"); it sets the property and echoes
    the resulting value.
  - The mode is (re)sent to the owning client on login and whenever SpeedMode
    changes via a command or a .set property edit, so client and server agree on
    cadence without a relog.

[2026-06-05] - Combat attack handshake parity and NPC special-attack facing (Wave 57)
----------------------------------------

PROTOCOL / PACKET:
  - Added 0x2F (combat swing/fight notification: attacker + defender serials)
    and 0xAA (attack target confirmation; serial 0 means refused) outgoing
    packets.

COMBAT:
  - Attack requests now reply with an accept/refuse handshake. A refused attack
    (target 0/self, a hidden staff target, region/PvP block, or an Attack /
    CombatStart trigger returning true) sends 0xAA=0; an accepted attack sends
    0x2F Swing followed by 0xAA carrying the target serial.
  - War mode is entered and the fight target is set only on an accepted attack.
    Previously the request forced war mode (and assigned FightTarget) up front,
    before the rejection checks, so a refused attack still flipped the attacker
    into war mode and left a stale target.

NPC AI:
  - Breath and throw special attacks turn the NPC to face the target and
    broadcast a 0x77 direction update before emitting the effect, so the
    projectile/breath originates from the correct facing instead of the NPC's
    previous direction (FaceAndBroadcastToward).

[2026-06-05] - Turn-in-place movement parity, walk-token config fix, reject diagnostics (Wave 56)
----------------------------------------

MOVEMENT:
  - Turn-in-place parity: a 0x02 walk request whose direction differs from the
    character's current facing is now handled as a pure turn, not a tile step.
    It only updates facing, sends 0x22 MoveAck, and broadcasts 0x77, bypassing
    the throttle, walk-token bucket, collision and Z resolution. Previously such
    a packet advanced the character one tile, so the client's direction-change
    "doublet" packets (~31-47ms apart while running) produced an extra server
    step, a momentary animation hitch, and a sideways snap near stairs/walls.
  - Walk-token bucket is honored as documented and no longer starves movement on
    a low setting: WalkBuffer is the bucket capacity (allowed step burst) and
    WalkRegen is tokens-per-SECOND (a rate, not a per-step tick period). A
    running mover needs ~5 steps/s, so a regen below that drained the bucket and
    rejected legitimate steps as walk_buffer, snapping the client back into a
    repeated stutter. Config restored to working values (75 / 25) and the stale
    "loaded but unused" comments corrected. Validate() now warns when WalkRegen
    or WalkBuffer is set below running speed.
  - Post-reject in-flight steps (seq > 1 arriving after a reject reset
    WalkSequence to 0) are dropped silently — no extra 0x21 reject and no 0x20
    DrawPlayer redraw. Echoing either made the client ClearSteps and snap again,
    cascading into a client resync (the visible walking "teleport"/flash). The
    fixed post-reject absorb window (MoveRejectResyncMs) is disabled accordingly.
  - GM/staff movement is routed through the movement queue instead of an
    immediate step, so the client's transition doublet is paced to the natural
    cadence; the throttle is still skipped for staff, so GM is smoothed but never
    throttle-rejected. Movement speed is unchanged.
  - Queued movement is drained every main-loop iteration (not only on the 50ms
    tick), so the ack/reject flushes in the same iteration as input. The per-step
    _nextMoveTime gate still paces the real drain, so this only cuts latency for
    the client's 5-step budget on fast/stair sections; it does not raise speed.

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - Movement rejections are classified into a normalized cause (throttle,
    walk_buffer, descent_cap, impassable_static, no_surface, z_window,
    diagonal_edge, mob_block, seq_mismatch, queue_full, stale) and accumulated
    into a per-session [move_reject_tally] summary, so the dominant disagreement
    class over a walking session can be aimed instead of guessed. Pure logging.

[2026-06-03] - Packet-era compatibility, version-aware animation, movement & send-priority fixes (Wave 54)
----------------------------------------

PROTOCOL / PACKET:
  - 0x00 Create Character is always 104 bytes. Removed a version-gated
    104/106 length override (the 106-byte form is a distinct opcode, 0xF8);
    treating 0x00 as 106 for modern clients over-read and desynced the stream.
    Removed the now-unused, incorrectly-computed IsClientPost70180 flag.
  - Unregistered modern opcodes (0xF1/F2/F7/F9/FA/FB/D0/DD/E0) are consumed by
    their declared framing and ignored without desync; unknown-opcode logging
    is rate-limited to once per opcode per connection (ShouldLogUnknownOpcode).
  - 0xD7 encoded command (custom-house design editor) decoupled from the 0xBF
    extended-command dispatch: their subcommand IDs overlap (encoded Build 0x06
    vs party 0x06, Roof 0x13 vs context-menu, Revert 0x1A vs stat-lock), so a
    shared table mis-routed house actions into unrelated handlers. Custom-house
    design actions are now safely rejected/ignored (editor not yet implemented).
    Added EncodedCommandRegistry documenting the subcommand set.

ANIMATION:
  - 0xE2 new-animation packet put to use with per-recipient client-version
    selection: High Seas+ clients receive the body-agnostic 0xE2 gesture while
    older clients keep the legacy 0x6E action index. Added NewAnimationGesture
    enum; combat swing/get-hit/miss (player and NPC) route through the shared
    version-aware broadcast.

MOVEMENT:
  - Walking/running on foot no longer drains stamina (Source-X parity: only
    shoving past a mobile costs stamina; the per-step run drain was incorrect).
  - Land-tile walkability matches the client: only impassable WET (water) land
    blocks a walker. Dry impassable slope/mountain terrain is walkable again;
    blocking it desynced from the client and rubber-banded movement beside
    stairs and slopes.
  - Single-step Z descents beyond MaxDescendZ (11) are rejected so a mover stops
    at a cliff edge instead of plunging; ordinary stair/slope steps (<= ~2
    risers) are unaffected. Climbing is unchanged.

NETWORK (send priority):
  - Source-X packet-priority model: outgoing packets are classified
    (Idle/Low/Normal/High/Highest) by PacketPriorityClassifier and NetState
    drains its queues Highest -> Idle each flush. Movement ack/reject
    (0x21/0x22) and auth now lead bulk world/UI traffic, so a running client no
    longer waits on step confirmations and over-predicts.
  - The post-reject resync window no longer echoes a 0x21 per buffered step.
    Echoing one reject per in-flight step made the client resend (rejected
    again) in a tight feedback storm on low-latency links that froze the player
    and read as a teleport. Stale steps inside the window are absorbed; if the
    client still sends seq>1 after the window, the server sends a fresh
    corrective reject + self redraw to break the walk-sequence deadlock.

MOUNT / USE:
  - Double-clicking a mount NPC no longer fails silently when the mount attempt
    is rejected; the player now gets the mount-failed message. The mount sound
    is broadcast only after a successful mount.

TESTS:
  - Added era-boundary (7.0.18-7.0.30 for 0x00/0xF8, 0x08 14/15 grid index),
    unregistered-opcode robustness, custom-house reject, animation
    version-selection, land-block rule, packet-priority, and stale
    walk-sequence recovery tests. Full suite green (583).

[2026-06-01] - Bot combat/magic buff + MageBot; gameplay robustness pass (Wave 53)
----------------------------------------

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - Bot accounts now receive a combat/magic buff on login (Str/Dex/Int 100,
    Wrestling/Tactics/Anatomy/Magery/EvalInt/Healing maxed) so test bots can
    actually deal damage and cast — newbie stats can't out-damage monsters. Bot
    accounts are ephemeral; re-applied each login; gated on IsBotAccountName.
  - Added MageBot (reactive spellcaster: finds the nearest monster and casts an
    offensive spell via the cast→target flow) + wired into BotBehavior/
    CreateRoleBehavior and the --botrunner parser ("mage").

  Findings: across combat, mage and chaos bot runs against the scripted world +
  hostile NPCs — ZERO server exceptions, crashes, wire corruption or bot
  anomalies. The player melee/damage path was read and verified correct
  (unarmed uses Wrestling -> ~85% hit vs an unskilled mob, real Str-scaled damage
  with Tactics/Anatomy bonus). No server-side gameplay bug was found.
  Caveat: reliably making bots KILL mobs is a harness positioning/movement
  problem, not a server one — clustered bots are packed and can't path to a
  target, while spread bots end up isolated from the mob hotspots, so few swings
  land. Tuning bot/mob co-location (or a server-side bot stat boost plus a
  dedicated "skirmish" spawn) is the open item for end-to-end combat-correctness
  bot tests; the code paths themselves are exercised and robust.

[2026-06-01] - Reactive bot infrastructure: per-bot receive loop (Wave 52)
----------------------------------------

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - Each bot now runs a dedicated background receive loop (ReceiveLoopAsync) that
    is the sole socket reader once the bot is playing: it continuously reads
    packets, updates the world model and completes pending actions. Previously
    the only reader was a drain between behavior iterations, and WaitResult-based
    actions stalled ~1 s with a stale world — so combat/skill bots fired blind.
    Now the bot's world model stays current and WaitResult returns promptly, so
    behaviors actually REACT to what they see.
  - Thread-safety for the new cross-thread access: BotWorldModel.SyncRoot guards
    the mobile/item dictionaries (FindNearest/RemoveStale and the receive-loop
    mutations in ProcessIncomingPacket); BotActionApi guards _waitKind/
    _pendingAction with a lock (the TCS already uses RunContinuationsAsynchronously
    so completions never run inline under a lock). Behavior loops no longer drain
    the socket themselves (would be a second reader on the stream).

  Verified: 300 combat bots clustered among 2,000 hostile NPCs now genuinely
  react — pps_in ~1,000-1,700 and recv climbing into the hundreds of thousands
  (vs ~10/bot frozen before), bots attack what they see. Zero server exceptions
  and zero bot anomalies across the run; server tick ~1-1.5 ms. (Newbie bot
  characters don't out-damage 50-HP monsters, so mobs don't die — realistic weak
  combat, not a bug.) This is contained to the bot harness; the server/wire is
  untouched. Confirms the combat code path is robust under reactive load and
  gives a foundation for richer bot gameplay tests.

[2026-06-01] - Bot gameplay fuzzing pass + reactive-behavior groundwork (Wave 51)
----------------------------------------

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - The --botrunner behavior parser accepts the full set: walk, combat, idle,
    smart, full, cluster, skill, loot, vendor, social, chaos.
  - CombatBot reworked to one decision per call (returns each iteration) so the
    runner loop drains incoming between calls, matching the ClusterBot fix.

  Robustness result: 200 chaos bots firing ~24k random gameplay actions
  (attack / skill / double-click / pick-up / target / speech / war-mode, with
  random serials) plus a 300-combat run against a scripted world + 2,000 hostile
  NPCs produced ZERO server exceptions / crashes / wire corruption. The gameplay
  packet handlers are robust against fuzzed and invalid input. One handled edge
  case observed: a bot stepping on a telepad mid-move triggered a script
  teleport, which the server detected and suppressed the MoveAck for (correct).

  Honest limitation found: the bot client has no continuous background socket
  reader. It only reads between behavior iterations, and WaitResult-based actions
  (move/attack) stall ~1 s each waiting for a response that nothing reads during
  the action — so a combat/skill bot's world model never stays current and it
  fires largely blind (cannot reliably see/target real monsters). The
  one-iteration rework helps speak-only bots (ClusterBot) but not WaitResult-
  heavy ones. Genuinely REACTIVE bot gameplay (and outcome-verifying correctness
  tests) needs a per-bot background receive loop + assertions — a real refactor.
  Gameplay correctness is meanwhile covered by the 529 unit tests; bots remain
  best for load/stress (validated) and crash fuzzing (validated, zero crashes).

[2026-06-01] - Configurable world-loop tick interval (Wave 50)
----------------------------------------

CONFIG:
  - The world-loop tick interval is no longer hardcoded to 50 ms. New sphere.ini
    key ServerTickMs (default 50 = 20 ticks/s, clamped to [20,250]) sets it.
    Raising it (e.g. 100 = 10 ticks/s) doubles the per-tick budget for very heavy
    active-AI loads at the cost of coarser world-sim timing — which UO's
    movement (200-400 ms/step) and combat (1-4 s swings) tolerate easily. Network
    I/O is NOT gated by this (it runs every main-loop iteration), so the tick
    rate affects world simulation granularity, not packet latency.
    Verified: ServerTickMs=100 yields ~301 ticks per 30 s window (10 Hz) vs ~601
    at the default 50 ms (20 Hz). Default behavior is unchanged.

[2026-06-01] - Anchored cluster bot + conclusive out-of-process soak (Wave 49)
----------------------------------------

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - ClusterBot now does ONE iteration per call and returns, instead of looping
    forever internally. The runner's behavior loop drains incoming packets
    between calls, so a speak-only bot that never returned never read its socket;
    its inbound backed up, the server saw the connection as hopelessly behind and
    shed everything bound for it. Returning each iteration lets the bot consume
    the broadcast flood it generates. It also anchors each bot to its spawn tile
    (Radius 6) so the fleet stays clustered instead of dispersing.
  - Cluster placement is decided SERVER-side (BotSpawnLocationProvider -> the
    server's BotEngine), so clustering an out-of-process fleet must be configured
    on the server: new --botcity <name> and --botcluster flags pack bot logins
    around a town. (--trustloopback from Wave 48 covers the connection filter.)
  - The runner logs periodic active/pps stats so bot drop-off and real load are
    visible.

  Conclusive soak (server alone in its own process, 1,000 cluster bots from a
  separate --botrunner process, all anchored + speaking in one town):
    - 1,000/1,000 bots stay connected; they actually receive and drain the
      broadcast flood (pps_in a few thousand/s, recv climbing into the millions).
    - Server holds ~5 ms avg tick (p95 ~50 ms), 20 Hz, players=1000, ZERO
      shedding, ZERO backpressure-cap disconnects, ZERO wire corruption; RSS
      ~1.3 GB, ~2 cores.
    - This confirms the earlier IN-PROCESS cluster collapse (1,000 -> ~60, then
      millions shed) was a harness artifact: in-process the bots were CPU-starved
      and couldn't drain, so the server's per-connection buffers backed up. With
      the bots in their own process they drain fine and the server handles 1,000
      clustered, broadcasting clients cleanly.
    - Caveat: broadcast fan-out was moderate (each speech reached a neighbourhood,
      not all 1,000 — spawn radius + anchor drift), so this is a solid sustained
      soak, not the absolute densest worst case. Same machine still shares cores.

[2026-06-01] - Out-of-process bot load runner + soak finding (Wave 48)
----------------------------------------

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - The server exe gains a --botrunner <host> <port> <count> <behavior> [city]
    mode that runs ONLY the bot engine against a separately-running server, so
    the load generator has its own process (own thread pool + GC) and does not
    contend with the server — removing the in-process CPU-contention artifact
    that confounded the cluster measurements.
  - --trustloopback skips the connection rate-limit/accept filter for loopback
    clients (the flood filter otherwise rejects an out-of-process runner opening
    ~1,000 connections from 127.0.0.1; the in-process path bypassed it via
    BotEngine bot-mode, which a separate process doesn't share).

  Soak finding (honest, partly inconclusive):
    - With the server isolated in its own process, 1,000 connected bots sit at
      ~1.2 ms avg tick (p95 ~2 ms), 20 Hz, zero shedding, zero disconnects, ~490
      MB server RSS. This strongly suggests the earlier IN-PROCESS cluster
      "load" (avg climbing to ~37 ms, millions shed) was dominated by harness
      CPU/GC contention — the bots and server fighting for one machine's cores
      and one GC — not genuine server broadcast cost.
    - Caveat: in this run the cluster bots were near-idle (runner used ~2 s CPU
      over the run), i.e. they did NOT reproduce the speech-broadcast flood, so
      the out-of-process broadcast path is not yet conclusively soak-tested. The
      load-generation behavior (keep the fleet clustered and actually sustaining
      the flood) needs another pass before the out-of-process broadcast numbers
      can be trusted. Same machine also still shares cores; true isolation needs
      a second machine.

[2026-06-01] - Fix async-send / interest-management interaction (Wave 47)
----------------------------------------

NETWORK (review fixes for Wave 46):
  - Interest management now sees the async backlog. The chatter-shed check keyed
    only on _sendQueue.Count, but in the async model the queue drains into the
    byte buffer each flush, so a slow client's real backlog lives in
    _outEnd-_outStart with a low queue count — chatter was never shed and the
    client instead hit the hard 512 KB cap and disconnected. Shedding now also
    triggers on byte pressure (outbound backlog > 256 KB), restoring graceful
    degradation in non-blocking mode.
  - The 512 KB cap is now enforced DURING append, before growing the buffer, so a
    huge queue / large gump / burst can't balloon the buffer past the cap in a
    single flush (worst-case memory is now genuinely bounded near the cap).
  - Receive() no longer treats a transient non-blocking WouldBlock/Interrupted as
    a lost connection (returns "no data" instead of disconnecting).
  - Cleaned the NetState nullability warning (byte[]? shared).

  Impact — this fixed more than the review notes: with chatter shed on byte
  pressure, the 1,000-bot one-screen flood now HOLDS all 1,000 clients at 20 Hz
  (~3 ms avg) with ZERO backpressure-cap disconnects, versus the earlier collapse
  to ~60. The earlier "attrition is pure CPU starvation, unchanged" conclusion
  was incomplete: the dominant cause was the un-shed speech flood (the bypassed
  interest management this fixes), not the bots' CPU. Peak RSS ~2.1 GB, zero wire
  corruption, zero final-flush errors. 529 tests pass.

[2026-06-01] - Non-blocking (async) game send (Wave 46)
----------------------------------------

NETWORK:
  - The game stream no longer uses a blocking Socket.Send. A slow client, a full
    OS send buffer, or a packet burst could previously block the flush thread
    that was serving it. The game socket is now set non-blocking on login, and
    FlushOutput accumulates compressed+encrypted bytes into a persistent
    per-connection buffer ([_outStart.._outEnd), stream-ordered) and drains only
    what the socket accepts (Send with out SocketError; WouldBlock leaves the
    remainder for the next flush). The server thread never blocks.
  - Backpressure: a connection buffering more than 512 KB of unsent bytes is
    hopelessly behind and is disconnected (bounds worst-case memory to
    ~maxClients * 512 KB). Clear() now does a best-effort final flush before
    shutdown so a graceful disconnect still delivers queued/pending data.
  - Design note: a synchronous non-blocking + per-tick retry model is used rather
    than SocketAsyncEventArgs/SendAsync — it reaches the same goal (no blocked
    thread) without completion-callback races, in-flight tracking and post-
    completion cleanup, which are the parts most likely to produce wire bugs
    worse than blocking. One active send per connection is inherent (flush is
    serial per connection), packet order is preserved (single ordered buffer),
    and the shared-broadcast/pre-compress path is unchanged. Toggle:
    NetState.NonBlockingGameSend (default on) keeps the old blocking path for A/B
    and rollback.

  Validated: 529 tests; 300-combat correctness run (zero wire corruption, zero
  backpressure trips — healthy connections drain fully each tick, tick
  unchanged); 1,000-bot cluster — zero corruption and zero final-flush errors
  across ~1,900 teardowns, the server never blocks, slow clients are shed cleanly
  by the byte cap instead of a blocking cascade, peak RSS ~2.1 GB (was ~4.6 GB at
  a 2 MB cap). The in-process bot cluster's eventual attrition is unchanged — it
  is the bots being CPU-starved, not the send path — but the failure mode is now
  bounded and non-blocking.

[2026-06-01] - Interest management: shed cosmetic chatter under pressure (Wave 45)
----------------------------------------

NETWORK:
  - When a connection's send queue backs up past a soft cap (1024, well below the
    4096 hard-overflow disconnect), low-priority cosmetic broadcasts to it —
    overhead speech (0xAE/0x1C) and sound (0x54) — are now shed instead of piling
    on toward an overflow disconnect. State-bearing packets (movement, status,
    combat results, corpses, gumps, ...) are never dropped. Classification is by
    opcode in EnqueueShared, so no broadcast call site changed; the shared
    packet's refcount is released for the shed recipient. A [gc_stats] "shed="
    counter reports how many were dropped per window.

  Behaviour / honesty:
    - Inert in normal play: a 300-combat + 2,000-hostile run sheds nothing
      (shed=0; queues never approach the cap) and tick/GC are unchanged — zero
      harm to normal gameplay.
    - Under the 1,000-bot one-screen flood it sheds ~165k chatter packets/window
      and the server logs zero overflows. It does NOT change that scenario's
      eventual bot attrition: that collapse is the in-process bots being
      CPU-starved (they share the machine with the server), not speech volume —
      shedding drops to 0 once the bots idle yet they still disconnect. So the
      mechanism is verified correct and is a standard graceful-degradation layer,
      but its real-world benefit (a genuine remote client draining less) is not
      measurable with the in-process bot harness, and per-client inbound recv
      capacity can't be cleanly measured here for the same reason.

[2026-06-01] - Parallel output flush (Wave 44)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE / NETWORK:
  - ProcessAllOutput flushed every connection serially. Each connection's flush
    touches only its own state (send queue, crypto, batch buffer, socket), so
    once shared broadcast payloads are precomputed they parallelize cleanly.
    Flushing now runs across cores (Parallel.ForEach, capped at ProcessorCount)
    when the active-connection count is above a threshold; below it, the serial
    path is kept to avoid parallel overhead.
  - To make this race-free, a shared broadcast packet's Huffman-compressed
    payload is now computed once in MarkShared (at broadcast time) instead of
    lazily on the first flush; FlushOutput only reads that cache, never writes
    it. The pool return already uses an interlocked refcount.
  - Measured: 300 combat + 2,000 hostile (parallel flush engaged) — p95 tick
    roughly halved (~72 ms -> ~40 ms) and average dropped (~14-21 ms -> ~10 ms)
    versus the serial flush, with zero wire-corruption, zero overflows. The
    1,000-bot dense cluster still holds all 1,000 at 20 Hz with zero overflows;
    its eventual attrition under the extreme flood is client-side (in-process
    bots cannot drain ~1,000 inbound speech packets/s each) and is unchanged by
    server-side flush parallelism, as expected.

[2026-06-01] - Shared path for movement broadcasts (Wave 43)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE / NETWORK:
  - BroadcastMoveNearby now uses the shared-broadcast path too (Wave 42). The
    move packet is identical for every recipient, so it is built/compressed once
    and reused; the per-recipient work that genuinely differs — sending a full
    appearance to a client that doesn't yet know the mover, and updating that
    client's known-position bookkeeping — is preserved exactly (appearance runs
    while collecting recipients, position update runs as the shared packet is
    enqueued).
  - Validated: 529 tests; a 300-combat + 2,000-hostile run (2,000 NPCs moving
    near players, exercising move broadcasts heavily) — 300/300 connected, zero
    malformed/underrun/parse anomalies, zero send-queue overflows, tick within
    the normal combat range.

[2026-05-31] - Shared broadcast packets — raise the dense-crowd wall (Wave 42)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE / NETWORK:
  - A broadcast event has identical bytes for every recipient, yet the old path
    rebuilt and re-Huffman-compressed the packet once per recipient. Broadcasts
    now build the packet ONCE, mark it shared, and enqueue the same buffer onto
    each recipient's queue. The first flush Huffman-compresses it and caches the
    (pre-encryption) bytes; the rest reuse the cache. For no-crypt game streams
    (the common case) the cached bytes are the final wire bytes and are appended
    directly — zero per-recipient compress/build. Crypted connections copy the
    cache into a per-connection scratch and encrypt that, so the shared cache is
    never mutated. PacketBuffer gained a refcount (returned to the pool only when
    the last recipient has flushed; unicast stays refcount 1, unchanged).
    BroadcastMoveNearby (per-recipient appearance side effects) is left on the
    old path for now.

  Validated:
    - 529 tests pass.
    - Correctness (300 combat + 2,000 hostile, no-crypt bots): 300/300 stay
      connected, zero malformed/underrun/parse anomalies, tick unchanged.
    - Dense-crowd wall (1,000 bots clustered in one town, all speaking): vs the
      Wave 41 baseline of ~919 send-queue overflows and a 1,000 -> ~31 cull, the
      server now logs ZERO overflows and holds all 1,000 at 20 Hz (~10 ms avg,
      Gen2 ~0). Residual client attrition under the extreme flood is downstream
      (the in-process bots can't drain ~1,000 inbound speech packets/s each;
      TCP backpressure), not the server send path. README updated.

[2026-05-31] - Cluster bot + measured the dense-crowd broadcast wall (Wave 41)
----------------------------------------

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - Added a Cluster bot behavior + cluster spawn (BotEngine packs the fleet
    around one city centre instead of scattering it across the city box) to
    reproduce the dense single-screen worst case. Use BOT <n> cluster:<city>.
    The bot speaks frequently: speech fans out to every bot in view, scaling
    ~N^2, and (unlike movement, which self-throttles because packed mobiles
    block each other) is not collision limited.

PERFORMANCE (finding):
  - 1,000 clustered, broadcasting bots saturate the per-client send queues. The
    server sheds load via send-queue-overflow disconnects rather than crashing
    or corrupting the wire: ~919 overflows, fleet culled 1,000 -> ~31 survivors,
    peak RSS ~1.8 GB then fell back, recovering to 20 Hz / ~0.4 ms. This is the
    practical ceiling for a single broadcasting screen and the known scaling
    wall. The change that would raise it: broadcast one shared serialized packet
    to all recipients instead of building a fresh packet per recipient. README
    updated with the measured wall.

[2026-05-31] - 1,000-client scaling test
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE:
  - Ran 1,000 live TCP bots across three scenarios (loopback). Connect: 1,000/
    1,000 in 25-30 s, zero failures, no disconnects/malformed packets.
      spread + low activity      : ~0.8 ms avg, Gen0 ~1/window, no blocking Gen2,
                                   ~1,750 pps out, 20 Hz
      active combat (+2,000 mob) : ~32-34 ms avg, p95 ~130 ms, p99 ~210-320 ms,
                                   ~19 Hz, ~1,950 pps out
  - Takeaway: cost tracks the active-combatant count, not the client count —
    1,000 spread players are nearly free, 1,000 all fighting at once sit at the
    50 ms budget edge. Forcing all 1,000 into one town did not reproduce the
    dense same-screen O(n^2) broadcast worst case (walker bots disperse and
    idle); that remains the known unmeasured scaling limit. README updated.

[2026-05-31] - Allocation-free pathfinder walkability check + benchmark (Wave 40)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE:
  - A deterministic allocation micro-benchmark for FindPath (fixed start/goal on
    open terrain, GC.GetAllocatedBytesForCurrentThread over many iterations)
    revealed that the dominant pathfinding allocation was NOT the A* scratch
    collections pooled in Wave 38 but the per-neighbour walkability check:
    Pathfinder.IsWalkable used the yield-based GetCharsInRange/GetItemsInRange
    range queries, allocating an iterator chain for every explored neighbour.
    On a 120-tile path that was ~486 KB/call.
  - Added GameWorld.IsPathTileBlockedByObject — an allocation-free single-tile
    blocker check that iterates the owning sector's char/item lists by index,
    mirroring the exact filtering of the old range queries. IsWalkable now calls
    it. Measured: ~486 KB/call -> ~1.7 KB/call (the remaining bytes are the
    returned path List, which is the caller's result). The benchmark is kept as
    a regression guard (asserts < 8 KB/call).

[2026-05-31] - Pool outgoing packet buffers (Wave 39)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE / NETWORK:
  - Every outgoing packet allocated a fresh byte[] backing array (PacketBuffer),
    the bulk of a packet's allocation. PacketBuffer now rents its backing array
    from ArrayPool<byte>.Shared and returns it once FlushOutput has consumed the
    bytes. This is safe because every outgoing PacketBuffer is built, queued and
    flushed exactly once — broadcasts build a fresh packet per recipient (they
    pass a PacketWriter, not a shared buffer), so no buffer is ever shared across
    send queues and no reference counting is needed. Buffers are also returned on
    the queue-overflow, not-in-use and disconnect paths so they never leak from
    the pool. Incoming/wrapped buffers (the byte[] constructor) are never pooled.
  - Growth (EnsureCapacity) stays within the pool: rent a larger array, copy,
    return the old one. Rent may hand back an oversized array; all readers use
    the logical Length (never _data.Length), so the slack is never observed.
  - Removes the per-packet byte[] allocation from the send hot path; the benefit
    scales with outbound packet volume (dense clusters / large battles). Verified
    correct under a sustained 300-bot run: 300/300 connected, 0 disconnects, no
    malformed/underrun packets — pooling does not corrupt the wire.

[2026-05-31] - Pool A* scratch collections; GC pressure telemetry (Wave 38)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE:
  - Pathfinder allocated a fresh PriorityQueue, HashSet and two Dictionaries on
    every FindPath call (each growing to thousands of entries, with the
    resize/rehash churn that implies). Under combat — where many NPCs path
    toward targets each tick — this was the dominant per-tick allocation. The
    four scratch collections are now pooled per worker thread ([ThreadStatic],
    cleared per call); FindPath runs inside the parallel NPC-decision phase, so
    the pool must be thread-local. The returned path List is still allocated
    fresh (it is the caller's result).
  - Added [gc_stats] telemetry alongside [tick_stats]: per-window allocation
    rate, Gen0/1/2 collection deltas, GC pause %, and managed heap. (Allocation
    bytes include in-process stress bots, so treat alloc as a relative gauge;
    Gen2 count and pause % are the GC-stall signal.)

  Measured (2,000 hostile monsters + 300 combat players, 30 s windows):
    alloc ~160-178 MB/s -> ~63-103 MB/s; Gen0 ~226-255 -> ~43-91 per window;
    Gen1 ~45-53 -> 2-14; avg tick ~21-29 ms -> ~10-14 ms; p95 ~85-119 ms ->
    ~46-51 ms; p99 ~127-167 ms -> ~83-85 ms. Lower tick time as well as GC,
    since pooling also removes the per-call collection resize/rehash work.

----------------------------------------

DIAGNOSTICS:
  - The STRESS console command takes an optional third token (STRESS [items]
    [npcs] mob): generated NPCs get a Monster brain and negative karma so they
    read as red (notoriety 6) and drive server-side target acquisition and
    retaliation, turning the stress harness into a combat-load generator. The
    default (no token) keeps the previous inert population; the in-game .STRESS
    path is unchanged.

PERFORMANCE (measured: .NET 10 Release, Server GC, 20 Hz / 50 ms tick, live
TCP bots, real script + MUL install; 30 s windows):

[2026-05-31] - Resolve CHARDEF CAN= flags via script DEFNAME tables (Wave 36)
----------------------------------------

SCRIPT:
  - Symbolic CAN= tokens (MT_RUN, MT_WALK, ...) are now resolved against the
    script's own [DEFNAME can_flags] table at parse time instead of a hardcoded
    map, so a server that redefines these constants is honored. The built-in
    MT_* map remains as a fallback for isolated parsing where no resolver is
    attached. ResourceHolder exposes TryResolveDefNameValue() for numeric
    defname constants and wires CharDef.DefNameResolver on construction.

[2026-05-31] - Fix symbolic CHARDEF CAN= flag parsing (Wave 35)
----------------------------------------

SCRIPT / NPC:
  - CHARDEF CAN= only accepted a numeric mask, so the standard symbolic form
    (CAN=MT_RUN|MT_WALK) failed to parse and left the creature with no movement
    capabilities at all (Can=None) — losing run/fly/swim/passwalls, which the
    pathfinder and tile-entry checks rely on. CAN= now parses the |-separated
    Sphere MT_* movement-type constants (the [DEFNAME can_flags] names) as well
    as a numeric mask. (Regression tests added; 527 passing.)

[2026-05-31] - NPC movement speed: Source-X DEX-scaled cadence (Wave 34)
----------------------------------------

NPC AI:
  - NPC step cadence now follows the Source-X formula (CCharNPCAct move-tick):
    it scales with DEX and the creature's MoveRate instead of a flat rate.
    Running (combat/chase) is ~250ms at high DEX up to ~1.6s at low DEX; walking
    (idle wander) ~1s to ~2.6s; clamped to [100ms, 5s]; pets run a little faster
    (DEX floored to 75). The previous flat 400ms made ordinary mid-DEX creatures
    chase noticeably faster than Source-X. Also fixes the MoveRate sense (higher
    MoveRate now means faster, as in Source-X, not slower).

[2026-05-31] - Cap NPC pathfinding node budget — the real crowd-stall fix (Wave 33)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE:
  - Profiling pinned the crowded-combat tick stall to a single cause: A*
    pathfinding. The Pathfinder's node cap (20000, sized for player
    half-continent .walk) meant an NPC chasing a target it cannot reach through
    a press of bodies explored the full 20000 nodes — ~366ms PER call.
  - FindPath now takes an optional maxNodes; NPC combat-chase passes a far
    smaller budget (2000) — ample to route around local obstacles toward a
    target in sight, while bounding a blocked search to ~20ms. Player .walk
    keeps the full budget.
  - Measured on the pathological 50k-monster cluster around 8 fighting players:
    tick dropped from ~8.8s to ~0.13s typical (max ~0.5s) — the headline
    fix that the earlier budget/scan/throttle waves had been bounding around.
    525 tests pass.

[2026-05-31] - Throttle NPC A* recompute in churning crowds (Wave 32)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE:
  - A* path recompute is now throttled per NPC (at most once per ~750ms). In a
    churning crowd the cached next step is invalidated almost every tick (a
    neighbour moves onto it), which previously forced a fresh A* search every
    tick. Between allowed recomputes the NPC follows its cached path or faces
    the target and holds. A dedicated throttle timestamp survives path-cache
    drops (and is swept for gone NPCs) so the limit actually binds.
  - Helps real crowded combat (e.g. a champion spawn where mobs jostle); the
    pathological 50k-clustered stress remains dominated by other per-NPC
    combat-brain cost that needs profiling to isolate further.

[2026-05-31] - NPC target-scan bounding in same-faction crowds (Wave 31)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE:
  - FindBestTarget now caps the number of attackable candidates it evaluates
    (not just hostile ones). Wave 30's cap only counted positive-motivation
    targets, so a monster surrounded by its own kind still evaluated every
    neighbour before finding the few real enemies — O(local density) per NPC.
    It now considers its nearest handful; a target farther back in a crowd is a
    closer NPC's problem, so combat still engages.
  - GetAttackMotivation does the cheap hostility test before the FindRegion
    lookup, so non-hostile candidates (the bulk of a crowd) skip the region
    query.
  - Note: the residual cost of thousands of monsters densely clustered around
    players is pathfinding/movement in the crowd, which is inherent to that
    (artificial) density and unaffected here; normal play is unaffected.

[2026-05-31] - NPC AI tick-cost bounding under crowded combat (Wave 30)
----------------------------------------

PERFORMANCE:
  - Per-tick NPC budget: a mass sector activation (a player entering a densely
    populated area) could make thousands of NPCs due in one tick and run their
    AI serially, stalling the tick for several seconds. The tick now processes
    at most a bounded number of NPCs and defers the overflow to the next tick.
  - Bounded target acquisition: FindBestTarget previously did a line-of-sight
    raycast (against the real static map — the dominant cost) for every nearby
    mobile, making acquisition O(crowd) per NPC. It now ranks candidates by
    motivation without LOS, caps how many are evaluated, and verifies LOS lazily
    only on the top few — a few raycasts per NPC regardless of crowd size.
  - Net: a pathological stress (50,000 monsters clustered around 8 fighting
    players) dropped from ~8.8s ticks to ~2.2s; normal and realistic loads are
    unaffected. (525 tests pass.)

[2026-05-31] - Headless 'stress' console command (Wave 29)
----------------------------------------

ADMIN / DIAGNOSTICS:
  - Added a `stress [items] [npcs]` console command mirroring the in-game
    .STRESS GM speech command, so the load-test population can be generated
    from a headless server (CI / smoke). Routes to StressTestEngine.QueueGenerate.
  - Smoke-verified on the real script/map data: generating 8,000 NPCs took ~1s
    and the tick loop stayed healthy (avg ~0.6ms, 8,006 chars + 6 players) with
    zero errors. (Note: stress NPCs are neutral load dummies, so combat bots —
    which only engage hostile monsters — do not fight them.)

[2026-05-31] - Headless 'bot' console command (Wave 28)
----------------------------------------

ADMIN / DIAGNOSTICS:
  - Added a `bot <count> [walk|combat|idle|smart]` console command so the bot
    stress/smoke framework can be driven from a headless server (stdin / CI),
    not only via the in-game .BOT GM speech command. Routes to the same spawn
    path. Verified end-to-end: bots auto-create accounts, create characters,
    enter the world, and walk — with the movement validator correctly rejecting
    water/impassable steps and fast-walk against the real map data.

[2026-05-31] - .NET 10 migration, ServerGC, deterministic test suite (Wave 27)
----------------------------------------

RUNTIME / BUILD:
  - All SphereNet projects retargeted net9.0 -> net10.0 (LTS). Full solution
    builds clean; 525 tests pass under net10.
  - ServerGarbageCollection + ConcurrentGarbageCollection enabled on the Host
    entry point (the game Server already had them).

TESTS (flaky CI fix, no tests removed):
  - Root-caused the intermittent CI failures to process-wide mutable static
    hooks left set across tests (ObjBase/Item.ResolveWorld,
    Character.ResolveAccountForChar which drives PrivLevel, VendorEngine.World).
    Under xUnit's non-deterministic order a later test resolved against a stale
    hook (e.g. a player inheriting another test's GM account).
  - Added a BeforeAfterTest attribute that resets those hooks before/after every
    test, plus assembly-wide serialization. The suite is now green across
    repeated runs regardless of order.

[2026-05-31] - D-prefix fix extended to function calls (Wave 26)
----------------------------------------

SCRIPT ENGINE:
  - The D-prefix fix (Wave 24) now also covers D-prefixed FUNCTION calls: a
    [FUNCTION] whose name starts with 'd' (e.g. DamTypesOfString) was losing its
    leading 'd' and never resolving. The D-handler fallback now resolves the
    full token via the function resolver as well as the variable resolver.

TESTS:
  - ExpressionParser regression extended with a D-prefixed function call.

[2026-05-31] - No-space <Rnnn> random expression form (Wave 25)
----------------------------------------

SCRIPT ENGINE:
  - <Rnnn> (no space, e.g. <R999>) is now accepted as the random 0..nnn-1 form,
    matching the spaced <R nnn>. 'R' followed by a digit is random; 'R' followed
    by a letter (REF, REGION, ...) is left alone. Previously the no-space form
    was unresolved and read 0, so IF !(<R999>) was always true (the rare branch
    fired every time).

TESTS:
  - ExpressionParser regression test for the no-space <R5> form (spaced <R 5>
    still works).

[2026-05-31] - Bare <dispid>/<dex> expression resolution fix (Wave 24)
----------------------------------------

SCRIPT ENGINE:
  - The "D force-decimal" prefix was wrongly swallowing bare self-properties
    that start with 'd' (DISPID, DEX, DIR, ...): it stripped the leading 'd'
    and resolved the remainder (<dispid> -> <ispid> -> 0). It now tries the
    'd'-stripped remainder first (preserving the legitimate <DHITS>/<DLOCAL.HEX>
    decimal form) and, only if that is unresolved, resolves the full token as a
    property.
  - Added an Item <DISPID>/<ID> read property (reflects the DISPID override,
    defname-or-hex form like BASEID). There was no read before, so
    IF (<dispid> == i_xxx) weapon-type bonus dispatch and furniture open/close
    (DISPID toggle) did not work.

TESTS:
  - ExpressionParser regression test that <dispid>/<DEX> are not mangled while
    the <DHITS> decimal form is preserved (524 passing).

[2026-05-31] - Script intrinsics RESOURCETYPE / RESOURCEINDEX (Wave 23)
----------------------------------------

SCRIPT:
  - <RESOURCETYPE defname> and <RESOURCEINDEX defname> resolve a defname to its
    resource type code and index. The type uses the Source-X RES_* numbering
    (CharDef=6, ItemDef=14, Spawn=37, ...) so that
    <RESOURCETYPE <entry>> == <def.res_chardef> compares correctly. The worldgen
    spawner's NPC/item discrimination and staff restype menus rely on this.
    Resolved via ResolveDefName; an unknown defname returns 0 (RES_UNKNOWN).

[2026-05-31] - Region periodic triggers @RegPeriodic / @CliPeriodic (Wave 22)
----------------------------------------

REGION TRIGGERS:
  - @CliPeriodic fires periodically for every online player on their current
    region (SRC = the player). @RegPeriodic fires once per tick for each region
    holding at least one player (SRC = a representative player), mirroring
    Source-X CSector's iRegionPeriodic environ tick; uninhabited regions never
    tick. Region ambient sound/music scripts (ON=@RegPeriodic SRC.SOUND,
    ON=@CliPeriodic SRC.MUSIC) now run. Reuses the existing FireRegionEvents
    mechanism (same path as Enter/Leave/Step).

[2026-05-31] - NPC speech broadcast (SAY/SAYU/EMOTE) (Wave 21)
----------------------------------------

NPC SPEECH:
  - SAY / SAYU / SAYUC / EMOTE now BROADCAST as overhead speech to nearby
    clients instead of a private system message to the source (SAY = ASCII
    0x1C, SAYU/SAYUC = Unicode 0xAE, EMOTE = emote type). An optional
    @color,font,mode prefix is parsed for the hue. NPC dialog/bark lines were
    previously invisible because they only went to the source as a system
    message.

[2026-05-31] - NPC AI morale/kiting and vendor restock unification (Wave 20)
----------------------------------------

NPC AI:
  - Morale/fear (Source-X NPC_GetAttackContinueMotivation): the decision to
    flee is now based on RELATIVE strength instead of a fixed "HP < half"
    threshold — STR difference + relative HP% difference. A strong, healthy
    NPC presses a weak target even below half HP; a weak/hurt NPC flees an
    overwhelming one. Applied as a penalty only.
  - Ranged kiting (Source-X NPC_FightArchery): when a target closes inside a
    ranged NPC's minimum range, the NPC backs off (~50%) to reopen the gap
    instead of standing locked in melee unable to fire.
  - NpcAIFlags bit values aligned to the NPC_AI_* defines (0x20 gap kept), so
    a raw script NPC.AI integer maps to the correct bits in future.

VENDOR:
  - GM VENDORINV restock now writes to the virtual stock container (LAYER 26)
    that the buy gump reads from, not the regular backpack — so GM-defined
    stock both displays and stays excluded from the world save.
  - Restocked items stamp PRICE from the itemdef VALUE; the two restock paths
    (template SELL= and GM VENDORINV) now share the same virtual stock model.

TESTS:
  - Unit test for the morale penalty (weak flees / strong presses); vendor
    trade tests moved to a serial collection to avoid a shared-static race
    (523 passing).

[2026-05-29] - Vendor virtual stock and lazy NPC loot materialisation (Wave 19)
----------------------------------------

VENDOR STOCK (VIRTUAL):
  - The vendor stock container (LAYER 26/27) and its items are no longer
    written to the world save; they are rebuilt from the SELL template
    (VENDOR_SELL_LIST tag) when a player opens the vendor. This removes
    thousands of transient stock records from saves with many vendors.
  - Buying decrements the stock amount; a depleted entry is removed, and the
    container is repopulated from the template on the next open once empty.
  - Buy now validates the stock serial against the vendor's own stock
    container, preventing a crafted packet from "buying" an arbitrary world
    item by serial.
  - Stock price is stamped from the itemdef VALUE; an item with no PRICE tag
    now uses the same fallback price as the display instead of 0 (the server
    side previously rejected such items and broke the purchase).

NPC LOOT (LAZY):
  - NPC plain loot (non-wearable, non-ITEMNEWBIE chardef ITEM= entries) is no
    longer materialised onto the living NPC at spawn; it is rolled straight
    into the corpse at death (Source-X CTRIG_CreateLoot parity). Living NPCs
    carry no transient loot items in the world save.
  - Wearable gear (weapons/armour) is still equipped at spawn (combat /
    appearance) and reaches the corpse via the normal unequip path.

TESTS:
  - Regression tests for vendor virtual stock: decrement, depletion removal,
    non-stock serial rejection, over-stock amount rejection, price fallback
    (522 passing).

[2026-05-29] - NPC AI: Source-X parity fixes and smarter behaviors (Wave 18)
----------------------------------------

NPC AI - CORRECTNESS / PARITY:
  - Flee logic: a fearful NPC (negative motivation) now routes to ActFlee
    instead of silently dropping its target.
  - Multicore ApplyDecision is sorted by NpcUid before applying, removing the
    non-deterministic completion-order apply and matching single-thread behavior.
  - _losFailCounts leak: separate purge pass for NPCs that never built a path
    cache entry.
  - Multicore reschedule now checks IsDead (symmetry with single-thread), so a
    dead NPC is not re-queued into the timer wheel.
  - Self-kill (reactive-armor reflect): killer==victim is attributed as null
    (no Kill trigger on self).
  - Beneficial-spell targeting fix: ChooseBestSpell now returns the cast target,
    so heal/cure go to the right recipient. Previously every spell was cast on
    the enemy, so an NPC "self-heal" actually healed its enemy.

NPC AI - SMARTER BEHAVIORS:
  - Spell combo chain: Paralyze -> Explosion -> EnergyBolt -> Poison while the
    target is locked down (COMBO_STEP/COMBO_TARGET state).
  - Ally support: caster NPCs heal/cure a wounded nearby ally, not just self.
  - Hidden-target pursuit: when a target hides, the NPC moves to its last known
    spot and tries Reveal instead of giving up immediately.
  - ReacquireDelay: target-less NPCs throttle the full-range scan (reset on being
    attacked, so retaliation is never delayed).
  - Pet mode revert: after an attack target dies, the pet returns to its previous
    order (Guard/Follow) instead of trailing the master.
  - Threat targeting (Source-X NPC_AI_THREAT): NPCs prefer whoever has dealt
    them the most damage, driven by the attacker list (the previously-unused
    NpcAIFlags.Threat is now honored).
  - FightMode bias (FIGHTMODE tag): weakest / strongest / evil target preference.
  - Dynamic tick: badly-hurt NPCs act slightly slower.
  - Backoff: timid animals back off from the nearest threat to a safe distance.
  - DetectHidden: guards / high-INT NPCs periodically reveal hidden players.
  - Stuck -> Teleport: a stuck caster blinks toward the target instead of giving
    up.
  - Forced target: bard Provocation (PROVOKED_TARGET) and scripted ConstantFocus
    (CONSTANT_FOCUS) override normal target selection.
  - Scout retreat: creatures with Hiding vanish mid-flee to break pursuit.
  - Looting (Source-X NPC_AI_LOOTING): looter NPCs scavenge items from nearby
    corpses into their pack (LOOTING tag or global flag).
  - IntFood (Source-X NPC_Act_Food): hungry NPCs eat food from their pack or
    graze (INTFOOD tag or global flag).
  - Spellbook spell loading (Source-X NPC_AddSpellsFromBook): a caster NPC with
    no scripted spell list derives one from a carried/equipped magery spellbook.
    (Wand-holding NPCs already cast reagent-free via the wand path.)
  - Hireling wage (Source-X NPC_OnHirePay): a hired NPC (HIRE_WAGE tag) is paid
    from the master's bank box on a timer and deserts when it can't be paid;
    hirelings are exempt from hunger-based loyalty loss.

DOCS:
  - docs/ restructured: added ARCHITECTURE, STAFF_COMMANDS, TRIGGERS and a docs
    index; ADMIN_SECURITY folded into DEPLOY; stale internal notes removed.
  - README rewritten in English with README-TR.md (Turkish).

[2026-05-29] - Gameplay bug fixes and Source-X parity completion (Wave 17)
----------------------------------------

SCRIPT ENGINE:
  - Numeric brace-range {n m}: random-range and weighted {a w b w} selection in
    the expression parser; CharDef stat lines now roll between min/max.
  - FOR argument forms: FOR x (1..x), FOR min max, FOR var max, FOR var min max,
    with inclusive ranges, count-down, and a named loop variable.
  - MAX/MIN intrinsics, the @ power operator, and the numeric 3-way
    QVAL(v1,v2,lt,eq,gt) form.
  - ItemDef TDATA1/TDATA3 defname capture with lazy resolution.

COMBAT:
  - Era-0 hit-chance now factors in target DEX and a ranged-weapon adjustment.
  - Era-aware damage bonus is percentage-based; tactics/anatomy excluded in era-0.
  - Damage min>max guard prevents a Random.Next exception.
  - Weapon parry with a shield or a one/two-handed weapon.
  - Reactive-armor reflected damage is now attributed to the attacker.

MAGIC:
  - Spell-success scale fix: SKILLREQ is checked at the correct scale (high-skill
    casters no longer fizzle constantly).
  - Implemented CreateFood and DispelField; MindBlast now uses the INT-difference
    formula; EvalInt scales spell damage.
  - Cast-recovery cooldown plus a light skill-based faster-casting effect.
  - Field spells form a multi-tile wall and deal periodic tick damage to
    stationary targets.
  - Incognito disguises the real name and restores it on expiry.
  - Recall/Gate are blocked while frozen/jailed and against blocked destination
    tiles.
  - Magic-resist circle aligned with GetCircle().

SKILLS:
  - GMs no longer accrue skill/stat gains.
  - Taming difficulty rescaled to 0-100, so high-HP creatures are tameable.
  - Stealing fails without a backpack, preventing item loss and a free criminal
    flag.
  - Crafting: exceptional durability bonus, resource hue transfer, and randomized
    failure resource loss.
  - RemoveTrap springs the trap on failure; bandages gain an anatomy bonus and
    produce bloody bandages; Veterinary routes through Healing.
  - SkillEngine uses Random.Shared for multicore thread safety.
  - Gathering no longer yields more than a depleted node holds.

TRIGGERS:
  - @ReceiveItem / @NPCAcceptItem fire when giving an item to an NPC.
  - @Criminal (cancellable), @SeeCrime (nearby NPCs), @SpellInterrupt, @Hunger.

ITEMS:
  - Item CONT= / Z= / LAYER= setters for script-driven container moves.
  - DUPE verb; character CURE / REVEAL / ATTACK verbs; character ARMOR/AR read.
  - Crops/foliage harvesting, seed planting, and empty-pitcher filling from water.
  - Light sources: in-container ignite block and charge consumption; switch
    graphic swap; food/drink single-unit consumption.

WORLD:
  - Timed jail auto-release (DateTime-based, reboot-safe) plus expired-jail
    cleanup on login.
  - Party: proper disband notification and honoured invite-accept result.
    Guild: leave privilege check, candidate->master promotion, multi-guild block.
  - Housing: transfer cap, footprint passability, and IDOC lockdown/secure item
    preservation.
  - Zero-value creatures grant no fame/gold, preventing farming.

CHARACTER:
  - Poison ticks broadcast health/damage packets and attribute the kill.
  - HP regen halts while poisoned; starvation drains stamina/hits; FOOD is
    clamped; resurrect leaves at least 1 HP; pet control-slot summation and
    loyalty warnings.
  - Movement shove now costs stamina exactly once (fixing the double-deduction /
    false-block bug).

TESTS:
  - Regression tests for brace-range, MAX/MIN/@, and QVAL (515 passing).
